# Spec Changes

Semantic changes to the specification. Git history captures diffs; this file captures intent.

## 2026-06-18

- **Pi SDK version bridge hardened to fail closed; its AC5 contract test realigned** ([REQ-AGENT-001](agents.md#req-agent-001-multiple-agent-types-supported) AC5 amended; stays Implemented). The prewarm Pi SDK version bridge (introduced 2026-06-17, which replaced the frozen `npm ci` with an npm `overrides` entry + lockfile-free `npm install` so the transitive `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent` always matches the `@latest` runtime agent) now **fails closed**: an empty resolved version aborts the build before reinstall, and a post-install assertion confirms the override actually pinned the transitive copy — so a future Pi packaging change can no longer silently ship a stale/unpinned prewarm SDK while the build stays green. AC5 gains a sentence describing the bridge + fail-closed behavior, and the `dockerfile-graphify.test.js` AC5 test (which still asserted the now-removed `npm ci` and was failing CI) is updated to assert the bridge contract (override write, lockfile drop, `npm install`, both fail-closed guards). The committed `overrides` value in `preseed/agents/pi/package.json` is documented as a build-time-overwritten placeholder. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-001 stays Implemented.

- **Usage disabled in enterprise; the username dropdown no longer opens (avatar stays visible)** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) Intent + AC2/AC6/AC8/AC9 amended; stays Implemented). Supersedes the read-only-Usage-in-enterprise decision from the 2026-06-17 "Enterprise dropdown: Logout hidden, read-only Usage enabled" entry below: the enterprise usage view always reports zero (the Timekeeper read path is not wired for enterprise), so the "Usage" dropdown entry is gated back to **SaaS-only** (`saasMode`, was `saasMode || enterpriseMode`) until that bug is fixed. With Usage gone, every enterprise username-dropdown entry is now gated away — Subscription + Usage are SaaS-only, Guided Setup + Logout are enterprise-hidden — leaving nothing to show. The **avatar/username trigger stays visible in every mode** (the user always sees their identity); in enterprise its `onClick` is made inert (`if (sessionStore.enterpriseMode) return`) in both `Header.tsx` and `Dashboard.tsx`, so clicking the avatar opens **nothing** instead of an empty dropdown. The per-item `!enterpriseMode` gates on Guided Setup + Logout were removed (the dropdown only opens outside enterprise, so those entries are unconditional inside it). The `/app/usage` page route is left unchanged — the underlying 0-reporting bug is deferred, not fixed here. Behavioral coverage flipped: `Header.test.tsx`, `Dashboard.test.tsx`, and `enterprise-surface-suppression.test.tsx` now assert that in enterprise the avatar trigger stays **present** but clicking it opens no dropdown (was: Usage present). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 stays Implemented.

- **Connect tier UI — live-review corrections (segmented toggle for Setup/Settings; panel dialog width fix)** ([REQ-AGENT-028](agents.md#req-agent-028-deploy-credential-token-creation-ux); stays Implemented). Owner reviewed the integration deploy on mobile + tablet and rejected two parts of the same-day redesign below. (1) **Settings "Push & Deploy" + Guided Setup:** the dropdown (`Select`) tier control inside `OAuthConnectCard` is replaced by a **segmented Minimal│Recommended│Advanced toggle** (`oauth-connect-tier-control`/`-option`/`-option--selected`, tokens-only, mirroring the production scope-tier control) with the description subtitle (`oauth-connect-tier-desc`) kept beneath it; the OAuth flow is unchanged and the connect button now reads "Connect {provider}". The connected state is also brought to production parity: a green "Connected" pill (`oauth-connect-badge`) and a "Disconnect" text-link (`oauth-connect-disconnect`) replace the green dot + bordered button. Orphaned `oauth-connect-tier-select` and `oauth-connect-btn--disconnect` rules are removed. (2) **Dashboard GitHub panel:** the `TierChooserDialog` popover no longer inherits the connect button's width (the button is a narrow centered inline-flex, which produced a cramped, badly-wrapped popover); it now uses a comfortable fixed width clamped to the viewport and anchored under the button, rendering like the "+ New Session" picker (desktop popover / mobile bottom sheet). Behavioral coverage updated: `OAuthConnectCard.test.tsx` + `DeployKeysSection.test.tsx` now assert the segmented control (all three tiers present, selected one marked, pick fires onSelect, selected tier in the connect URL, subtitle wired from the catalog). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-028 stays Implemented.

- **Connect tier UI redesigned; segmented `ScopeTierPicker` retired** ([REQ-AGENT-028](agents.md#req-agent-028-deploy-credential-token-creation-ux), [REQ-GITHUB-007](github.md#req-github-007-broaden-the-panel-gate-beyond-enterprise); both stay Implemented). Supersedes the `ScopeTierPicker` introduced in the 2026-06-17 follow-up below — that segmented control never shipped to `main`; it is replaced before merge by two surface-appropriate affordances confirmed with the user. (1) **Dashboard GitHub panel:** the connect card is restored to its original centered design (icon + one-line prompt + button) and the panel title stays "GitHub Browser"; the Connect button now opens a **responsive tier chooser dialog** — the same component pattern as "+ New Session" (a popover anchored to the button on desktop, a full-width bottom sheet on mobile, reusing `create-session-dialog.css`) — where each row shows a tier label + description and **picking a tier = connect** (navigates with `?tier=`). Enterprise connects directly with a bare URL and never mounts the dialog (GitHub App permissions are fixed). New `web-ui/src/components/connect/TierChooserDialog.tsx`; `web-ui/src/components/github/ConnectCard.tsx` rewritten to compose it. (2) **Settings "Push & Deploy" + Guided Setup:** the tier control inside the shared `OAuthConnectCard` is now a **dropdown (`Select`) with a description subtitle under the selected option** (`oauth-connect-tier`/`-select`/`-desc`), replacing the segmented picker (**later superseded — see the live-review correction entry above, which restores the segmented toggle and keeps the OAuth flow**); the connect-URL/account/connected states are unchanged. `web-ui/src/components/connect/ScopeTierPicker.tsx` and its test are deleted. Behavioral coverage: `TierChooserDialog.test.tsx` (new — renders all tiers + descriptions, marks selected, pick fires onPick, closes on backdrop/Escape), `OAuthConnectCard.test.tsx` (dropdown lists all tiers, change fires onSelect, selected tier in connect URL), `GitHubPanel.test.tsx` (non-enterprise: bare URL, click opens dialog, pick navigates with `?tier=`; enterprise: direct connect, no dialog), `DeployKeysSection.test.tsx` (both providers render the dropdown + subtitle). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-028, REQ-GITHUB-007 stay Implemented.

- **Landing hero-kicker stack fades fully to transparent** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) presentation; stays Implemented). The capability-word reel previously floored queued-word opacity at `0.14`, leaving a permanently-visible ghost column above the tagline that read as a cluster of words not lining up with the coral static text. `getHeroKickerOpacity` now takes the word count and ramps opacity **linearly from the active word (solid, on the baseline, never faded) up to fully transparent at the top of the stack** — the fade starts at the word above the active one, so the column dissolves into nothing instead of stacking. Animation (1.18em vertical travel, timing) is unchanged; only the opacity curve. Behavioral coverage: `hero-kicker.test.ts` (active solid, queued fades by stack position, top fully transparent); `components.test.ts` (queued word `0 < opacity < 1`) still holds. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **Cloudflare OAuth tier scopes aligned to the client's *granted* scopes** ([REQ-AGENT-064](agents.md#req-agent-064-connect-to-cloudflare-via-oauth); stays Implemented). Live testing showed Recommended/Advanced Cloudflare connects failing with `invalid_scope` while Minimal worked. Root cause was not invalid IDs — the four offending IDs (`access.write`, `ai.read`, `challenge-widgets.write`, `cf-agents.write`) are valid in the 361-entry `GET /client/v4/oauth/scopes` catalog but were **not among the scopes registered on the operator's OAuth client**, and a connect request can only narrow within the client's registered scopes. The server catalog (`src/lib/oauth-scopes.ts`) now requests only client-granted IDs: Recommended maps `access.write` → `zone-access.write` (Access: Apps & Policies; `dns.write` and `access-acct.write` were already present and unchanged); Advanced drops `ai.read` + `challenge-widgets.write` (ungranted; `ai.write` already covers Workers AI) and maps `cf-agents.write` → `agw.write` (Agents Gateway). README scope table updated to match. Structural scope tests (offline_access present, advanced ⊋ recommended ⊋ minimal, advanced ⊇ `ai.write`) still hold. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-064 stays Implemented.

## 2026-06-17

- **Engineering constitution hardwired into every preseed-managed agent** (new [REQ-AGENT-065](agents.md#req-agent-065-engineering-constitution-preseeded-to-all-agents), Implemented). Four engineering mandates — (1) no overengineering, (2) behavioral tests only (no theater / text-matching), (3) reusable/composable components and best practices, (4) SDD + TDD enforced — plus a **plan gate** (every plan must restate them as concrete success criteria) and a **done gate**, so they apply to all planning and coding without being restated each task. The preseed is the single source of truth: seeded as an advanced-gated Claude rule (`preseed/agents/claude/rules/engineering-constitution.md` + manifest, mode parity with `karpathy`/`frontend-components`), and injected into every Pi agent system prompt as an always-on `<codeflare_constitution>` block via the `before_agent_start` hook (`preseed/agents/pi/extensions/codeflare-pi.ts::ENGINEERING_CONSTITUTION`); the per-user `~/.claude` copy is a downstream seed artifact. Behavioral coverage (seeding + injection contract only, not the prose, per mandate #2): `host/__tests__/engineering-constitution.test.js`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-065 Implemented.

- **GitHub + Cloudflare "Connect" unified on OAuth across non-enterprise modes** (new [REQ-AGENT-064](agents.md#req-agent-064-connect-to-cloudflare-via-oauth), Implemented; [REQ-GITHUB-007](github.md#req-github-007-broaden-the-panel-gate-beyond-enterprise) Planned → Implemented; [REQ-GITHUB-001](github.md#req-github-001-github-token-capture-and-storage) AC4 + constraints, [REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC3/AC8, [REQ-GITHUB-008](github.md#req-github-008-enterprise-github-provider-configuration-via-setup) AC2/AC5, [REQ-AGENT-018](agents.md#req-agent-018-push--deploy-credential-management-ui), [REQ-AGENT-028](agents.md#req-agent-028-deploy-credential-token-creation-ux), [REQ-AUTH-015](authentication.md#req-auth-015-guided-onboarding-flow) AC1 amended; all stay Implemented). The three per-user credential surfaces (dashboard GitHub panel, Guided Setup onboarding, Settings "Push & Deploy" accordion) connected GitHub/Cloudflare inconsistently — the panel was OAuth but enterprise-only, the other two pasted a PAT / dashboard API token. They are now one flow. **Connect is decoupled from the panel gate:** `GET /api/github/connect` + callback + `POST /api/github/disconnect` (and the new Cloudflare equivalents) are `authMiddleware`-only, reachable by any authenticated user from Guided Setup + the accordion even when the panel is hidden; only `status`/`repos`/`clone` follow the panel. `githubFeatureEnabled` is now on in every mode and the **advanced-session entitlement** for the repo panel moved to the dashboard frontend (`Dashboard.tsx::githubPanelAvailable`, `sessionMode === 'advanced' || enterprise`, matching the Vault gate). A new **`CloudflareOAuthProvider`** mirrors the GitHub provider against `dash.cloudflare.com/oauth2/{auth,token,revoke}` (authorization_code + refresh_token, `offline_access`), persisting token/refresh/expiry across the existing `deploy-keys:<bucket>` Cloudflare fields (source `'oauth'`, encrypted, no new KV key); `getValidCloudflareToken` refreshes on expiry / fails closed, and the new composable `applyCloudflareOAuthToken` injects the refreshed token into the container env on session start (mirroring `applyEnterpriseBrowserToken`). All three surfaces compose one shared, reusable **`OAuthConnectCard`** (state matrix: disconnected → tier selector + connect navigation; connecting; connected → identity + account picker + disconnect); the per-user token-paste UI is removed (OAuth-only), and the orphaned dashboard-token-URL builders (`getGithubTokenUrl`/`getCloudflareTokenUrl` + their scope catalogs) were deleted, leaving `token-scopes.ts` as the tier-label catalogs only. The scope **tier** (minimal/recommended/advanced) now flows through the connect URL's `tier` query param into a **server-side** scope catalog (`src/lib/oauth-scopes.ts`): GitHub OAuth-App classic scopes + Cloudflare Wrangler-style scopes (always `offline_access`), supersets per tier (the GitHub App path's fixed permissions ignore it). GitHub provider Setup config was **un-gated enterprise → admin-any-mode** (`getProviderFromKv`, no longer enterprise-only; `getGithubProvider` resolves KV-first in every mode then env fallback), and the operator's **Cloudflare OAuth client id + secret** join the admin-gated Setup wizard (`CloudflareProviderChooser`; id plain, secret encrypted at rest, fail-closed without `ENCRYPTION_KEY`). **Enterprise is byte-identical:** `getCloudflareProvider` returns null in enterprise (every CF-OAuth route fails closed), the GitHub egress injection / hidden accordion / hidden Guided Setup / admin-global Browser Rendering token are untouched. Behavioral coverage: `cloudflare-token.test.ts`, `cloudflare-oauth.test.ts`, `oauth-scopes.test.ts`, `github.test.ts`, `Dashboard.test.tsx`, `OAuthConnectCard.test.tsx`, `DeployKeysSection.test.tsx`, `OnboardingPage.test.tsx`, `CloudflareProviderChooser.test.tsx`, `ConfigureStep.test.tsx`, `setup.test.ts`, `setup/handlers.test.ts`, `token-scopes.test.ts`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-064 + REQ-GITHUB-007 Implemented; REQ-GITHUB-001/002/008, REQ-AGENT-018/028, REQ-AUTH-015 stay Implemented.

- **Cloudflare OAuth scope IDs corrected; GitHub panel UI restored + non-enterprise scope-level picker** ([REQ-AGENT-028](agents.md#req-agent-028-deploy-credential-token-creation-ux), [REQ-GITHUB-007](github.md#req-github-007-broaden-the-panel-gate-beyond-enterprise); both stay Implemented). Follow-ups to the OAuth-connect unification above, from live integration testing. (1) **Real Cloudflare scope IDs.** The server scope catalog (`src/lib/oauth-scopes.ts`) used placeholder colon-form strings (`account:read`, `ai:write`) that Cloudflare's OAuth server rejects with `invalid_scope`; they are replaced with the real dot-form IDs from `GET /client/v4/oauth/scopes` (`account-settings.read`, `workers-scripts.write`, `ai.write`, …), mapping the capabilities of the old token-creation deeplink (workers/kv/r2/d1/routes/dns/access/pages/containers/queues/ai/browser-rendering/vectorize/turnstile/observability/ci/r2-catalog/cf-agents). The operator's OAuth client must register the advanced superset; the per-connect tier requests a subset within it. (2) **GitHub panel card restored** to its original centered design (the shared-card migration had regressed it); enterprise byte-identical. (3) **`ScopeTierPicker`** (new reusable component): a segmented Minimal/Recommended/Advanced selector with a subtitle describing the selected level (sourced from the tier catalog), replacing the bare `<Select>`, shown on all non-enterprise connect surfaces (panel + Guided Setup + Settings "Push & Deploy"); enterprise hides it (GitHub App fixed permissions ignore the tier) and sends a bare connect URL. `tierOptionList` removed (catalogs consumed directly). The root `README.md` gained a detailed operator procedure for registering both OAuth apps (incl. Cloudflare's Client-Secret-Post token auth + public-client `client_uri` DNS-TXT domain verification). Behavioral coverage: `ScopeTierPicker.test.tsx` (new), `OAuthConnectCard.test.tsx`, `GitHubPanel.test.tsx` (enterprise vs non-enterprise gate), `DeployKeysSection.test.tsx`, `oauth-scopes.test.ts`, `cloudflare-oauth.test.ts`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-028, REQ-GITHUB-007 stay Implemented.

- **Landing hero kicker drops "enterprise"** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) positioning copy; stays Implemented). The rotating-words kicker prefix changed from "The enterprise agentic" to "The agentic" (rendered "The agentic [word] engine"); `words[]` + `engine` suffix unchanged, so the data-driven word tests (which read `HERO.kicker.words`) are unaffected. Content-model only (`landing/src/content/site.ts`). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **Vault open is key-gated; button breathes accent→green instead of bouncing to `.auth`** ([REQ-VAULT-018](vault.md#req-vault-018-vault-browser-prewarm-readiness-gating) new AC8; stays Implemented). Users on JS/service-worker-restricted (e.g. corporate) browsers saw the Vault button go "ready" too fast, then land on SilverBullet's "Authentication not enabled" (`.auth`) page on open. Root cause: the readiness gate proved server reachability + prewarm sync but **not** that the encryption key was available at open time — the native service worker deliberately flushes its in-memory key ~5s after the prewarm client disconnects, so every real open relies on the worker's `__cfRecover` re-fetch, and the pre-open check only validated SW + IndexedDB. Fix: a new `checkVaultKeyRecoverable` helper verifies the key is recoverable from the auth-gated `/.vault-key` endpoint (the same one `__cfRecover` uses) before opening. If recoverable, the tab opens immediately. If not, the button enters a non-openable **`preparing`** state (breathing in the accent/theme colour) and a background poll re-checks local readiness + key recoverability; once both hold it becomes **`armed`** (breathing green) and the next click opens the tab **synchronously within the click gesture** so it is never pop-up-blocked on strict browsers. Open intent clears on open or when the session is no longer active. `@impl` `vault-local-readiness.ts::checkVaultKeyRecoverable`, `Layout.tsx::handleVaultOpen`, `VaultButton.tsx` (new `preparing`/`armed` states); behavioral coverage in `vault-local-readiness.test.ts`, `VaultButton.test.tsx` (new), and `Layout.test.tsx` (preparing→armed→open). **Status:** REQ-VAULT-018 stays Implemented.

- **Enterprise dropdown: Logout hidden, read-only Usage enabled** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC2 amended + new AC9; stays Implemented). Two enterprise UX fixes in the username dropdown (Header + Dashboard menus). **Logout (AC9):** hidden in enterprise — under Cloudflare Access SSO the in-app logout is ineffective (it clears the Access session but the IDP silently re-authenticates on the next request), so sign-out is governed by the IDP / device. **Usage (AC2):** the read-only "Usage" entry is now shown in enterprise (was SaaS-only), so enterprise users can see their monthly compute consumption; "Subscription" stays SaaS-only. No new machinery — the Timekeeper already records compute in every mode (only quota *enforcement* is bypassed in enterprise) and `/app/usage` was already route-unguarded; the change is the dropdown gate (`saasMode || enterpriseMode` for Usage; `!enterpriseMode` for Logout) plus hiding the Usage page's in-page "Subscription" billing button outside SaaS. Behavioral coverage in `Header.test.tsx` and `Dashboard.test.tsx`. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 stays Implemented.

- **Dashboard panel labels disambiguated: STORAGE USAGE / GITHUB BROWSER / STORAGE BROWSER** ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC8 amended; stays Implemented). In enterprise mode two "STORAGE" labels appeared together — the left-column stat-card section divider (above the R2 bucket usage card) and the right-column storage-panel header (the earlier FILES→STORAGE rename). The labels are now distinct: the left stat divider reads "Storage Usage" (it shows files/folders/bytes used), the right file-browser header reads "Storage Browser", and the GitHub panel header reads "GitHub Browser" for symmetry. CSS uppercases all three (STORAGE USAGE / STORAGE BROWSER / GITHUB BROWSER). Text-only change in `Dashboard.tsx` (`dashboard-section-divider`, `files-panel-title`) and `GitHubPanel.tsx` (`github-panel-title`); testids unchanged, so the structural tests (which assert by testid, not copy) are unaffected. **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-002 stays Implemented.

- **Fix: "Guided Setup" was still shown in enterprise mode via the Dashboard menu** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC8 amended; stays Implemented). AC8 hides the username-dropdown "Guided Setup" (per-user onboarding) entry in enterprise, but the implementation gated only `Header.tsx`. The dashboard view renders its **own** user dropdown in `Dashboard.tsx`, whose "Guided Setup" item was never gated — so enterprise users, who land on the dashboard, still saw it. The Dashboard item is now wrapped in `<Show when={!sessionStore.enterpriseMode}>`, mirroring `Header.tsx` (and matching AC2, which already covers both the Header and Dashboard menus). AC8's `@impl` now lists `Dashboard.tsx` and AC8's wording says "both the Header menu and the Dashboard menu"; behavioral coverage added in `Dashboard.test.tsx` (item present when not enterprise, absent when enterprise). The store flag is the live `sessionStore.enterpriseMode` set in `App.tsx` from the authenticated user. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 stays Implemented.

- **`high` container tier disk raised 8 GB -> 12 GB** ([REQ-OPS-007](operations.md#req-ops-007-container-specs-configurable-per-environment) AC1 amended; stays Implemented). The `high` tier was 2 vCPU / 6 GiB / **8 GB** disk, leaving headroom under Cloudflare's "max 2 GB disk per 1 GiB memory" rule (6 GiB allows up to 12 GB). It now uses the full **12 GB** ephemeral disk at the same 2 vCPU / 6 GiB — no RAM/CPU change, no cost change beyond disk. This relieves the per-session working-disk constraint (large monorepos + node_modules + build output) for enterprise, which runs `high`. Cloudflare's predefined `standard-2` (1 vCPU / 6 GiB / 12 GB) sits at the same 2-GB-per-GiB ratio, confirming 12 GB at 6 GiB is valid (not just under the cap). Patched in both deploy workflows (`deploy.yml`, `deploy-dockerhub.yml`), `wrangler.toml` comment, and the configuration/README docs. Takes effect on the next enterprise redeploy. **Status:** REQ-OPS-007 stays Implemented.

- **GitHub repo-list row cap is now per-breakpoint (7 desktop / 5 tablet)** ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC6 amended; stays Implemented). The repo-list scroll viewport previously capped at ~10 rows on every viewport above the mobile breakpoint. It now caps at 7 rows on desktop (`>=1024px`) and 5 rows on tablet (`600-1023px`) before scrolling; mobile (`<=599px`) is unchanged — it still grows to fill the available height (min 3 rows) and keeps the GitHub ↔ R2 flip. CSS-only (`github-panel.css`): the desktop base `max-height` dropped from `--repo-row-h` × 10 to × 7, and a `600-1023px` media band caps at × 5. The px caps remain CSS viewports, not data limits, so all fetched repos stay rendered and searchable (not unit-asserted in jsdom). **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-002 stays Implemented.

- **Hero capability-word ticker drops "infrastructure"** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving); stays Implemented). The vertical kicker word set removed "infrastructure"; final set: coding, operations, testing, review, orchestration, deployment, toolchain, security. Content-model only (`HERO.kicker.words`); the ticker is data-driven and the `ENGINE` suffix tracks the active word's measured width, so layout and the data-driven word tests are unaffected (the longest word is now "orchestration"). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **Landing + onboarding-email outcome copy broadened beyond code** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) positioning copy; stays Implemented). With the positioning now "engineering engine, not coding assistant," the hero definition and the Shift lead framed every outcome as "a pull request to merge" / "before it merges", which under-claims the non-code work the agents do (SSH into infrastructure, orchestrate, configure). The outcome language now reads "handed to your team to approve, whether that is a pull request to merge or a change to run" and "your team reviews the evidence before it executes"; the onboarding email's matching line was aligned the same way and brought onto the rebrand vocabulary (governed engineering agents / your own estate). The spec-driven-development machinery copy is deliberately left code-specific: `/sdd init` bootstrapping, the code knowledge graph, the diff/PR-boundary enforcement loop, and the Legacy reverse-engineering section genuinely operate on a repo's code, tests, and diffs, so genericizing them to "work / systems / change" would be less accurate, not more. The terminal demo and enforcement gate stay a concrete code/PR example. No requirement semantics changed. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **Hero capability-word ticker revised** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving); stays Implemented). The vertical kicker (`THE ENTERPRISE AGENTIC [WORD] ENGINE`) dropped "delivery" (a vague outcome word that overlapped "operations") and gained the broader-scope capabilities "orchestration", "deployment", and "security"; "toolchain" was kept. Final set: coding, operations, infrastructure, testing, review, orchestration, deployment, toolchain, security. Content-model only; the ticker is data-driven and the `ENGINE` suffix tracks the longest word (still "infrastructure"), so layout and the data-driven word tests are unaffected. REQ-LANDING-001 AC4's narrative quote of the hero definition was also synced to the new "approve, whether a pull request to merge or a change to run" wording. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **The R2 storage panel gets a "STORAGE" header in enterprise mode, mirroring the GitHub panel header** ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC8 amended; stays Implemented). When the GitHub panel is enabled (enterprise mode), the right column's storage face now carries a "STORAGE" panel header — an uppercase label with a gray bottom border identical to the GitHub panel's "GITHUB" header, and matching the existing modal StoragePanel's "Storage" wording — with the mobile flip-back control inside it. In non-enterprise / onboarding mode there is no GitHub panel to mirror, so the storage panel renders without the header (unchanged), which also keeps it the lone, fully-visible mobile face. Implemented in `Dashboard.tsx` with `.files-panel-header` / `.files-panel-title` in `dashboard.css` (named `files-panel-*` to avoid colliding with the modal's `.storage-panel-*`) reusing the same design tokens as the GitHub header. **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-002 stays Implemented.

## 2026-06-16

- **Positioning rebrand: "agentic coding engine" → "the enterprise agentic engine", plus a canonical agent vocabulary** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) and [REQ-LANDING-003](landing.md#req-landing-003-landing-social-share-and-search-metadata) positioning copy; both stay Implemented). Two passes. First, the tagline dropped "coding": the hero/positioning line is now "The enterprise agentic engine" and the standalone descriptor "agentic engine", propagated across the landing, PRODUCT copy, SEO/OG/Twitter metadata (`src/lib/seo.ts`), the PWA manifest, transactional email, the in-app marketing surfaces (Subscribe/Onboarding/Usage/Login), and documentation. Second, a scoped copy refinement on the **landing page, both `/login` surfaces, the root README, and the GitHub About** settled a canonical agent vocabulary: `engineering agents` (everyday) and `governed engineering agents` (hero/OG moments) replace "coding agents"/"autonomous agents"; "autonomous" is dropped; the capability clause is `build, test, review, and operate`; and positioning "your own cloud / cloud account / cloud boundary" becomes `your own estate` (broadens the footprint without naming a vendor, while factual Cloudflare references stay in the technical docs). The README story was rewritten to this voice with the OG card as its hero image. The social card (`web-ui/public/og.svg` → `og.png`) is reproducibly rasterized via a committed JetBrains Mono font pipeline (`web-ui/scripts/rasterize-og.mjs` + `web-ui/scripts/fonts/*.ttf`, `@resvg/resvg-js`). Copy was checked against the avoid-ai-writing/humanizer rulesets (no em dashes, no AI-vocabulary tells). The estate/engineering-agents refinement is intentionally scoped to landing + login + README + About for now; the other surfaces keep the tagline-pass wording. Historical changelog entries retain the original wording. No requirement semantics changed. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 and REQ-LANDING-003 stay Implemented.

- **Two Partial REQs promoted to Implemented by closing their automated-test gaps** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) Partial → Implemented; [REQ-AGENT-057](agents.md#req-agent-057-pi-review-status-command) Partial → Implemented). Both were built but verification-gapped. REQ-ENTERPRISE-005's CA-trust (AC2) and Copilot BYOK (AC3) entrypoint behaviours now have host tests (`host/__tests__/entrypoint-enterprise-ca-copilot.test.js`) asserting the `.bashrc` CA env prepend (`NODE_EXTRA_CA_CERTS` at `CF_CA_SRC`, idempotent, omitted when `ENTERPRISE_MODE` unset) and the Copilot BYOK block (`api.openai.com` base-url, placeholder credential, `COPILOT_MODEL` = default route, token-limit hints, stale route overwritten on re-run); the AC3 token-limit hint was reconciled to the implemented `920,000` (the spec read `1,050,000`). REQ-AGENT-057's `/review-status` rendering (AC1) and audit-log tail (AC3) were manually verified only; the renderer was extracted as a pure `renderReviewStatus` and `recentReviewEvents` exported (production path unchanged), with behavioral tests (`src/__tests__/lib/review-command.test.ts`) for the rendering contract, read-only/idempotency (AC2), and the JSONL tail. No production behaviour changed. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-005, REQ-AGENT-057 Implemented.

- **Admin access via Cloudflare Access groups** (new [REQ-ENTERPRISE-014](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-014-admin-access-via-cloudflare-access-groups), Implemented; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC8 added; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-010](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-010-access-gated-jit-user-provisioning) entry gate widened). Admin (= Setup / user-administration) access was email-only (KV `role:'admin'`). An enterprise admin can now also grant admin to members of named Cloudflare Access groups, configured in a new "Cloudflare Admin Access Groups (optional)" Setup chip field beside the user-access groups; the email-based "Admin Users" list stays. Groups persist comma-joined under `SETUP_KEYS.ENTERPRISE_ADMIN_ACCESS_GROUP` and round-trip via prefill. Elevation is a **live** per-request check confined to `requireAdmin` (a new `resolveAdminAccessGroup`, parallel to `resolveSessionAccessGroup`) — never the hot `authenticateRequest` path and short-circuited for users already `admin`, so every non-admin request and every non-admin route stays byte-identical and removing a user from the group revokes Setup access on the next request (fails closed on any get-identity error). The elevation lives only on the Hono context (no KV admin record written). The entry-entitlement gate now admits admin-group members too (membership tested against the union of user + admin groups) so an admin in no *user* group is not locked out, but admin groups never arm the gate by themselves. Admin groups are excluded from per-group routing by construction. All enterprise-gated; non-enterprise Setup shape + admin authorization byte-identical. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-014 Implemented.

- **Enterprise UI/UX refinement pass: GitHub panel, clone picker, per-group routing, header** ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC4 amended + AC6/AC7/AC8 added, [REQ-GITHUB-004](github.md#req-github-004-clone-a-repository-into-a-session) AC1 amended, [REQ-ENTERPRISE-013](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-013-per-group-dynamic-routing) AC5 amended, [REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC8 added; all stay Implemented). Dogfooding produced concrete corrections, landed with composable primitives + behavioral tests. GitHub panel: a refresh control (the storage panel's `mdiSync`) and an icon-only Disconnect (`mdiConnection`) — both a new shared `IconButton` — plus the owner login and each repo name as external `target="_blank"` links to GitHub; the repo list is now a hidden-scrollbar scroll container capped at ~10 rows on desktop and grown to fill (min 3) on mobile (CSS viewport, not truncation); on mobile a `mdiFlipVertical` control in the panel header swaps the GitHub ↔ R2 panels in place (animated, reduced-motion → instant), hidden on desktop where both still stack. Clone picker: the running-session row now matches the new-session agent rows (one shared `ClonePickerOptionRow` — same left edge, the session's own agent icon, a "Running in <agent>" subtitle). Per-group routing: route selection is now green/gray toggle **pills** (new `PillToggle`) instead of checkboxes; "Apply to all groups" shows only when more than one group exists; the global "Default Route" editor is hidden once any group is added (per-group owns routing; the stored global default stays the no-match fallback). Header: the username-dropdown "Guided Setup" (per-user onboarding) entry is hidden in enterprise mode. All UI is mode-agnostic or already enterprise-gated; non-enterprise surfaces unchanged. **Status:** all four REQs stay Implemented.

- **Fix: the empty GitHub panel covered the R2 file browser on mobile when GitHub is disabled** ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC8 amended; stays Implemented). The mobile GitHub ↔ R2 flip defaulted the right-column face to GitHub, but `GitHubPanel` renders nothing while GitHub is disabled (non-enterprise / onboarding / status not yet loaded). The empty GitHub face therefore became the active mobile face and hid the R2 storage browser behind it — a blank panel below the storage summary, as seen dogfooding the integration deploy. The active face is now derived from `githubStore.enabled` (`Dashboard.tsx::effectiveFace`): when GitHub is disabled the storage panel is the sole mobile right-column face and the "Show GitHub" back-control is not rendered; when enabled the flip behaves exactly as before. Desktop (both panels stacked via `display:contents`) was never affected. **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-002 stays Implemented.

- **Enterprise GitHub provider configured in the Setup wizard (KV-backed), not deploy secrets** (new [REQ-GITHUB-008](github.md#req-github-008-enterprise-github-provider-configuration-via-setup), Implemented; [REQ-GITHUB-001](github.md#req-github-001-github-token-capture-and-storage) AC4 amended). GitHub integration was dark on enterprise-integration because `getGithubProvider` read `GITHUB_APP_*`/`OAUTH_*` env vars that `deploy.yml` never injects and enterprise admins cannot set. Admins now choose the provider (GitHub App vs OAuth App) and enter its client id + secret in the Setup wizard (`GitHubProviderChooser`); the type + ids are stored plain and each secret encrypted at rest in KV under dedicated `SETUP_KEYS.GITHUB_*` keys (separate pairs per provider so switching preserves the other's). `getGithubProvider` is now async and resolves the active provider from KV (decrypting the secret) before the unchanged env-var fallback. A blank secret on save keeps the stored one (no clobber); a secret submitted with no `ENCRYPTION_KEY` is rejected (400) rather than written in plaintext, and a stored secret that cannot be decrypted fails closed. `GET /api/setup/status` echoes the type, both client ids, and a per-provider `…ClientSecretSet` boolean, never the secret. All reads/writes are inside the existing `isEnterpriseMode` gate; non-enterprise Setup shape and the env-var path are byte-identical (guard test). Mirrors the admin-global Browser Rendering token ([REQ-BROWSER-007](browser-run.md#req-browser-007-enterprise-admin-configured-browser-rendering-token)). SaaS OAuth-app-with-extra-scopes stays out of scope. **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-008 Implemented.

- **Per-group dynamic routing added to enterprise Setup** (new [REQ-ENTERPRISE-013](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-013-per-group-dynamic-routing), Implemented; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway) AC4, [REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC1, [REQ-ENTERPRISE-012](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-012-setup-configured-dynamic-route-catalog-and-access-group-list) AC2/AC4 amended; REQ-ENTERPRISE-004 and REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 stay Implemented, REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 remains Planned — its AC1 amendment is tested but AC2/AC3/AC5/AC6 still lack automated tests). Routing was global (one `DYNAMIC_ROUTES` catalog + one `DEFAULT_ROUTE` for everyone). Admins can now scope, per Cloudflare Access group, which routes are active + a default route + reasoning, with an "Apply to all groups" shortcut. Config persists as a JSON map under `SETUP_KEYS.GROUP_ROUTING`; `configure` rejects (400) a group whose default isn't in its routes, whose routes aren't a subset of the global catalog, or whose key isn't a configured group, and deletes an empty map. A session resolves the first of its matched groups (in configured order) with a non-empty entry, falling back to the global catalog; **with no per-group config, behavior is exactly as before** (user-confirmed). Both routing sinks — the LLM interceptor's per-request enforcement and the container env fan — read one shared group-aware `resolveRouteCatalog` core so they cannot drift, preserving the default-drift rule. The Setup wizard renders one per-group card per group (only when ≥1 group and ≥1 route), and `addAccessGroup` seeds a new group's routing from the global default + full catalog so cards are never empty. All enterprise-gated; non-enterprise Setup shape + resolution byte-identical. As part of the frontend work the `ConfigureStep` chip-list/select pattern (duplicated 3-4×) was extracted into composable `ChipListField`/`Select`/`Checkbox` primitives with structural oracle tests (behavior-preserving DOM). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-013 Implemented.

- **GitHub integration completed end-to-end and flipped to Implemented; panel scoped to enterprise mode, the broaden deferred** ([REQ-GITHUB-001..006](github.md) Planned → **Implemented**; new [REQ-GITHUB-007](github.md#req-github-007-broaden-the-panel-gate-beyond-enterprise) Planned). The remaining phases of the GitHub domain landed with behavioral tests and are now verified: the panel + repository listing ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing): `GET /api/github/status` + `/repos`, server-side proxy that never returns the token, mobile-first sibling to the storage panel), enterprise egress injection ([REQ-GITHUB-003](github.md#req-github-003-enterprise-egress-injected-github-credentials): a `GitHubInterceptor` WorkerEntrypoint stamps the per-user token at the `github.com`/`api.github.com` boundary — git Basic vs API Bearer + `X-GitHub-Api-Version` — fails closed with no upstream request when no token, and is scoped solely by the per-session `props.bucket` binding so a session can only ever inject its own user's token), the clone flow ([REQ-GITHUB-004](github.md#req-github-004-clone-a-repository-into-a-session): a session picker of running sessions then "new session", clone into `$USER_WORKSPACE/<repo-verbatim>` refusing a pre-existing folder, new-session clone-before-agent via `entrypoint.sh` + the host `git-clone` resolver, running-session clone via the `CONTAINER_AUTH_TOKEN`-authed internal RPC), and disconnect/offboarding ([REQ-GITHUB-005](github.md#req-github-005-disconnect-and-offboarding-revocation): `POST /api/github/disconnect` revokes at GitHub for App/OAuth sources and clears the deploy-keys fields, with offboarding revoking on the same `user-cleanup` path). Non-enterprise transport ([REQ-GITHUB-006](github.md#req-github-006-other-mode-container-transport)) is unchanged (deploy-keys→`GH_TOKEN`) and verified by the container-env placeholder-vs-real assertions. **Scope decision:** the panel gate stays **enterprise-only** for now ([REQ-GITHUB-002](github.md#req-github-002-github-panel-and-repository-listing) AC3 reworded from the three-way enterprise/advanced-SaaS/per-user-toggle gating to enterprise-only, anchored to `githubFeatureEnabled`); broadening the gate to the SaaS `advanced` tier and a per-user toggle (default off) is split out as the new **Planned** [REQ-GITHUB-007](github.md#req-github-007-broaden-the-panel-gate-beyond-enterprise) (P2) rather than left as unmet acceptance criteria. Spec-hygiene fix folded in: REQ-GITHUB-004 carried a duplicated acceptance criterion "4." (one anchored, one not) — the unanchored duplicate was removed so the list numbers 1–5 cleanly. **Status:** REQ-GITHUB-001..006 Implemented; REQ-GITHUB-007 Planned.

- **Enterprise Browser Rendering token moved to the Setup wizard; per-user deploy-keys accordion hidden in enterprise; browser-run surface gated on the token** (new [REQ-BROWSER-007](browser-run.md#req-browser-007-enterprise-admin-configured-browser-rendering-token), Implemented; [REQ-GITHUB-001](github.md#req-github-001-github-token-capture-and-storage) Constraints note). Now that Connect GitHub provides GitHub credentials in enterprise, the per-user "Push & Deploy" settings accordion is redundant and is hidden in enterprise mode (`SettingsPanel`). Because browser-run still needs a Cloudflare Browser Rendering token, an admin now configures one (+ account id) once in the Setup wizard (`ConfigureStep`); it is stored encrypted at rest (kv-crypto) and masked on prefill (the wizard learns only whether a token is set, never its value). At session start in enterprise the admin-global token/account override the now-unused per-user Cloudflare deploy-key fields and reach the container as `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID` via the existing env path (`applyEnterpriseBrowserToken` in `lifecycle.ts`) — the narrowly-scoped `Browser Rendering - Edit` token is allowed in the container (it grants only Browser Rendering, which the agent can already do through its own browser tools), so unlike the GitHub token it is **not** egress-injected. When no token is configured (any mode, or a non-advanced session) the whole browser-run surface is withheld: the MCP servers and Pi extension already self-gate, and the `browser-run` / `browser-e2e` SKILL.md files are now stripped from both agents so the agent is never left with a skill for a tool it lacks (`entrypoint.sh` else-branch). The same "no provider → no skill" gap was closed for **consult-llm**: its non-enterprise "no usable provider" path now removes the consult-llm skill too, matching its existing enterprise branch ([REQ-AGENT-031](agents.md#req-agent-031-consult-llm-key-isolation-subscription-backend-and-multi-agent-parity)). **Status:** REQ-BROWSER-007 Implemented.

- **Vault readiness is now current-device proof, and cache cleanup no longer runs from dashboard mount** ([REQ-VAULT-018](vault.md#req-vault-018-vault-browser-prewarm-readiness-gating) AC1-AC7, [REQ-VAULT-015](vault.md#req-vault-015-vault-idb-lifecycle-and-listing-filters) AC3-AC4, [REQ-VAULT-017](vault.md#req-vault-017-silverbullet-native-service-worker) AC1/AC3; stay Implemented). Browser prewarm ready messages now require local `sb_data_*`, local `sb_files_*`, and active per-session service-worker proof for the current browser/device; the ready click rechecks that proof and restarts prewarm if the browser cache was cleared. The Vault button stays visible but guarded, with click/tap feedback while preparing or retrying, and the app requests best-effort persistent browser storage without treating denial as fatal. Orphan IDB sweeping moved from Dashboard mount to successful authoritative session-list loads so an initial empty store cannot delete the active browser cache. The vendored native SilverBullet service worker is refreshed to the Dockerfile-pinned 2.9.0 bytes, and `Index.md` is restored to a clean dashboard source with Notes/References ahead of the recent widgets and no implementation marker comments.

- **Landing hero top line becomes a capability-word engine ticker** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 + enhancement constraint amended; stays Implemented). The hero kicker is now modeled as `THE ENTERPRISE AGENTIC [WORD] ENGINE`: static words stay coral, the active capability word is command white, queued words remain visible above as a ghosted vertical stack, and client enhancement measures the active word so `ENGINE` tracks its changing width instead of reserving the longest word. The chosen capability set is coding, operations, infrastructure, testing, review, delivery, and toolchain, reflecting Codeflare's broader internal-endpoint / orchestration scope rather than coding alone. Server markup contains the full stack plus an in-flow baseline sizer for no-JS and reduced-motion fallback. `HeroKicker.astro` and `hero-kicker.ts` keep the behavior centralized; structural and rotation-model tests cover the data-driven word stack and top-wrap rotation.

- **Pi PR-boundary reconciliation parses shell wrappers structurally** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1; stays Implemented). The post-command reconcile backstop now tokenizes shell commands and unwraps `env`, `command`, `nice`, and `timeout` wrappers before looking for `git` or `gh`, so `env -u NAME VAR=value gh ...` and timeout-wrapped commands force fresh PR-state reconciliation without relying on a wrapper-heavy regex.

- **Pi review summaries wait for a live session before posting** ([REQ-AGENT-062](agents.md#req-agent-062-pi-pr-boundary-review-result-delivery) AC6-AC7; stays Implemented). Review results remain pending until Pi can display them in the active session, reducing false `/review-results` fallbacks after off-turn review completion.

## 2026-06-15

- **GitHub integration domain added (panel + clone + enterprise egress-injected auth)** (new [REQ-GITHUB-001..006](github.md); all Planned). A new `GitHub` domain: a panel beside the R2 storage browser to Connect GitHub and browse/clone repositories, with the in-session agent acting with the user's own GitHub permissions. Token capture reuses the existing `DeployKeys.githubToken` entry (no new KV key) behind a two-provider seam — an internal **GitHub App** (user-to-server, refreshable ~8h tokens) for enterprise/EMU and the existing OAuth App for non-EMU SaaS. Enterprise reuses the AI-Gateway container egress-injection layer to inject the per-user token into `github.com`/`api.github.com` at the boundary, so the real token never enters the container (placeholder `GH_TOKEN` only); other modes keep the existing deploy-keys→`GH_TOKEN` path unchanged. See [AD81](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad81-reuse-the-container-egress-injection-layer-for-per-user-github-tokens). Phase 1 (token store + two providers, [REQ-GITHUB-001](github.md#req-github-001-github-token-capture-and-storage)) landed with behavioral tests (`src/__tests__/lib/github-token.test.ts`); the remaining REQs are in progress. **Status:** all REQ-GITHUB Planned.

- **Pi PR-boundary reconciliation now refreshes PR state after git/gh commands** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1; stays Implemented). Successful shell commands that invoke `git` or `gh` force a fresh PR-state reconcile, so wrapper or unclassified pushes cannot hide behind a stale cached PR head.

- **Pi PR-boundary reconciliation now reaches nested repos after reload** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1; stays Implemented). Missed review heads are recovered from GitHub PR state instead of silently skipping when the SDD repo is nested under the session workspace.

- **Vault opens only after full browser prewarm; dashboard focuses Notes and References** ([REQ-VAULT-012](vault.md#req-vault-012-vault-button-render-and-dashboard-landing) AC3-AC5, [REQ-VAULT-018](vault.md#req-vault-018-vault-browser-prewarm-readiness-gating) AC1-AC6, [REQ-VAULT-001](vault.md#req-vault-001-persistent-vault-directory-survives-across-sessions) AC3, [REQ-VAULT-010](vault.md#req-vault-010-codeflare-authoritative-files-preseeded-into-the-vault-on-every-boot) AC2, [REQ-SEC-008](security.md#req-sec-008-security-headers-on-every-response) AC2/AC4; stay Implemented). The Vault button now has two readiness gates: the existing server probe must first prove the proxied SilverBullet server is reachable, then a hidden same-origin iframe runs the real bootstrap + SilverBullet client until IndexedDB/service-worker sync and the full object index are ready. The button remains disabled through prewarming, timeout, and error states; failed or timed-out prewarm attempts retry in the background and the button enables only after a validated same-origin `codeflare-vault-prewarm` ready message for the current prewarm attempt. Vault proxy security headers now allow same-origin framing (`X-Frame-Options: SAMEORIGIN` plus `frame-ancestors 'self'`) while still blocking cross-site framing and avoiding SilverBullet-breaking `default-src 'none'`. The preseeded `Index.md` now leads with Notes and References, and `init_user_vault()` always creates `References/` alongside `Notes/`. Priority/lazy indexing for visible non-priority folders is documented as out of scope because stock SilverBullet queues every visible `/.fs` entry into the browser object index.

- **App share-card and PWA metadata refocused** ([REQ-SETUP-010](setup.md#req-setup-010-social-share-preview-metadata-on-the-public-landing-page) AC4 reworded, AC5 removed; stays Implemented). The web-ui app shell's Open Graph / Twitter share card and the PWA install description now carry the "enterprise agentic coding engine" positioning instead of the retired "ephemeral IDE" tagline, and the canonical share copy is no longer pinned to a fixed sentence.

- **Landing + login surface componentized; hero reel now loops** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 amended + `@impl`/`@test` extended; [REQ-AUTH-020](authentication.md#req-auth-020-onboarding-mode-landing-integrated-login-and-access-request-flow) `@impl`/`@test` extended; both stay Implemented). The monolithic `index.astro` (~770 lines of hand-duplicated markup tested by copy-string matching) and `login.astro` were refactored into a composable component system so a change propagates from one place: a `Terminal` chrome + the two animation stylers extracted as `Transcript` (last-line cursor / typed / roll-middle) and `GateSteps` (rolling rows) — both stylers' timing, classes, and data-attributes preserved exactly — plus layout primitives (`Section`, `SectionHead`, `Header` unifying the landing + login navs, `FeatureGrid`/`FeatureCard`, `MicroCta`, `TrustStrip`), the specialized bodies (`LedgerTable`, `ReviewBoard`, `OrchTree`), and the login UI (`LoginCard`, `SsoAccordion`, `RequestedPanel`); pages are now pure composition. The entrance/flicker logic moved into `scripts/reveal.ts` (testable; above-the-fold elements are never animated from opacity 0). The Container-render copy-string theater was replaced with behavioral component contracts (`components.test.ts`), a structural oracle for the composed page (`index-page.test.ts` / `login-page.test.ts` rewritten), and a `reveal.ts` DOM test. **Behavior change:** the hero capability reel now loops continuously and shuffles per load (`data-ft-loop` + `data-ft-shuffle`) instead of playing once and stopping (`data-ft-once`), so the page is never static (#39); the engine still supports play-once mode but no live terminal uses it. The three cursor-mode proof terminals (legacy `/sdd init`, context web-fetch, context e2e) now type their last transcript line in when the terminal scrolls into view, via a new `landing/src/scripts/type-on-view.ts`: `Transcript` wraps that line in a `[data-typeline]` span, and the script clears and types it on first IntersectionObserver hit, then rests on the full line with its blinking caret (intersection-gated, armed ahead of the viewport so it never flashes the full text first; reduced-motion / no-JS leave the full server-rendered line untouched). Covered by `type-on-view.script.test.ts`; the cadence (`TYPE_MS`) matches `feature-terminals.ts`. This upgrades the earlier static blinking caret (#32). Folded-in visual fixes (proof terminals type their last line in on view #32, dogfood full width #35, footer symmetric © #33, contact aside fine print #34, hero spine + substation spacing #36/#37, `/login` flicker + transition #38, nav breathing room #40) became component props / central CSS rather than per-instance patches. No new requirements; the public contract (routes, AC1-AC3, AC5) is unchanged.

- **Scroll-in entrance flash eliminated for texts and terminals** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) presentation; `reveal.ts` + `proof.ts` arm timing; `reveal.script.test.ts` strengthened; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: scrolling the page (most visible on small mobile / tablet viewports) flashed each text block and terminal briefly before it settled. Two compounding causes, both the same shape: an element painted at its resolved, visible state and then snapped hidden by an animation that armed only after it was already on screen. (1) `reveal.ts` armed the `.reveal` fade-up via `inView` at `-60px` (60px after the element had entered the viewport), so it painted full-opacity and then snapped to 0 and faded back up. Below-the-fold `.reveal` targets (and `[data-stagger]` children) are now hidden up front at setup, while still off-screen, so they fade up cleanly from a hidden start on entry; no-JS and reduced-motion visitors still see everything, and above-the-fold elements still play no entrance (the existing open-page flicker fix is unchanged). (2) `proof.ts` added `.is-live` at `rootMargin: -80px 0 -80px 0` (80px into view), arming the terminals' `backwards`-filled row keyframes (`term-type` / `proof-row`) after the rows were already visible, which snapped them hidden then replayed; and because the terminal wrapper revealed at -60px but its rows armed at -80px, the rows flashed inside the now-visible terminal. The arm now fires ~100px ahead of the viewport (`rootMargin: 0 0 100px 0`) so the hidden start happens off-screen and the rows animate in as the artifact arrives. Presentation-only; no copy or structural change. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **Cursor-terminal caret hugs the typed line, matching the hero** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) presentation; `Transcript.astro`; `components.test.ts` strengthened; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: the blinking caret on the cursor-mode proof terminals sat one space after the last character once the line finished typing, while the hero caret hugs its text. Cause: in the shared `Transcript` component the cursor branch emitted the line text and the caret on separate source lines, so Astro inserted a whitespace text node between them, and `.t-line` is `white-space: pre` / `pre-wrap`, which renders that as a visible space. The hero's typed-reel line has its `.ft-typed` span and caret adjacent on one line, so it never had the gap. The cursor branch is now written the same way (text and caret adjacent, no inter-element whitespace); a `components.test.ts` assertion pins the caret's `previousSibling` to the `[data-typeline]` span so the gap cannot silently return. Presentation-only; one component, one behaviour. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.

- **PR-boundary review autofix is no longer expired before it can run** ([REQ-AGENT-062](agents.md#req-agent-062-pi-pr-boundary-review-result-delivery) AC3/AC6; stays Implemented). The delivery age backstop now applies only to the display summary (which has the `/review-results` fallback), so an autofix announcement that has not yet caught a live session stays pending and fires on the next live tick instead of being marked `failed` at zero attempts — and the summary backstop was widened from 10 to 30 minutes so a long (15-20 min) review or work run no longer false-escalates a summary that would have delivered on the next idle tick.

## 2026-06-14

- **Onboarding user approval works (tier-mutation gate widened to OIDC modes) and the admin panel collapses to a Simple Approve / Block control** ([REQ-AUTH-018](authentication.md#req-auth-018-user-management-admin-panel) Intent + AC2/AC4 + Constraints amended, `@impl`/`@test` extended; stays Implemented). Owner-reported follow-on to the onboarding work: an admin could not approve a pending user in onboarding mode. Root cause: `PATCH /api/users/:email` (the approval mechanism) was gated on `isSaasModeActive`, so the only app-owned mode that could mutate tiers was SaaS; an onboarding admin clicking approve got a 400 "Subscription tiers are only available in SaaS mode". Fix (backend): the gate becomes `isSessionOidcMode(c.env)` (SaaS active OR onboarding active) with the message recast to "Access tiers are only configurable in SaaS or onboarding mode" (`src/routes/users.ts`); enterprise mode is already 403'd by the user-management router middleware (REQ-ENTERPRISE-009) and default/CF-Access mode has no tier-gated access, so PATCH still 400s in those. Fix (UI, `web-ui/src/components/admin/UserManagement.tsx`): the panel now reads `saasMode` from `GET /auth/status` and adapts — SaaS keeps the full per-user tier + session-mode `<select>`s and the "Approve All (Standard)" bulk action; onboarding (no paid tiers) renders a per-user **Approve** (grants full access: `unlimited` tier + `advanced` session mode) for pending/blocked users, a **Block** (`blocked` tier) for active users, and an "Approve All" bulk action to that same full-access tier. New `.user-mgmt-btn--block` style (muted outline, reddening on hover, distinct from the red delete ×). Tests: `users.test.ts` gains an onboarding-mode PATCH-approval success case and a default-mode PATCH-rejection case (asserting the new "SaaS or onboarding" message); the existing SaaS PATCH cases are unchanged (SaaS still clears the gate). **Status:** REQ-AUTH-018 stays Implemented.
- **SaaS billing surfaces no longer leak into onboarding mode: gated on `saasMode`, not `!enterpriseMode`** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) Intent/AC1-4/AC6/Constraints amended; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: the integration (onboarding) deployment showed the full SaaS billing UI (Standard/Pro plans, subscription management, usage, the subscription submenu) even though `SAAS_MODE` is inactive. Root cause: the billing surfaces were gated on `!enterpriseMode`, correct for the original two-mode world (enterprise vs not) and spec-compliant under the old REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 AC6 ("flag unset → byte-identical"). When onboarding was added as a third mode it is `!enterprise` AND `!saas`, so it fell into the "show billing" bucket and inherited every SaaS surface (the deploy log + GitHub-only login confirmed the worker was genuinely in onboarding mode, not stale/SaaS — config was correct). Fix: the billing surfaces now gate on the positive `saasMode` signal (render only in SaaS; hidden in enterprise, onboarding, and default alike): the Header + Dashboard "Subscription"/"Usage" dropdown items, the SettingsPanel "Manage Subscriptions" admin block, the Layout monthly-quota / "Upgrade" banners, and the SessionSection Standard/Pro session-mode selector (now a `saasMode` accessor prop). The `SubscribeGuard` (App.tsx) redirects away from `/app/subscribe` whenever `saasMode` is not active, backed by a new `saasMode` field on `GET /api/auth/status` (`src/routes/auth.ts`, + `AuthStatusResponseSchema` + `AuthStatus` type). The admin/routing surfaces stay enterprise-gated: "Manage Users" still renders in onboarding (`!enterpriseMode`), as do first-login routing (AC5) and the setup "Regular Users" section (AC7). Components read `sessionStore.saasMode` (already mirrored from `/api/user`). REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 reframed from enterprise-only suppression to a two-axis model (billing → `saasMode`, admin/routing → `enterpriseMode`); AC6 rewritten as three-mode parity. Tests: `enterprise-surface-suppression.test.tsx` + `enterprise-layout-suppression.test.tsx` + `Header.test.tsx` rewritten for saas/onboarding/enterprise (each billing surface: shown in SaaS, hidden in onboarding, hidden in enterprise); `SettingsPanel.test.tsx` mock gains `saasMode`; `auth.test.ts` asserts `/auth/status` exposes `saasMode` reflecting `SAAS_MODE`. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-008 stays Implemented.

- **Landing copy humanized to strip AI-writing tells, triaged field by field; OG card text retuned** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) + [REQ-LANDING-003](landing.md#req-landing-003-landing-social-share-and-search-metadata) impl copy in `landing/src/content/site.ts` and `web-ui/public/og.svg`/`og.png`; `index-page.test.ts` sub-tag literal `context/drives` → `context/automation`; both stay Implemented). The change is structural, not just lexical: the section titles no longer share one rhetorical mould, the stacked "not X, it's Y" antithesis drops from ~15 occurrences to two kept deliberately (the hero headline and the PIPELINE title), the compulsive lead tricolons are broken, and the puffery ("generational leap", "citizens of your pipeline", "watch the work not the weeds", "the open web distilled", the over-used "governed") is gone; documentation joins the spec-and-tests proof story at the owner's direction. Content keeps its capitalised pillar word so the nav-pillar echo and tests hold; CSS lowercases it. (2) **Sub-section markers** — `.substation` sub-blocks now carry a NESTED tag one path level deeper (`~/security/operations`, `~/cost/tenancy`, `~/platform/runs-everywhere`, `~/context/drives`); the path depth marks them as sub-sections, so hierarchy reads from the path, not size alone. (3) **Under-terminal text hierarchy** (the owner's recurring complaint that size-alone read as an accidental near-miss) — new `--fs-subhead` token (`clamp(1.4rem, 1.2rem + 1.1vw, 1.7rem)`) fills the empty h2->h3 gap so the substation head sits a decisive >=1.4x step above the 1rem card terms; the card term is `--fs-body` semibold white over its `--fs-body` regular grey explanation, a term/definition pair distinguished by weight + colour at one size. - **Under-terminal card-label case normalized to one heading case (#15 correction)** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) structural Constraint updated; stays Implemented). - **Onboarding-mode logout fix** ([REQ-AUTH-009](authentication.md#req-auth-009-logout-dispatches-by-mode) AC2 widened; `@test` extended; stays Implemented). On the integration (onboarding) deployment, SPA logout redirected to the Cloudflare Access system logout endpoint, which rejected the `returnTo` with "Invalid redirect URL". Root cause: `/logout` only routed to the GitHub logout path under `isSaasModeActive`, so onboarding — which also issues the app's own `codeflare_session` — fell through to CF Access. Fixed by dispatching on `isSessionOidcMode(env)` so SaaS and onboarding both take `/auth/github/logout`, while default/enterprise CF Access deployments are unchanged; added SaaS + onboarding logout-dispatch regression tests (the onboarding case keeps `auth_domain` set to prove the OIDC branch wins).

(1) The folder indicator dot in the storage browser was hardcoded blue (`FOLDER_ICON.color` via an inline style); it now drops the inline colour and is painted in CSS by `var(--color-accent)`, so it tracks the Appearance accent like the rest of the themed UI (file dots keep their per-type colours). (2) Pi failed to start on integration ("Extension does not export a valid factory function: browser-run-helpers.ts"): the helper module, split out of `browser-run.ts` in the symmetric-Browser-Run change, was the only `*-helpers.ts` in the Pi extensions dir missing the no-op default factory the extension scanner requires; added it (matching the other helper modules) and regenerated `agent-seed.generated.ts`.

Because a bright accent fails white text, a new `--color-accent-contrast` token (set by `applyAccentColor` via a YIQ-brightness helper `accentContrast`: warm near-black `#160a06` on bright accents, near-white on dark ones) is the foreground of every accent-filled control (the dashboard New Session button and the shared primary Button, plus header / settings / storage / file-preview / onboarding / setup accent buttons); it resolves to white for the old blue, so it is a no-op for dark accents and only flips bright ones. The New Session button's "Upgrading..." label loses its ellipsis ("Upgrading"), in both the dashboard button and the session dropdown. (SaaS-only `subscribe` / `subscription-management` styling is deeply blue-hardcoded and outside the onboarding/enterprise deploy scope, left for a separate SaaS recolor.) (5) **Dashboard tips are mode-aware and refreshed** — tips were shown unconditionally, so onboarding / enterprise deployments saw SaaS-only advice ("Switch to Pro mode", "Check your compute usage") for features they do not have; a `saasOnly` flag now hides those outside SaaS (`sessionStore.saasMode`, newly mirrored from `/api/user` like `enterpriseMode`), and new engine-capability tips were added (delegate to subagents, parallel PR reviewers, agent-driven browser e2e, knowledge-graph recall, autonomous steering from any device, any-agent-one-engine). - **Onboarding sign-in now actually reaches `/app`: the app-owned `codeflare_session` is trusted in onboarding mode, plus a `/login` cleanup and corrected enterprise-SSO copy** ([REQ-AUTH-020](authentication.md#req-auth-020-onboarding-mode-landing-integrated-login-and-access-request-flow) gains AC5 + a new constraint; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: in onboarding mode, GitHub sign-in bounced back to the marketing landing and `/app` showed "Authentication required." Root cause (not the OAuth App config, which is correct for the integration domain): the access layer only trusted the `codeflare_session` cookie when `SAAS_MODE=active`, but onboarding runs `SAAS_MODE=inactive`. The GitHub callback *issued* the session, but `getUserFromRequest` (`validateSaasOidc`) and the index.ts session-refresh both gated on SaaS only, so an approved user's session was never trusted/refreshed and `/app` rejected it, bouncing to the landing. Fix: a shared `isSessionOidcMode(env)` = `SAAS_MODE` active OR `ONBOARDING_LANDING_PAGE` active (`src/lib/onboarding.ts`); `validateSaasOidc` is renamed `validateSessionOidc` and gated on it; the index.ts refresh and the `requireActiveUser` tier gate (`src/middleware/auth.ts`) likewise extend to onboarding (so `/app` stays approved-users-only — a pending onboarding visitor with a session is still 403'd). Enterprise/default deployments are untouched (they use Cloudflare Access). Tests: `auth-gaps.test.ts` (REQ-AUTH-020 — session trusted in onboarding, not trusted when neither mode active, AuthError on missing secret, no fallthrough on invalid session), `auth-saas.test.ts` (tier gate in onboarding), `onboarding.test.ts` (`isSessionOidcMode`). Also on `/login`: the two redundant `codeflare` wordmarks were removed (the "Sign in to Codeflare" title carries the brand) and the "Back to codeflare.ch" link moved to the top-left as a back affordance; the enterprise-SSO panel copy was corrected to the real model (SSO is wired in when Codeflare Enterprise is deployed into the customer's own cloud account, where their IdP and access policies are configured, which is why it starts with a conversation). A new constraint documents that each deployment domain needs its own GitHub OAuth App (one callback URL per classic OAuth App). Surfaced by the owner testing onboarding sign-in on the integration domain. **Status:** REQ-AUTH-020 stays Implemented.

- **Deploy workflow provisions GitHub OAuth in onboarding mode, not just SaaS** ([REQ-AUTH-020](authentication.md#req-auth-020-onboarding-mode-landing-integrated-login-and-access-request-flow) deploy gap closed; no AC change, stays Implemented). The onboarding `/login` GitHub sign-in needs `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` (injected as a deploy-time `--var`) plus the `OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` / `OAUTH_JWT_SECRET` worker secrets, but `deploy.yml` gated all three on `vars.SAAS_MODE == 'active'`. Since deploy `--var`s are replaced per deploy (unlike secrets, which persist), an onboarding deploy with SaaS off would drop the `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` var and skip the GitHub OIDC secrets step, silently breaking "Continue with GitHub". The OAuth `--var` injection and the GitHub OIDC secrets step now fire for `vars.SAAS_MODE == 'active' || vars.ONBOARDING_LANDING_PAGE == 'active'` (Resend already covered onboarding; Stripe stays SaaS-only). Surfaced by the owner asking what integration needs to deploy in onboarding mode. **Status:** REQ-AUTH-020 stays Implemented.

a new legacy-rescue station (`id="legacy"`, station 02) sits between method and security showing `/sdd init --import` building a spec baseline and `/sdd clean` realigning drift; a quiet vertical station spine numbers the instrument stations only (01 method, 02 legacy, 03 security, 04 context, 05 pipeline, 06 cost) via a `.station-marker` per section and a desktop hairline thread, while operations and the calmer tail stay un-numbered; the method `.method-clauses` coral counter is removed (numbering now lives in the spine) and the two pillars render as plain label-and-prose; `--section-y` is tightened so the page is a touch denser; the footer is stripped to one centered "Built with Codeflare · © 2026 Gray Matter GmbH" line (logo, nav links, and the GitHub mark removed, so the GitHub link now lives only in the dogfood CTA); and the dogfood transcript is amplified with verified-real anchors (`sdd status REQ-LANDING-001` / Status: Implemented / `@impl` index.astro + FeatureTerminals.astro + site.ts / `@test` index-page.test.ts / shipped via PR #533) closing on a "real anchors · enforced at every PR boundary" foot. The legacy `/sdd init` (Import/Resume) and `/sdd clean` motions are real; the counts (38/12) and PR #533 are illustrative like the page's other example figures. Copy stays free of en/em dashes (CI tripwire; `·` / `→` / `/` / `;` separators). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Onboarding-mode login moves onto the landing design system, with a post-OAuth access-request flow (new [REQ-AUTH-020](authentication.md#req-auth-020-onboarding-mode-landing-integrated-login-and-access-request-flow))** ([REQ-AUTH-020](authentication.md#req-auth-020-onboarding-mode-landing-integrated-login-and-access-request-flow) added, Status Implemented; cross-references [REQ-AUTH-002](authentication.md#req-auth-002-saas-mode-uses-direct-github-oauth), [REQ-AUTH-013](authentication.md#req-auth-013-custom-branded-login-page), [REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving)). In onboarding mode (`ONBOARDING_LANDING_PAGE` active, `SAAS_MODE` not active) the Worker now rewrites `GET /login` to the landing-built Astro login page (`/landing/login/`), sharing the marketing landing's tokens, fonts, and mouse-splash; SaaS mode keeps the SPA `/login` unchanged. The page (`landing/src/pages/login.astro` + `landing/src/scripts/login.ts`, `LOGIN`/`TRUSTED`/`ORCHESTRATION` exports in `site.ts`) offers GitHub sign-in (→ `/auth/github/login`) plus four enterprise SSO buttons (Microsoft Entra ID, Okta, Ping Identity, Google Workspace) rendered as expand-to-CTA controls that deep-link to the contact form with `topic=enterprise-deployment` (preselected via the new `pickDeepLinkTopic` in `contact-controller.ts` / `ContactForm.astro`) — they never start an OIDC flow. After GitHub OAuth (`src/routes/github-auth.ts`), an active-tier user still lands at `/app/`; a non-approved user in onboarding mode now gets a pending access record with `requestedAt` (idempotent across repeat sign-ins), admin + user confirmation emails via Resend (new `sendAccessRequestConfirmation` reusing `sendEmail` in `src/lib/email.ts`), and a redirect to `/login?status=requested` that the page reshapes into a "request submitted" confirmation. The branch never runs in SaaS mode (which keeps `/app/subscribe`) or enterprise mode. No Turnstile re-challenge on this path because the GitHub OAuth already authenticated the human. Tests: `landing/src/__tests__/login-page.test.ts` (Container render: github href, four SSO CTAs, requested state, robots noindex), `login.script.test.ts` (status/error param state), `contact-controller.test.ts` (`pickDeepLinkTopic`), `src/__tests__/routes/onboarding-login.test.ts` (`/login` rewrite, mode-aware callback redirect + emails). **Status:** REQ-AUTH-020 Implemented.
