## 2026-06-12

- **`/review-status` now resolves a nested-clone session correctly instead of warning "not inside a git repository"** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC5 extended to the `/review-status` command; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: in a session whose Pi cwd is a non-repo parent workspace (`/home/user/workspace`) with the real clone nested (`/home/user/workspace/ai-news-digest`) and work done via `cd repo && ...`, `/review-status` warned "not inside a git repository" even though review state existed in the nested `.git`. Root cause: `review-command.ts` carried a duplicated, narrower resolver — `activeRepo(startDir) = findGitRoot(startDir)` over the session cwd only — that even commented "See resolveReviewRepo() rationale" while NOT using it, so it ignored the in-memory active-repo / review-repo fallbacks the rest of the review system (the reaper, on-turn finalizers, statusline footer) already share. Fix: `/review-status` resolves through the shared `resolveReviewRepo()` (session cwd → in-session review repo → in-memory active repo → process cwd; in-memory recall only, never the flap-prone sentinel for routing), and — because it is strictly read-only — falls back for DISPLAY to the same guarded on-disk sentinel the footer uses (`activeRepoSentinelForDisplay`, guarded to a git repo inside a session root); the duplicated `activeRepo(startDir)` is removed. Test: `review-state.test.ts` adds the exact nested-workspace case (non-repo session cwd + nested in-memory active repo resolves the clone, beating processCwd); the guarded display-sentinel fallback is already covered by its existing reject-outside-root / reject-non-git / empty-content cases. Agent seed regenerated; mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. Pi-only; the local agent re-seeds from R2 on next session start. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented.
- **Landing two-mode polish pass: the security section folds into one unified boundary gate, a dogfood proof section + GitHub link are added, the hero goes two-column on desktop with a shorter transcript, the feature terminals get live per-tile typing, and the card-grid sections become hairline editorial columns** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 security-section wording updated and the dogfood/GitHub elements added to the enumeration; `@impl` anchor added for `feature-terminals.ts`; `@test` annotation extended to the unified boundary gate and the dogfood section; nav links and section anchor ids otherwise unchanged; no serving/contact/metadata change, REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). Owner feedback on the deployed page: the hero terminal looked too packed on mobile and half-empty on desktop (fixed with a two-column desktop hero and short varied transcript lines); the three feature-terminal cursors blinked in sync and "looked fake" (now one idle terminal blinks while the rest type/hold/delete/loop on staggered starts via `feature-terminals.ts`); the security boundary's weak flow diagram plus a small-✕ denied list "broke the styling and flow" (recast as one `.gate.boundary` of pass/deny rows reusing the enforcement-gate grammar — three approved paths, three the architecture makes impossible — with the egress-inspection strip kept as its sibling, and no provider or CDN vendor named in the copy); the remaining boxed card grids and per-section eyebrows were dropped for hairline `.feature-col` editorial columns; and a GitHub link (nav + footer) plus a "Codeflare built this page" dogfood section now point at the public repo (`GITHUB_URL`). `FeatureTerminals.astro` and `feature-terminals.ts` are load-bearing `@impl` files. Copy stays free of en/em dashes (CI tripwire; `·` / `→` / `/` separators). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing shift section reworked: the big-number stat band and the assistant-vs-engine checkmark comparison are both replaced by a grid of four animated "feature terminals", and the hero terminal gains an animated agent statusline foot** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 enumeration updated — "stat band" → feature-terminal grid; nav links and section anchor ids unchanged; no serving/contact/metadata change, REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). Owner feedback on the deployed page: the checkmark value-list and the stat band were disliked both content-wise and visually, the under-hero terminal snippets "look great" and should recur for real codeflare features, and the terminals should feel "alive but calm". Changes: (1) **Feature terminals** — a new `FeatureTerminals.astro` renders `FEATURE_TERMINALS` (four compact terminals: gateway egress denial + reroute, ephemeral session with zero endpoint footprint, the PR #207 six-lane review, and SDD spec enforcement), each a real command-and-output in the page's existing terminal idiom with a one-line caption foot, replacing both the `STATS` band and the `SHIFT.assistant`/`engine` checkmark comparison (both exports removed from `site.ts`, along with the now-unused `Stat`/`ComparisonColumn` types). (2) **Alive-but-calm animation** — the hero terminal gains a coding-agent statusline foot (`agentfoot.ts`: context %, model, reasoning level, with an occasional compaction beat) and a one-shot line-typing reveal on scroll-in; the blinking caret is retained. All motion is reduced-motion-safe with the server-rendered resolved state as the static fallback (no JS required), and the transcript lines are kept short so the hero terminal wraps on mobile instead of forcing horizontal scroll (the reported mobile-overflow fix). Copy stays free of en/em dashes (CI tripwire; `·` / `→` / `/` used as separators). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **PR-boundary review summaries now deliver reliably into the session instead of stranding on disk: the summary is sent with a plain idle-gated `pi.sendMessage` (Pi's synchronous append path) rather than a `triggerTurn`/`followUp` send** ([REQ-AGENT-062](agents.md#req-agent-062-pi-pr-boundary-review-result-delivery) AC6 added; stays Implemented). Owner-reported: running `/review-run` started the lanes fine, but no merged summary ever surfaced in the main session. Root cause (verified against the Pi SDK source `@earendil-works/pi-coding-agent`): `sendAnnouncement` emitted the summary with `{ triggerTurn: true, deliverAs: "followUp" }`, which routes the custom message through agent-core's `_runAgentPrompt` (not streaming) or `agent.followUp` / `agent.steer` (streaming) queues — paths whose custom-message persistence depends on a live agent loop emitting `message_end`, so off-turn or post-reload the send silently no-op'd: the delivery nonce never landed in the transcript and the announcement looped `attempted→failed` without ever displaying. The entire nonce-verify / retry / `/review-results`-fallback machinery (AC2–AC4) existed to paper over exactly this unreliable send. Fix: deliver the summary the same way `/review-results` already does — a plain `pi.sendMessage` with NO options, which takes Pi's `appendCustomMessageEntry` path that synchronously persists the nonce-bearing content AND displays it in one step — gated on `pi.isIdle()` so it is never steered into a streaming turn (the [REQ-AGENT-062](agents.md#req-agent-062-pi-pr-boundary-review-result-delivery) AC6 idle-gated delivery rule); when the agent is mid-turn the summary stays pending for the next idle tick (`agent_end` / `turn_end` / `session_start`). The nonce-verify/retry phase is now a backstop, not the primary delivery path. The autofix request still uses `triggerTurn`/`followUp` (it intentionally triggers a fix/commit/push turn — unchanged). Because the idle gate defers WITHOUT burning a retry attempt while the agent streams, `announcementReconcileDecision` gained an age backstop (keyed on `createdAt`, max 10 min) so a summary that never observes an idle tick still escalates to the `/review-results` fallback past that age instead of retrying invisibly forever, and a throwing `isIdle()` is counted as a failed attempt rather than a silent defer — both preserving REQ-AGENT-062's never-acked-and-lost guarantee (review-surfaced HIGH/MEDIUM, fixed in the same change; the age backstop is unit-tested as a pure decision). Runtime `pi.sendMessage`/`isIdle` wiring is a documented coverage-gap (REQ-AGENT-062 AC6) verified by inspection + jiti load-check + live smoke test; agent seed regenerated. Pi-only; the local agent re-seeds from R2 on next session start. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-062 stays Implemented.
- **PR-boundary review now survives a lost `tool_execution_start`: the push command is captured on `tool_call` too, so a reload/turn-boundary event drop no longer makes the boundary fast-path skip a push silently** ([REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC7; stays Implemented). Owner-reported on `ai-news-digest` PR #287 (`develop` -> `main`): a normal `git push origin develop` advancing head `ceeb1c5` created **no** review window — no `boundary_detected`, no pending state, no near-miss audit — even though the PR was open, non-draft, and targeting `main`, and CI ran fine. Root cause (verified against live source, not just the report): in `review-enforcement.ts` the tool-event handlers are asymmetric — `tool_call` (line ~1851) calls `onAgentStart` but does NOT seed the `toolStartArgs` cache; only `tool_execution_start` seeds it. The push command is recovered at `tool_result` via `withStartArgs`, so if `tool_execution_start` is lost (reload, turn boundary, different id shape), the command is gone by `tool_result`: `commandText()` returns empty, `isPrBoundaryTrigger("")` is false, and `onToolEnd` hits a silent `return` before it can even write a near-miss audit row. Fix (surgical set, owner-chosen): (1) **command survival** — `toolStartArgs` is now seeded on BOTH `tool_call` and `tool_execution_start` via a shared `rememberToolStartArgs`, mirroring the existing unconditional seeding (kept unconditional, not narrowed to command-bearing only, because the `agent`-tool result handler also relies on `withStartArgs` recovering its start-args); (2) **cache-fresh boundary read** — the boundary PR state read switched from the cached `prStateResultFor` to `prStateFreshResult` (invalidate-then-read), so a push landing within the 60s prCache TTL is decided against the new head, P4 failure distinction preserved; (3) **never-silent** — a successful `bash` result that still arrives with no recoverable command text now records a deduped `boundary_tool_end_ignored: missing_command_text_after_success` near-miss instead of returning invisibly. Deferred (heavier defense-in-depth, not needed for this miss because the recovered command carries its `cd <repo>` so nested-repo resolution works on the fast path): the durable `.git/` boundary-intent file and the guarded on-disk active-repo fallback for the reconcile backstop. This is a separate, pre-existing bug from the same-day incremental-scope fix below — different code path (trigger/detection vs. review scope), so the scope change did not cause it. Runtime tool-event wiring is a documented coverage-gap (REQ-AGENT-036 AC7) verified by inspection + jiti load-check + the manual missed-boundary smoke test; agent seed regenerated. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-036 stays Implemented.
- **PR-boundary re-reviews now actually honor incremental scope: the shared reviewer agent defs and enforce skills are scope-agnostic, and the Pi lane guard makes the incremental window binding** ([REQ-AGENT-040](agents.md#req-agent-040-pr-boundary-lane-classification-and-agent-dispatch) AC8 added; [REQ-AGENT-060](agents.md#req-agent-060-pi-durable-review-lane-tool-surface) AC8 added; both stay Implemented). Owner-reported on a reliable Pi integration run: the first review of a PR correctly covers the full diff (no prior ack), but every *subsequent* review re-reviewed the entire PR diff against `main` instead of only the new commits since the last acked clean head. Root cause was not the scheduler — `reviewPrompt`/`docUpdaterPrompt` already emit a correct incremental task prompt ("Scope is ONLY the incremental diff from `<base>` to `<head>`... Do NOT review the full PR diff"). The defeating factor was the **shared agent/skill definitions**, which affirmatively instructed the opposite: `code-reviewer.md` step 1 ("Gather the full diff -> `git diff origin/main...HEAD`"), the `spec-reviewer`/`doc-updater` Step 0d diff-classification blocks, and the `spec-enforce`/`doc-enforce` "Git diff syntax" / `diff` Inputs all hardcoded the full-PR diff as the producer — so the reviewer obeyed the def and re-scanned the whole PR. Fix follows the owner's principle that *the scope limitation must never live in the agent or its enforce skill* (those are seeded to Pi, Claude, and every other CLI): the defs/skills are now **scope-agnostic** — they review exactly the window the caller hands them (a `<base>..<head>` range, the "review ONLY the incremental diff" instruction, or `CODEFLARE_REVIEW_BASE`/`CODEFLARE_REVIEW_HEAD` in the environment), default to the full change set only when no window is given, and never widen a provided window back to the full PR diff. The full-PR `git diff origin/main...HEAD` blocks remain, demoted to the explicit default-only fallback. Enforcement (Pi-only, kept out of the shared defs): `spawnDurableLane` now exports `CODEFLARE_REVIEW_BASE`/`CODEFLARE_REVIEW_HEAD`/`CODEFLARE_REVIEW_BASE_REF` when an acked base exists, and `review-lane-guards.ts` gained `reviewScopeBlockReason`, which blocks full-PR diff commands (`gh pr diff`; any `git diff` ranging two- or three-dot against the base branch — `origin/<ref>`, the base ref itself, or main/master/develop) in incremental mode while allowing the window forms (`git diff <base> <head>`, `--name-only`, `-- <path>`, and a bare SHA range `<base>..<head>`). The always-on whole-tree consistency passes (walk-every-REQ / walk-every-doc-file) are unchanged — they validate tree-wide invariants, not the diff, and stay quiet on a clean tree. Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (`reviewScopeBlockReason` matrix: no base allows all, acked base blocks `gh pr diff` + `origin/<ref>...` full diff, window forms allowed; seeded reviewer defs assert scope-agnostic + full-diff default). The env binding in `spawnDurableLane` is runtime wiring (documented coverage-gap, same as the other detached-lane ACs). All changes live in the preseed source and the regenerated agent seed (`src/lib/agent-seed.generated.ts`); the local Pi agent re-seeds from R2 on next session start, so no manual `~/.pi/agent/` mirror is needed. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-040 / REQ-AGENT-060 stay Implemented.
- **Landing reframed as one governed run ("The Governed Run"): every proof artifact bound to a single PR, with DLP/guardrails/zero-trust/SDD-enforcement/browser-isolation promoted to mono evidence and the governance spine reordered to carry the page** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 enumeration + client-JS-enhancement constraint extended; nav links and section anchor ids unchanged; no serving/contact/metadata change, REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). Owner ask: the enterprise features (zero trust by design, DLP, guardrails, spec-driven development *enforcement* not just framework capability, browser isolation) were not prominent enough, and the page should read like the pinnacle of enterprise agentic-coding orchestration with Codeflare as the engine. A design workflow (6 directions, adversarial judging, synthesis) converged on binding the existing four proof artifacts into ONE run so they read as camera angles on a single change moving through the engine, rather than four unrelated widgets. Changes: (1) **Spine** — a single `SPINE` const in `site.ts` (`REQ-PAY-014` / `AC3` / `PR #207`, user `a.chen`, team `payments`) sourced once and referenced by the hero transcript, the enforcement gate, the review board, and the cost ledger so the IDs can never drift between artifacts; a hairline mono spine strip under the hero terminal names the run as the page's quiet table of contents. (2) **Hero transcript** rewritten to the governed run with the enforcement detail the owner asked for: a visible `spec-enforce` drift on AC3 (new `warn` tone), the agent correcting and re-verifying, a denied direct-provider egress rerouted through the AI Gateway (new `deny`/`t-deny` tone), and the verbatim line "specification, implementation and documentation aligned". (3) **Security** — DLP and guardrails lifted from buried card prose into auditable evidence: a new **egress-inspection strip** (`EGRESS`, a structural twin of the enforcement gate) shows one outbound model call with a guardrails pass, a single cardholder-PAN DLP redaction (the one amber `is-redact` beat), and an approved route; the denied-paths list gains "Privilege escalation: nothing to escalate into" and renders at equal weight beside the approved boundary path. (4) **Context** — browser isolation promoted from cards to a peer-level **isolation pipe** artifact (`CONTEXT.pipe`: source URL → isolated browser → structured markdown) with the load-bearing "the page never touches the agent container or your network" guarantee on the render node. (5) **Method** — the self-healing enforcement gate promoted ABOVE the prose, the three pillars rendered as numbered clauses of a control (not a feature-card grid), and the enforcement refrain stated verbatim as the gate caption. (6) **Stat band** reworked into instrument gauges: mono channel micro-caps (Gateway / Endpoint / Infra / Orchestration), a baseline tick under each value, and the one coral governance tick on the AI Gateway 100% anchor. (7) **Pipeline** review board gains an overhead conductor label (`PR #207 · 6 lanes dispatched · 1 human gate`). (8) **Cost** ledger bound to the spine run with a sample/totals reconciliation note (the visible rows are a sample of the run the totals cover). (9) **Order** — sections reordered so the governance spine (Method, Security, Operations, Context, Pipeline, Cost, Tenancy) carries the page and the platform-capability payoff (Platform, Browser) lands after it; Operations gains a closing coda and Tenancy's manifest is set in mono to echo the instrument grammar. The design workflow proposed a colored `border-left` "channel rail" on each artifact row; rejected on the design ruleset's side-stripe-border ban — the four-state legend is carried by the existing colored state pills instead. All copy stays free of en/em dashes (CI tripwire); every artifact still ships its resolved static state and a reduced-motion path. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Page-wide flare-fluid now runs on touch devices too, driven by scroll** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) constraint 5; no AC change). Owner request: the flare effect should be present on mobile while scrolling, matching the existing codeflare web app (whose `SplashCursor` runs the same fluid on all devices). The landing previously gated the WebGL fluid to `pointer: fine` (desktop) so mobile stayed solid. Now `splash.ts` gates on `prefers-reduced-motion` and WebGL availability (no longer on pointer type): desktop fine pointers still drive the fluid with the cursor, and touch devices (no cursor) drive it from page scroll. The engine (`splash-cursor-logic.ts`) gained a second, dedicated `scrollPointer` (kept separate from the touch/cursor `pointers[0]` so a touch-drag and a scroll never fight over one pointer) plus a `pointerMove(xFrac, yFrac)` method; `splash.ts` sweeps a virtual pointer along a gentle Lissajous path mapped from `scrollY` (rAF-throttled, first call primes without splatting, one seed splat on load so the hero shows flare before any scroll). `html.flare-on` (glass panels + scroll-linked veil) now activates on mobile too; reduced-motion and no-WebGL visitors still keep the solid surfaces. Constraint 5 reworded from "desktop/fine-pointer only" to "driven by the cursor on desktop and by page scroll on touch". **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing body reworked into mono "proof artifacts" + three bug fixes** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 content + AC presentation; nav links and section anchor ids unchanged, so the "all content sections with anchor ids matching the nav links" AC still holds; no serving/metadata change). Owner feedback: the hero is strong but the body card grids read as generic AI-template content; make it more distinctive and "wow" while staying calm, add more terminal-style examples, and out-class Kiro and Conductor. After a competitive teardown (both rivals' biggest gap is a near-absent security/governance story, and both prove the product by showing it *work*) and consulting Google + OpenAI's latest models, the weakest card sections were converted into proof artifacts in the hero's terminal aesthetic, each rendering its resolved final state in markup and replaying a one-shot reveal on scroll-in via a new `proof.ts` (`[data-proof]` + `.is-live`; reduced-motion keeps the static state): (1) **Method** self-healing enforcement gate (`METHOD.gate`) that visibly fails (spec-enforce, tdd-enforce) then corrects and passes, replacing the flat enforcement trace; (2) **Security** boundary data-path now also lists what the architecture makes impossible (`BOUNDARY_BLOCKED` denied-paths) and lights the approved path stage by stage; (3) **Pipeline** parallel review board (`PIPELINE.lanes`/`verdict`) of six reviewer lanes (two catching a finding and re-proving it) converging on one human triage gate, replacing the static snippet; (4) **Cost** attribution ledger (`COST.ledger`) where every line carries an owner and the closing total reads zero unattributed. Removed the now-unused `SnippetLine` type. Also fixed three reported bugs: **(a)** mobile horizontal scroll (the pipeline mono block forced its CSS-grid track wider than the viewport; fixed with `min-width:0` on `.split` children + `overflow-x:clip` on body); **(b)** the nav "Sign in" link bounced unauthenticated visitors back to the landing (`/app/` redirects to `/`); now points at the SPA `/login` provider chooser that starts OAuth; **(c)** content "flash" while scrolling on mobile (Motion's `inView` re-fired the reveal on every re-entry; made one-shot with a `WeakSet` guard). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing gains a "Context" section: browser-isolated web ingestion to agent-ready markdown** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 content, covered by "all content sections with anchor ids matching the nav links"; no behavior change). Owner input: Codeflare agents consume internet locations using browser isolation, turning JavaScript-heavy and gated-off content into structured markdown optimized for agent ingestion. A new section (`#context`, placed after Platform so internal scaffolding flows into external web context; deliberately NOT added to `NAV_LINKS` to avoid crowding the 7-link nav) presents the capability in three cards (`CONTEXT` in `site.ts`): browser-isolated retrieval (pages render in a throwaway isolated browser that runs their JavaScript and interactive steps, so SPAs, dynamic dashboards, and login-gated docs resolve to real content without touching the agent container or your network), distillation to clean structured markdown (headings/tables/code/links kept, chrome/scripts stripped, token-efficient), and ingestion straight into the session context or knowledge graph inside your boundary. Rendered with the existing tagged-card template (plain `section` so band rhythm holds after the plain Platform section). No serving, contact-pipeline, or metadata change (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing positioning broadened beyond code: a new "Operations" section on governed infrastructure access** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 content, covered by "all content sections with anchor ids matching the nav links"; no behavior change). Owner input: Codeflare is for more than coding — the same governed autonomous agents can orchestrate infrastructure, patch servers, and support migrations. A new section (`#operations`, added to `NAV_LINKS` between Security and Pipeline so it builds on the just-established zero-trust boundary) presents the capability: the agents reach internal hosts, databases, and control planes through zero-trust, policy-scoped tunnels gated by Cloudflare Access, so a session sees only what its group's policy allows (no flat-network VPN, no credentials in the container); they operate rather than only author (orchestration, patching, migrations, runbooks, incident response) with the same review pipeline + human triage gating the change; and every connection/command is attributed in the customer's own logs. Three cards (`OPERATIONS` in `site.ts`), rendered with the existing tagged-card template; the hero's coding-led hook is deliberately left intact. No serving, contact-pipeline, or metadata change (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing flare-fluid extended page-wide, the hero scramble unblocked, and the duplicate demo CTA removed** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) client-JS-enhancement constraint reworded hero→page-wide; no AC/behavior change). Three owner follow-ups after seeing the deploy. (1) **Scramble fix (was broken live).** The hero accent-word scramble never ran on the deployed site: the Worker serves landing docs under a strict CSP (`script-src 'self'`, no `'unsafe-inline'`/nonce), and Astro inlines any bundled script under ~4 KB straight into the HTML, so the (small) scramble and contact-controller modules were refused by CSP — while the larger splash/reveal modules stayed external and ran (hence "splash works, scramble doesn't"). The same inlining blocked a `data:` font under `font-src 'self'`. Fixed at the build layer, not by weakening the CSP: `vite.build.assetsInlineLimit: 0` (`landing/astro.config.mjs`) forces every script/font/asset out to an external `/landing/_astro/*` file served from `'self'`. (2) **Flare-fluid now page-wide.** The fluid moves from a hero-only absolute canvas to a fixed full-viewport layer (`.flare-field` in `BaseLayout.astro`) behind every section, reacting to the cursor across the whole page (window-bound listeners). A scroll-linked readability veil keeps it vivid behind the hero and deepens to a near-solid, legible wash once the hero scrolls away; content panels become translucent "glass" floating over it (dense-text panels near-opaque for prose AA, showcase artifacts blurred; stat tiles/flow nodes/form inputs stay solid). The whole glass system activates only when the fluid is actually live (`splash.ts` sets `html.flare-on`), so touch / no-WebGL / reduced-motion visitors keep the solid default surfaces. Still desktop/fine-pointer only, off under `prefers-reduced-motion`, paused on a hidden tab. (3) **Duplicate "Book a demo" removed.** It appeared in both the nav and the hero; the nav now carries only the "Sign in" launch, the hero keeps "Book a demo" as the lead CTA (still in the footer too). No serving, contact-pipeline, or metadata change (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing gains a restrained micro-interaction pass (calibrated via the `emil-design-eng` craft skill)** (no REQ behavior change; presentational, covered by REQ-LANDING-001's client-JS-enhancement constraint). Five subtle, purposeful touches, all GPU-friendly (transform/opacity/shadow), under ~250ms on the project's existing strong ease-out, hover gated to `(hover: hover) and (pointer: fine)`, and stopped under `prefers-reduced-motion`: grid reveals now stagger their children (60ms cascade via `[data-stagger]`) instead of fading as one block; the primary CTA lifts with a soft flare shadow on hover; nav links grow an underline from the left; cards gain a faint flare edge-glow on hover; and the sticky nav gains a depth seam (shadow/border, no movement) once scrolled past the hero. Deliberately skipped as slop: stat count-ups, parallax, per-section bespoke entrances, gradient shimmer, magnetic buttons. **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing gains a hero flare-fluid signature and a Sign in launch path into the app** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) two new constraints: client-JS-enhancement extended + app launch CTA). Two owner requests, shaped through the `impeccable` design tooling before building. (1) **Flare-fluid signature.** A cursor-reactive WebGL fluid simulation (ported from the web-ui `SplashCursor` / `splash-cursor-logic.ts` set into `landing/src/lib/`, pinned to the flare palette instead of the original rainbow) mounts behind the hero only (`landing/src/scripts/splash.ts`). Per the brand register's "drenched hero is voice" permission and "art direction per section", it is the page's single bold moment: it dissolves into the section below (CSS mask) so the dense lower sections stay calm and AA-legible. The hero terminal is the one deliberate glass panel (translucent + backdrop-blur) with the fluid animating faintly under it (the in-app session-window look) — glass is used here and nowhere else, honoring impeccable's "glassmorphism as default" ban. Desktop/fine-pointer only (mobile stays clean and fast), disabled under `prefers-reduced-motion`, paused off-screen (IntersectionObserver) and on a hidden tab; a readability scrim (gated to when the canvas exists) keeps hero prose above 4.5:1. (2) **Launch path.** The landing had no way into the app; a Sign in action (nav + footer) now links to the existing `APP_LINKS.signIn` (`/app/`), the auth wall handling unauthenticated visitors — no new auth behavior. No serving, contact-pipeline, or metadata change (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **Landing content sharpened to Codeflare's real product, spec-driven development elevated to a standout, and the hero accent word given the Codeflare scramble effect** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 + new client-JS-is-enhancement constraint). The owner reviewed the calm rebuild (entry below) and asked for content and one effect, not a redesign. Changes: (1) the hero accent word ("a coding assistant.") now carries the Codeflare scramble effect ported from the web-ui `ScrambleText` component (`use-scramble-text.ts`, fourPhase) to vanilla DOM — a perpetual hold/scramble/decrypt/swap loop, reduced-motion-safe, with each word split into a width-locked box so the glyph churn never reflows the headline on mobile (`landing/src/scripts/scramble.ts`, loaded from `BaseLayout.astro`). (2) The hero terminal's generic "rate limiting" session is replaced with a real Codeflare flow: `/sdd init` bootstrapping spec-driven development off a knowledge graph, tests-first TDD, a `/review --deep` 6-agent PR boundary, verification vs code + docs, and human triage. (3) A new "method" section (`#method`, in `NAV_LINKS`) presents spec-driven development as a standout: Codeflare both develops under SDD and *enforces* SDD + TDD compliance as a self-healing loop that gives the agent no room to deviate, shown with a concrete enforcement trace of a drift caught and corrected. (5) Every "gateway" reference is made explicit as the AI Gateway with guardrails, DLP, and rate controls (security egress card, boundary-flow node, cost inference layer, tenancy checklist, FAQ, stat band). - **Landing page rebuilt: the "governed session" terminal UI replaced with a calm, conventional enterprise page** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4 rewritten, superseding the same-day governed-session entry below). The owner rejected the full-page fake-terminal conceit (fixed session chrome + status bar + session clock, per-section prompt-path/timestamp labels, the four hero stats reframed as preflight boot assertions, and the hero terminal FLIP-splitting into a four-pane animated fleet) as visually chaotic and exhausting, especially on mobile. The page is now sans-serif prose with mono reserved for ONE static, legible terminal demo; a single locked accent; generous whitespace; drastically reduced copy; and varied per-section layouts (stat band, two-column compare, security cards plus a boundary data-path flow diagram, feature columns, a point list plus a static review-pipeline code block, cost layers, a tenancy checklist, and a FAQ accordion). Removed the gimmick machinery entirely: components (SessionChrome, StatusBar, SessionEnd, FleetTerminal, PreflightLedger, BoundaryDiagram, SecurityLedger, ManPage, SeedLog, PipelineRail, CostTrace, TenancyPlaque, DiffCompare, Section, PromptLabel, SessionPane, Snippet) and scripts (scene-script, status-bar-state, session-clock, fleet-scheduler, odometer, scrollspy, build-diff, flip-transform, terminal-player) with their unit tests. AC4 no longer requires fleet panes or preflight boot assertions; it requires the hero plus the single terminal, stat band, content sections, FAQ, and contact form to render statically with no JS. Serving, the contact pipeline (`contact-controller.ts`), and OG/Twitter metadata are preserved unchanged (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched). **Status:** REQ-LANDING-001 stays Implemented.
- **The missed-boundary review offer is now a passive toast ONLY — never a chat/transcript message** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) offer behavior). The `codeflare-review-offered` `pi.sendMessage` chat message (added 2026-06-11 for transcript durability) is removed, along with its `registerMessageRenderer`. A live Pi run (gpt-5.5 `clone-overrun-analysis.md`) after a clone of `ai-news-digest` (open develop→main PR #287, inherited head) showed the agent treating the chat-visible offer as an instruction: it read "Run `/review-run` to start the required reviewers" and spiraled into trying to auto-run/auto-skip the review after a clone-only request — turning a passive safety heads-up into unsolicited work. A `display:true` custom message is agent-readable, so a durable transcript copy of the offer is fundamentally unsafe. The offer now surfaces only as the `ctx.ui.notify` toast (UI-only, not agent-visible) plus the `boundary_offered` audit event; the per-session dedupe (`offerSurfacedThisSession`/`markOfferSurfaced`) is unchanged. Durability of enforcement is unaffected — the merge gate (the `gh pr merge` block) is the hard stop, not a transcript message. This does NOT touch the separate Graphify post-clone follow-up (`codeflare-pi.ts`), which still injects a `role:user` message; that is a distinct subsystem. Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`; seed regenerated. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Implemented.
- **Landing page redesigned as the "governed session" UI; AC4 tightened to no-JS completeness** ([REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving) AC4). AC4 now requires the full narrative — including the fleet panes — to render statically with no JS (hidden animation states only apply under a pre-paint `html[data-js]` flip). Behavior modules (`fleet-scheduler`, `scene-script`, `flip-transform`, `odometer`, `session-clock`, `status-bar-state`, `build-diff`, `scrollspy`, extended `terminal-player` with `onLineCommit`) are pure and unit-tested; rendered quantities (gateway request count, skill/subagent counts) derive from `site.ts` constants with count-integrity tests. No serving, contact-pipeline, or metadata behavior changed (REQ-LANDING-002/003 untouched).

## 2026-06-11

- **PR-boundary review RESULTS now reliably reach the main session — durable, nonce-verified, two-phase delivery (new [REQ-AGENT-062](agents.md#req-agent-062-pi-pr-boundary-review-result-delivery))** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC4 rewritten + stale `publishSummaryForCurrentPr` anchor fixed; [REQ-AGENT-059](agents.md#req-agent-059-pi-durable-review-fix-loop) AC1/AC2/AC4 anchors repointed `requestReviewAutofix`→`sendAnnouncement`). A gpt-5.5 root-cause analysis of an `ai-news-digest` incident proved the review ENGINE worked (lanes ran, results + `summary.md` written, head acked, gate cleared) but the **result was never delivered into the session** — `announced/summary-v3.sent` and `autofix.requested` markers existed yet no `codeflare-review-summary-v3` message was in the transcript. Root cause: `pi.sendMessage` persists a custom message only when the live agent session emits a `message_end` (role:custom) event → `appendCustomMessageEntry`; the off-turn `setInterval` reaper has no live session loop (and a reload-surviving WeakMap could hand the patch a STALE bound sender), so the send silently no-ops while `publishReviewSummary` had already claimed the one-shot `summary-v3.sent` marker BEFORE sending — permanently suppressing every retry. Fix: result delivery is now a second durable phase. A per-`(head,kind)` announcement state machine (`pending→attempted→visible|failed`, records under `.git/codeflare-review-jobs/<head>/announcements/`) replaces the one-shot markers; every summary/autofix message embeds a **nonce** and is marked `visible` ONLY when that nonce is found in the session transcript (`sessionContainsNonce`) — a send is never assumed delivered. `emitPendingAnnouncements`/`reconcileAnnouncementDelivery` (`drainReviewAnnouncements`) run on every live tick (`session_start`/`turn_start`/`turn_end`/`resources_discover`/`agent_end`), bounded by a 30s retry delay × 3 attempts; an exhausted announcement is marked `failed` and the user is told to run the new `/review-results` command (the guaranteed manual fallback). A persistent `results ready (not shown) — /review-results` footer status shows until delivery is proven. `installReviewMessageDedupe` was hardened to bind the CURRENT live sender (never a reload-surviving stale one) and to drop its in-memory v3 dedupe Set (the SM owns dedupe via nonce/`visible`). Pure decisions (`shouldAttemptAnnouncement`, `announcementReconcileDecision`, `reviewAnnouncementNonce`) + the record lifecycle (`ensureReviewAnnouncementPending`/`abandonReviewAnnouncements`) are unit-tested in `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts`; the live transcript-scan/per-tick drain/command/status wiring (AC4) is load-check + post-deploy live-smoke per the runtime-coverage convention. Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`; seed regenerated. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-062 Implemented; REQ-AGENT-059 / 061 stay Implemented.
- **New Landing domain (enterprise marketing page):** added [spec/landing.md](landing.md) with three REQs. [REQ-LANDING-001](landing.md#req-landing-001-mode-aware-public-landing-serving): unauthenticated `/` in SaaS or onboarding mode now serves a prerendered Astro landing app (built into `web-ui/dist/landing/`, graceful SPA fallback when absent) instead of the in-SPA LoginPage/OnboardingLanding marketing surface. [REQ-LANDING-002](landing.md#req-landing-002-demo-request-contact-pipeline): new `POST /public/contact` + `GET /public/contact-config` demo-request pipeline (Turnstile + Resend relay, no persistence, shared topic enum in `src/lib/contact-topics.ts`); the `/public` namespace gate widened from onboarding-only to onboarding-or-SaaS, with the waitlist keeping its onboarding-only gate. [REQ-LANDING-003](landing.md#req-landing-003-landing-social-share-and-search-metadata): the landing carries the enterprise-positioned OG/Twitter metadata; [REQ-SETUP-010](setup.md#req-setup-010-social-share-preview-metadata-on-the-public-landing-page) continues to govern the SPA's own metadata unchanged.
- **PR-boundary review-lane convergence round (post third-Fable):** closed the last divergence between `extractReviewFindings` and `countReviewSeverities` — a bare decorated severity label with no inline title (`**CRITICAL**` alone) was counted by the counter but dropped by the extractor (its `(.+?)` title group required ≥1 char), the same drift in the under-count direction. The extractor now shares the counter's byte-identical regex (`(.*)` title group) and surfaces the bare label as a finding with a placeholder `(untitled)` title rather than dropping a counted severity ([REQ-AGENT-053](agents.md#req-agent-053-pi-durable-review-status-and-result-formatting) new AC6, the parse-lockstep invariant). Spec hygiene from the same review round: [REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC1 now covers both the open/non-draft eligibility predicate and the empty-`baseRefName` onToolEnd fail-open.
- **Third Fable-5 deep review of the PR-boundary subsystem: two merge-gate fail-open holes closed, the baseline backstop suppressed after an in-session ack, plus leak/race/cleanup hardening (13 findings, all fixed)** ([REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement) AC6 gate input-decoding + foreign-repo skip; [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 autostart-vs-offer mechanism; [REQ-AGENT-063](agents.md#req-agent-063-pr-boundary-command-parsing) AC5 non-advancing-push exclusion; supporting [REQ-AGENT-054](agents.md#req-agent-054-pi-durable-review-lane-failure-handling) — no AC change). After clusters F–J the user commissioned a third Fable-5 ultrathink pass; it found 2 HIGH fail-open paths + 11 MEDIUM/LOW, all fixed and the user-triaged "fix all" honored. **The two HIGH are the only fail-open paths and both feed the otherwise-correct pure `mergeGateDecision` wrong facts at the gate edge.** (1) **Quoted-flag mis-target**: `mergeCommandTarget` tokenized the merge args with a raw `split(/[ \t]+/)`, so `gh pr merge -t "fix the gateway" 42` read the value's tail as the PR selector → the gate queried a phantom PR (→ allow) AND the retroactive audit missed it. Now tokenized with the quote-aware `shellWords`. (2) **gh exit-1 ambiguity**: `prStateResultFor` classified `failed = status !== 1`, but gh exits 1 for DNS failure, 401/403, 404, and rate-limit too (verified in-container), so every transient read as "no PR" → the gate failed OPEN during any GitHub blip. Now classifies by the error TEXT — a definitive GitHub "not found" (`no pull requests found` / `Could not resolve to a PullRequest|Repository`) is genuine absence; anything else with a non-zero exit is transient → fail CLOSED. The MEDIUM/LOW: a stale-PR `discardStale` now kills the discarded head's still-running lane children (was leaking reviewer processes on a force-push/close); the spawn lock reads lane state FRESH under the lock and releases only when the lock still holds our pid (closing a double-spawn TOCTOU + a lock-steal cascade); the finding extractor now requires the same decorated-label rule the counter uses, so bare prose ("Critical to the design…") no longer mints a phantom finding the count table says is 0; `git push --dry-run`/`-n`/`--delete`/`-d` no longer count as PR boundaries (a credential-probe dry run won't silently autostart on an inherited head — `--tags` stays a boundary since `git push origin main --tags` advances a head); the baseline backstop is SUPPRESSED once a branch was acked this session (a `git pull` of a remote-actor descendant now OFFERS instead of auto-starting a duplicate review — R7), keyed by the pending PR's persisted `headBranch` so an off-turn reaper finalizing under a different checked-out branch clears/marks the right branch; a `gh pr merge --repo OTHER/REPO` from inside an SDD repo is skipped by both the gate and the retroactive audit (was false-blocking + false-alarming a legitimate foreign merge); `savePending`/`writeAck`/breaker/block-count writes route through the atomic `safeWriteText` (no torn read for the 1 s footer / 20 s reaper pollers); the merge gate is deduped per tool id (was evaluated twice — `tool_call` + `tool_execution_start` — paying two cache-bypassed `gh pr view` calls + a duplicate audit row); and two dead-code carriers were removed (the unused `previousRemoteHead` reflog subprocess + its `selectReviewBase` param; the never-written `__codeflareReviewLaneDepth` lane guard, AD64/AD76). All five extensions pass the bundled-jiti load-check; mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. Tests: `review-trigger.test.ts` (`mergeCommandTarget` quoted multi-word flag value; `isPrBoundaryTrigger`/`isGitPushOnlyCommand` dry-run/delete exclusion), `review-state.test.ts` (`reviewInSessionContinuation` ackedThisSession suppression), `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (the extractor ignores a bare-prose severity word). The two HIGH I/O paths (gh classification, foreign-repo skip) and the spawn-lock/atomic-write changes are verified by inspection + the load-check (the repo's runtime-coverage convention). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-055 / 058 / 063 / 054 all stay Implemented.
- **Pi PR-boundary detection rewritten as a stateless regex parser (heredoc/ssh/https/env-prefix robust); review-repo resolution gained an in-memory active-repo fallback** ([REQ-AGENT-063](agents.md#req-agent-063-pr-boundary-command-parsing) AC2-AC6 robustness; [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC5 extended). After ~20 prior fixes the user reported "PR to main doesn't trigger the review — nothing offered, no question, nothing." Two root causes. (1) **Parser desync**: `review-helpers.ts` detected boundaries by tokenizing the whole command (`splitShellCommands`→`shellWords`); a `gh pr create --body "$(cat <<EOF …)"` whose heredoc body carried markdown pipes or apostrophes mis-split the tokenizer, dropping the `gh pr create` so no boundary fired. Replaced with stateless start/separator-anchored regexes (`RE_GIT_PUSH`/`RE_GH_PR_CREATE`/`RE_GH_PR_MERGE`/`RE_GH_PR_UPDATE_BRANCH`/`RE_GH_REPO_SYNC` + base-flag capture) over the RAW command — heredoc bodies can never desync it, and it newly recognises ssh/https remote-URL pushes and env-var-prefixed forms (`GIT_SSH_COMMAND='ssh -i k' git push`; `BOUNDARY_ANCHOR` now consumes quoted, space-bearing env values). (2) **Repo-resolution gap**: even a clean `git push` failed to reconcile because `resolveReviewRepo` returned undefined when the Pi session cwd was a non-repo parent workspace and no review had run yet. It now falls back — after `sessionReviewRepo`, before `processCwd` — to the **in-memory** active repo `codeflare-pi` tracks per tool execution (`recallActiveRepo`, the same signal the statusline uses; NOT the on-disk graphify sentinel, so routing stays sentinel-free per the 2026-06-10 decision). This is what fixes `/review-run`'s "I am not inside an SDD repository", the no-ctx reaper, and the reconcile backstop for a nested clone. Tests: `review-trigger.test.ts` (isPrBoundaryTrigger robustness: heredoc body, ssh/https remote, env-var prefix with quoted value, batched compound, false-positive guards), `review-state.test.ts` (`resolveReviewRepo` active-repo fallback before processCwd; sessionReviewRepo still preferred). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-063 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented.
- **Pi gains the `advisor` escalate-to-a-stronger-model tool (fifth always-on extension), an authored advisor skill, all pre-warmed and shadow-pinned** ([REQ-AGENT-005](agents.md#req-agent-005-pro-mode-includes-additional-skills-rules-agents-and-mcp-servers) AC8 four→five extensions). `@juicesharp/rpiv-advisor@1.19.1` is added to `preseed/agents/pi/package.json` + the entrypoint `required` set so it loads in every Pi session (always-on, ctx-independent — option chosen by the user alongside the already-present `pi-web-access`). The `advisor` tool hands the full conversation branch to a stronger reviewer model picked via `/advisor`; it authenticates through **Pi's own model registry** (no per-user API key — reuses the session's provider auth), as does `pi-web-access`'s `web_search` (zero-config Exa MCP). A codeflare-authored `skills/advisor/SKILL.md` (modes default+advanced, manifest-registered) tells the agent when/how to escalate; pi-web-access keeps its bundled `librarian` + existing codeflare web-access skill. **Pre-warm**: `rpiv-advisor` is baked into the image npm cache + jiti transpile warm automatically (both derive from the preseed `package.json`); separately `consult-llm-mcp` is pinned + globally installed in the Dockerfile so the Claude/Pi MCP config invokes the global bin with no per-session `npx -y` fetch. **Shadow pins**: `bump-shadow-pins.yml`'s `pi-preseed` job was generalized to diff EVERY preseed dep against npm latest (previously only `@gotgenes/pi-subagents` + `context-mode`, leaving the rpiv family / pi-web-access / pi-mcp-adapter untracked), plus a new `consult-llm-mcp` job for the Dockerfile pin (`bun` stays a deliberate manual pin). Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (advisor skill seeded among the five Pi tool-extension skills). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-005 stays Implemented.
- **Pi preseed extension hardening: cross-extension state moved to `globalThis`, boundary/clone detection scoped shell-only + env-prefix-tolerant, `gh pr view` cached, push-path enforcement fails open on empty base** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC5; [REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC1; [REQ-AGENT-063](agents.md#req-agent-063-pr-boundary-command-parsing) AC1-AC2; [REQ-AGENT-025](agents.md#req-agent-025-post-clone-graph-triage) AC1/AC5; [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1). Pi 0.79.1's loader (`createJiti(moduleCache:false)`) gives each extension its own instance of every imported module, so the module-local active-repo/review-repo memory written by `codeflare-pi.ts` was invisible to `review-enforcement.ts` and `local-statusline.ts` — the `gh pr view` reconcile tick fired every turn but bailed at `!repo` (no resolvable repo) before ever querying GitHub, which is why "PR to main still doesn't trigger review" survived ~20 prior regex fixes: the unmistakable signal was never queried, not mis-parsed. Repo memory and the `gh pr view` cache now live on `globalThis` via `Symbol.for` keys (`codeflare.activeRepo`/`codeflare.reviewRepo`/`codeflare.prCache`; cache TTL 60 s OPEN / 10 s negative, transient `gh` failures uncached). Boundary and clone detection extract command text shell-only (`commandTextFromEvent`/`shellCommandText`: Bash `.command`, `ctx_execute` `.code` only when `language === "shell"`, `ctx_batch_execute` `.commands[].command`), so non-shell `ctx_execute` source literals no longer false-fire; a shared `ENV_PREFIX` makes `BROWSER="" gh repo clone` / `GIT_TERMINAL_PROMPT=0 git clone` match. The clone directive distinguishes a stale graph (explicit STALE lead) from unknown freshness via `exists`/`freshness` callbacks. On the real-push `onToolEnd` path only, `isEnforcedPrForPush` fails open when an OPEN PR returns an empty `baseRefName`; the reconcile tick and merge gate stay strict. The command regex stays a loose candidate — `gh pr view` is the authoritative gate. Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (commandTextFromEvent shell-only gate; cloneTargetPath env-prefix forms; graphifyClonePromptDecision exists/freshness gating). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-036 / 063 / 025 / 058 / 061 stay Implemented.
- **Pi durable review reaper made retry-aware + self-healing; consult-llm Pi MCP server pinned keep-alive** ([REQ-AGENT-054](agents.md#req-agent-054-pi-durable-review-lane-failure-handling) AC6 clarified + AC7 added; [REQ-AGENT-031](agents.md#req-agent-031-consult-llm-key-isolation-subscription-backend-and-multi-agent-parity) AC4 extended). A live Pi run on integration (the deployed PR-boundary fix worked — repo + boundary detected) surfaced two issues. (1) **Durable orchestration mis-failed a retried lane**: a spec-reviewer lane hit a transient WebSocket error, pi auto-retried in-process and produced a clean final report, but the reaper marked it `failed` ~112 s in and never recovered. `summarizeLaneTranscript` set `agentEnded` on the `willRetry:true` attempt-end (treating a retryable attempt as terminal) and kept `errored` sticky across the retry, so even the later success read as unusable. Now an `agent_end` with `willRetry:true` does NOT settle the lane and discards that attempt's `errored`/`stopReason`/final-text so the retry's verdict stands alone; only a terminal `agent_end` (`willRetry:false`) settles it. `reapLaneDecision` + `reapDurableReviewLanes` gained self-healing: a lane an earlier/raced reaper marked `failed` whose transcript later carries a terminal clean usable result (and no result file yet) is recovered to `completed` (audit event `lane_recovered`); a killed/timed-out/genuinely-errored lane stays failed. (2) **MCP footer showed `0/1 … cached`**: the entrypoint wrote the Pi `consult-llm` mcp.json server with no `lifecycle`, so pi-mcp-adapter defaulted it to `lazy` and closed it on idle (the keep-alive was never shipped — FIX 4 was deferred, not a failed edit). It is now `lifecycle:"keep-alive"` (connect on startup, auto-reconnect); the Claude server is unchanged (Claude Code has no `lifecycle` concept). Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (retry-aware `summarizeLaneTranscript` + `reapLaneDecision` self-heal table), `entrypoint-consult-llm.test.js` (Pi server keep-alive; Claude server carries no lifecycle). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-054 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-031 stays Implemented.
- **Pi missed-boundary recovery: the reconcile baseline survives module reload AND advances on every in-session ack (autostart now fires for in-session descendant pushes), and a missed-boundary offer is durable in chat** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 mechanism hardened and AC4 extended). A live Pi run (gpt-5.5 debug report, `pr-boundary-review-trigger-debug-report.md`) on ai-news-digest PR #287 showed an in-session `git push` (04dc358 → 2bc5e29) to an open enforced develop→main PR neither auto-start review nor surface anything the user could see — reconciliation chose OFFER and emitted it only as a transient `ctx.ui.notify` toast (plus a `boundary_offered` audit event; no chat message). Two root causes. (1) **Baseline lost / never advanced**: `reviewSessionBaselineHead` was a module-local `Map`, so Pi 0.79.1's `createJiti(moduleCache:false)` reload reset it mid-session, AND it was only ever seeded from the first head observed — never updated when a review acked a head. After the 04dc358 review acked, the 2bc5e29 push had no ancestor baseline, so `reviewBaselineContinuation` returned false → OFFER instead of AUTOSTART. The baseline now lives on `globalThis` (`Symbol.for("codeflare.reviewSessionBaselineHead")`, helpers `reviewBaselineMemory`/`rememberReviewBaseline`) so it survives the reload, and `writeAck` advances it to every acked head — so an in-session push to a descendant of a just-reviewed head is recognised as an in-session continuation and auto-starts. This does NOT reintroduce the bug-A fresh-launch regression: the baseline is process-scoped and never read from disk, so a genuinely new process has no in-session ack and an inherited head still offers. (2) **Offer invisible**: the offer branch now emits a durable `codeflare-review-offered` chat message via `pi.sendMessage` (registered markdown renderer) alongside the toast and the `boundary_offered` audit event, deduped per head by the offered-marker, so the merge-blocking offer persists in the transcript. Also (AC4): the actual-command `onToolEnd` path now stamps a `boundary_tool_end_ignored` audit event (`no_resolvable_head`/`dedupe_skipped`) when a confirmed-enforced PR's boundary tool-event is dropped after the enforcement check, so a direct-path near-miss is diagnosable (reconciliation still backstops the start). Deferred from the report: the `tool_execution_start`-shape command-stitching accelerator (report Fix 2 — reconciliation is the authoritative gate, the command regex stays a loose candidate) and merge-gate offered-state wording (Fix 7). The pure `reviewBaselineContinuation`/`reconcileBoundaryAction` decision stays unit-tested; the globalThis store, baseline-on-ack, durable offer message, and onToolEnd audit are runtime wiring verified by inspection + a bundled-jiti load-check. Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Implemented.
- **consult-llm "List all available models" shows concrete Gemini/OpenAI IDs from the server startup log instead of mistaking provider selectors for models** ([REQ-AGENT-031](agents.md#req-agent-031-consult-llm-key-isolation-subscription-backend-and-multi-agent-parity) AC5 mechanism specified). A live Pi run (gpt-5.5 report, `llms.md`) showed that choosing "List all available models" listed provider SELECTORS (`gemini`, `openai`, `anthropic`, `deepseek`, `minimax`) instead of concrete model IDs (`gemini-3.1-pro-preview`, `gpt-5.5`, …), then asked a second useless provider-family question. Root cause: the skill told the agent to "read the supported set from the `consult_llm` tool's `model` parameter", but consult-llm-mcp v2.13.x deliberately removed the concrete-model enum from its schema (CHANGELOG: "Replaced hardcoded model enum with abstract selectors") and now exposes `model` as `string|null` + prose listing only selectors — there is no model-list tool and no schema enum on either the Claude or Pi MCP gateway (verified against the installed 2.13.4 package + the live tool schema). The concrete, per-session list is emitted only to the server startup log. Both `consult-llm` SKILL.md files (Claude + Pi) now read the latest `AVAILABLE MODELS:` block from `~/.local/state/consult-llm-mcp/mcp.log` (preferring a future list-models tool / schema enum if one ever appears), keep only Gemini (`gemini-*`) and OpenAI (`gpt-*`) IDs (this deployment configures only those two providers — anthropic/deepseek/minimax are ignored, never surfaced), print them grouped in chat, then ask one compact follow-up (latest Gemini / latest OpenAI / both / `Other` free-text exact ID); and never label selectors as "all available models". The upstream-only remedies (a first-class `list_models` MCP tool, a schema enum, or fixing Pi's MCP-gateway rendering) are outside codeflare's control and not attempted. Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (the broken "read the supported set from the model parameter" instruction is gone; both skills cite the startup-log source + Gemini/OpenAI scoping + never-present-selectors-as-models). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-031 stays Implemented.
- **Second Fable-5 deep review of the PR-boundary subsystem: the merge gate is now a pure, unit-tested decision over the PR the command actually targets; roll-forward kills superseded lanes; result-pruning is ancestor-scoped across both result dirs; plus a spawn lock, atomic result writes, gh-outage auditing, severity-prose hardening, draft suppression, and a multi-repo reaper** ([REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement) AC3 lane-abandonment + new AC6 merge-gate decision; [REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC1 draft clause; supporting [REQ-AGENT-054](agents.md#req-agent-054-pi-durable-review-lane-failure-handling), [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery), [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) — no AC change). With clusters A–E landed (entry above), the user commissioned a SECOND Fable-5 ultrathink pass over the whole subsystem to catch anything the first missed; it surfaced 11 further edge-case defects (P1–P11) and 10 regression risks (R1–R10), fixed here in clusters F–J and gated-cluster-first. (F) **Merge gate extracted to a pure decision**: the `gh pr merge` block logic became `mergeGateDecision(input)` (allow / bypass / block) in `review-job-helpers.ts`, fully unit-tested, with the handler reduced to thin wiring. It evaluates the PR the merge command *actually targets* — `mergeCommandTarget` (`review-helpers.ts`) parses a PR number, a `/pull/N` URL, a branch, or a `--repo`/`-R` slug out of the command (and skips value-flag arguments) rather than assuming the cwd branch — so `gh pr merge 123` against a different PR is gated correctly. It fails CLOSED when the targeted PR is readable-but-malformed (OPEN with empty `baseRefName`/`headRefOid`, via the new `prStateResultFor` that distinguishes a genuine no-PR `gh` exit from a transient failure) or when `gh` is transiently unreadable while any unacked merge-blocking head exists (pending, latched-breaker, or outstanding offer — surfaced by `gateCandidates`); and it blocks `--auto` on an enforced unacked PR (which would otherwise merge server-side after checks without re-consulting the gate). (G) **Resource/leak closure**: a roll-forward to a descendant head now `abandonDurableReviewLanes` on the superseded head (AC3 — killing only its still-`running` lane process groups; completed results are reused) in BOTH the classify path and `rollForwardAdvancedReview`; `pruneReviewResults` now loops over both result dirs (`sdd-review-results`, `codeflare-review-jobs`) and deletes only entries that are STRICT ANCESTORS of the kept head (`isAncestor`), never a sibling/descendant; `toolStartArgs` is cleared at the top of `agent_end`; result writes go through `safeWriteText` (tmp + atomic rename) so a crashed write can't leave a truncated JSON result; and `startDurableReviewLanes` takes an `O_EXCL` spawn lock (30 s stale TTL) so a double-fire can't spawn two lane sets. (H) **Autostart attribution**: a `boundaryActedThisSession` set keyed by `repo\0branch` (NUL-separated) is marked in `onToolEnd` BEFORE any window guard, so a dropped window still records the push; `durableJobIsActiveWindow` requires a running/completed lane before a durable job counts as a live reconcile window (an all-failed job no longer suppresses a fresh start). (I) **Correctness/polish**: the push path audits `pr_state_unreadable` and marks the boundary acted (so reconcile autostarts when `gh` recovers) instead of going silent during an outage; `countReviewSeverities` counts a severity word only when DECORATED as a finding label (`[HIGH]`, `**HIGH**`, `HIGH:`) so lane prose ("High-level summary", "Critical to the design") can't mint a phantom finding; `/review-skip` resets the in-memory window and clears the status row; `/review-status` shell-out is 5 s-bounded and resolves from the Pi session cwd; a push to a DRAFT PR no longer arms review (AC1 draft clause — reconcile catches it when the PR flips ready, and a draft can't merge meanwhile); and the no-ctx reaper finalizes EVERY repo with a pending review this session (`recallReviewRepos`), not just the last-pinned slot. (J) **Merge-gate posture documented as [AD80](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad80-pi-pr-boundary-merge-gate-is-report-only-and-defended-in-depth)**: the gate is report-only (blocks until the reviewers RAN, never on findings severity) and defended in depth — the `onAgentStart` pre-block PLUS a retroactive `merge_completed_unreviewed` audit+toast for wrapper forms the pre-block can't intercept (`bash -c`, `xargs`, server-side `--auto`). All four extensions pass the bundled-jiti load-check; mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`mergeGateDecision` — head_not_acked block, acked allow, non-enforced/no-PR allow, transient/malformed fail-closed with pending, breaker/offer candidate, bypass), `review-trigger.test.ts` (`mergeCommandTarget` — number/URL/branch/`--repo`/`--auto`/value-flag/wrapper; `isGhPrMergeCommand` wrapper-word tolerance). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-055 stays Implemented (new AC6 merge-gate decision unit-tested); REQ-AGENT-036 stays Implemented (draft clause); REQ-AGENT-054 / 058 / 061 stay Implemented.
- **PR-boundary review subsystem end-to-end hardening from a Fable-5 deep review: autostart driven by an explicit "this session pushed" signal, branch-keyed baseline, per-session offer dedup, merge-gate fail-closed-on-unreadable-PR, superseded-head lane cleanup, plus four lifecycle leaks** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 mechanism re-derived; supporting [REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement), [REQ-AGENT-056](agents.md#req-agent-056-pi-local-statusline-footer), [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) — no AC change). After ~30 rounds of incremental fixes (each tending to break an adjacent path), the user commissioned a Fable-5 ultrathink end-to-end review of the whole subsystem; it found 3 regressions + 16 edge-case defects, fixed here in five clusters. **This entry corrects the mechanism described in the "Pi missed-boundary recovery" entry above**: that design advanced the reconcile baseline on every ack (`writeAck` → `rememberReviewBaseline`) and deduped the offer with an on-disk per-head marker — both since replaced. (A) **Merge-gate holes**: the `gh pr merge` gate now reads PR state cache-bypassed (`prStateFresh`) so a just-pushed head can't merge against a stale cache; when `gh pr view` is unreadable AND an unacked pending review exists for the local head, the gate FAILS CLOSED (`pr_state_unreadable_review_pending`) instead of failing open; and it resolves the enforced head through the same `resolveEnforcedHead` the start path uses. (B) **Autostart-vs-offer re-derived**: the PRIMARY autostart signal is now `boundaryActedThisSession` — a `globalThis` set of repo+branch keys marked in `onToolEnd` the instant a real boundary command runs, BEFORE any window-creation guard, so a dropped window still records that this session pushed; the per-session baseline (now branch-keyed via `baselineKey`, seeded on first observation, NOT advanced on ack) is only a backstop for a reload that ate the tool-event. `reviewInSessionContinuation` autostarts on either signal; a head matching neither (fresh clone, relaunch, bare checkout of another branch) offers. The offer is deduped PER SESSION (`offerSurfacedThisSession`/`markOfferSurfaced` on `globalThis`), replacing the on-disk per-head-EVER marker that suppressed the offer forever (the "nothing offered, nothing" symptom on relaunch). (C) **Lifecycle/state**: a relative boundary-command cwd is resolved against the session cwd before `findGitRoot` (no more binding the parent workspace for a nested clone); review-repo memory is remembered only when a pending review actually exists (no poisoning the footer slot); the session-file path is recalled from `globalThis` so the no-ctx reaper reads the right transcript; `toolStartArgs` is consumed once; and a non-descendant head supersede now KILLS the abandoned head's still-running lane process groups (`abandonDurableReviewLanes`) and audits `review_superseded` instead of leaking them on the 1-vCPU box. (D) **Four leaks**: the dead `pruneReviewResults` is now called from `writeAck` (the single ack choke point) so old PR-HEAD result dirs don't accumulate; `session_start` guards on `isActiveRun()` so a reloaded-over stale instance can't double-spawn; the breaker-open / no-head near-miss audit is deduped once per (repo, head, reason) so the 20 s reconcile tick can't drown the event log; and the push fail-open path persists a concrete `baseRefName` ("main") instead of "" (an empty base made `loadPending` reject the row, orphaning the whole pending review). (E) Detailed plain-language comments were added throughout the four review extensions documenting the gh-pr-view-is-authoritative principle, the module-local/`globalThis`/disk state-tier model, and every non-obvious decision. The command regex stays a loose accelerator; `gh pr view` reconciliation remains the authoritative gate. All four extensions pass the bundled-jiti load-check. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`reviewInSessionContinuation` boundaryActed/baseline/offer cases), `review-trigger.test.ts` (`isGhPrMergeCommand`/`isGitPushOnlyCommand` env-prefix tolerance). Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 / 055 / 056 / 061 stay Implemented.

## 2026-06-10

- **consult-llm keys isolated to the MCP server, subscription-first backend, Pi parity, a five-choice model dialog, and full enterprise suppression** ([REQ-AGENT-031](agents.md#req-agent-031-consult-llm-key-isolation-subscription-backend-and-multi-agent-parity) rewritten 5-AC → 6-AC; [REQ-AGENT-009](agents.md#req-agent-009-llm-api-key-storage-encrypted-in-kv) + [REQ-AGENT-020](agents.md#req-agent-020-llm-api-key-management-ui) enterprise constraint added; [REQ-SESSION-015](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-015-container-port-readiness-gating-with-pre-warm-pre-condition) AC4 anchor clarified). The latest Pi auto-detects `OPENAI_API_KEY`/`GEMINI_API_KEY` from the container's GLOBAL env and prefers them over the user's subscription, silently draining the API account until OpenAI returns `429 insufficient_quota` (confirmed live: disconnecting the key + re-login fixed it). The keys were only ever meant for the `consult-llm-mcp` server but leaked to every agent via global-env inheritance. Fix, five parts: (1) **Isolation** — `container-env.ts` now injects the keys under a `CODEFLARE_`-namespaced name (`CODEFLARE_OPENAI_API_KEY`/`CODEFLARE_GEMINI_API_KEY`); the bare names NEVER appear in the container's global env, and `entrypoint.sh` maps them back to the standard names ONLY inside the consult-llm MCP server's scoped `env` block. (2) **Subscription-first** — OpenAI routes through the Codex CLI backend (`CONSULT_LLM_OPENAI_BACKEND=codex-cli`, reasoning effort high) when `~/.codex/auth.json` is present (passing the API key only as a fallback), else the API key; Gemini is always the API key (no consult-llm-compatible Gemini subscription CLI ships — gemini-cli was replaced by Antigravity per AD65, opencode's Google is Vertex/API-key only). (3) **Pi parity** — Pi now gets the consult-llm server via `~/.pi/agent/mcp.json` with `directTools:["consult_llm"]` (pi-mcp-adapter promotes it to a first-class tool) plus a native Pi `consult-llm` skill; it stays scoped to Claude + Pi only (kept in `CLAUDE_ONLY_SKILLS` so codex/opencode/antigravity — which have no consult-llm server — never get a skill referencing a missing tool). (4) **Five-choice model dialog** — the rewritten skill (Claude + Pi, `AskUserQuestion`/`ask_user_question`) offers four explicit choices + the tool's automatic "Other" write-in when the user names no model (latest Gemini, latest OpenAI, both, list-all), resolving "latest" through the server-side `"openai"`/`"gemini"` selectors — removing the old `curl /v1/models -H "Authorization: Bearer $KEY"` step that both leaked the raw key and pinned stale flagships. (5) **Enterprise off** — the whole surface is unavailable in enterprise mode (models route through the AI Gateway BYOK): keys not injected, `/api/llm-keys` returns 403 on every method, the Settings "LLM API Keys" section hidden, and the entrypoint writes no consult-llm MCP config and removes any seeded skill dirs. The MCP config is wrapped in a shell function invoked with `|| echo WARNING` so a jq/IO failure can never crash-loop the container before the init-complete flag. Tests: `container-env.test.ts` (CODEFLARE_-namespaced injection + bare-name-absent regression + enterprise no-inject), `host/__tests__/entrypoint-consult-llm.test.js` (real entrypoint block: codex-cli vs API backend, Pi directTools, no-provider skip, merge-preserves-existing, enterprise gate + skill removal), `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (consult-llm Claude+Pi-only scoping; five-choice dialog + selectors + no provider curl), `llm-keys.test.ts` (enterprise 403 on GET/PUT/DELETE before any KV touch). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-031 stays Implemented (all 6 ACs unit/host-tested); REQ-AGENT-009 / REQ-AGENT-020 stay Implemented.
- **Enterprise containers crash-looped on every start: a reserved jq keyword (`def`) in the Pi models.json build aborted `entrypoint.sh`** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC4 — `@test` added; no AC change). On `enterprise-integration` (and any enterprise tenant) containers would not start — diagnosed from Workers logs showing a terminal-WebSocket reconnect storm (~12/min), "Error proxying request to container", and teardown "Final sync did NOT complete… The container is not running", i.e. PID 1 exiting. The container base image is `node:24-bookworm-slim` → Debian bookworm → **jq 1.6**, and `entrypoint.sh`'s enterprise Pi models.json build used `jq -c --arg def "$ENTERPRISE_DEFAULT_ROUTE" '… [$def] …'`. `def` is a **reserved jq keyword** (function definition), so `$def` is a compile error; because the jq runs in an unguarded command-substitution under `set -euo pipefail`, the failure aborted the whole entrypoint → the container exited and crash-looped. It was enterprise-only because the block is gated on `ENTERPRISE_MODE=active` (plain integration on the identical image was healthy). Fix: rename the jq arg to `defroute`/`$defroute` (verified end-to-end against the live catalog `["general_usage","development","code_review","documentation"]`). The gap that let this ship: `container-env-llm.test.ts` covered the Worker fanning the route vars but nothing ran the entrypoint jq against a real `jq` binary. New `entrypoint-enterprise-pi-models.test.js` runs the real models.json build block (one model per route + empty-catalog fallback) and statically forbids any jq `--arg`/`--argjson` named after a reserved jq keyword. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 stays Planned (AC4's models.json build now has regression coverage; AC2/AC3/AC5/AC6 entrypoint behaviours remain untested).
- **Getting-started docs now self-heal on session start instead of being lost forever when the create-time seed fails** ([REQ-STOR-009](storage.md#req-stor-009-getting-started-docs-auto-seeded-on-first-session) AC6 added). New users got their agent-config preseed but no Docs & Examples until they manually clicked "Recreate Docs & Examples" — confirmed against 10 days of integration Workers logs showing hundreds of agent-config seed events and ZERO getting-started seed events. Root cause: getting-started docs were seeded only by the one-shot `bucketResult.created` gate in `ensureBucketAndSeed`/`browse.ts`, inside a try/catch that swallows failures with a warning, over the `overwrite:false` HEAD-precheck path on a freshly created bucket the code itself notes "is not always immediately writable on the S3 data plane." A single cold-bucket failure was swallowed and the create-only gate never re-fired, so docs stayed missing permanently. Agent configs survived only because they have OTHER reseed paths (the Recreate button, mode-change reconcile, the REQ-AGENT-049 preseed-hash upgrade) that getting-started docs lacked; the AC5 retry (added for this same incident class) only mitigated within a single attempt and was still swallowed by the caller. Fix: `ensureBucketAndSeed` now seeds getting-started docs whenever a new `gettingStartedSeeded` preference marker is unset (not gated on `created`), persisting the marker only after a successful idempotent (`overwrite:false`) seed — so a cold-bucket failure recovers on a later session, existing user edits are preserved, and once marked the user's deletions are respected. Mirrors the `lastPreseedHash` self-heal pattern. Tests: `container-lifecycle-helpers.test.ts` (self-heals on an un-marked existing bucket + sets marker; skips once marked; leaves marker unset on failure so it retries). **Status:** REQ-STOR-009 stays Implemented.
- **Dockerhub deploy backend-test step gained the `@cloudflare/vitest-pool-workers` teardown-crash guard** (no AC change; CI parity). `deploy-dockerhub.yml` ran a plain `npm test`, missing the exit-code guard that `deploy.yml` and `test.yml` both carry, so every Dockerhub deploy failed deterministically after all 2675 tests passed (one unhandled `Worker exited unexpectedly` pool-teardown error → exit 1). The identical guard (accept a non-zero exit ONLY when the pool-crash fingerprint is present, exactly one error, ≥1 test passed, nothing failed) is now in all three workflows. **Status:** no status change.
- **Pi session startup restored to pre-bundle speed: image-baked jiti transpile cache + pinned pi version** ([REQ-SESSION-015](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-015-container-port-readiness-gating-with-pre-warm-pre-condition) AC5 added). The 6-package preseed bundle made every fresh container cold-transpile the Pi extension graph through jiti before Pi's first PTY output — measured live at ~9s cold vs ~4s warm — which pushed the host pre-warm past its 20s hard cap and doubled perceived session startup (15s → 30-35s). jiti caches transpiles under `$TMPDIR/jiti` (its path-valued `JITI_FS_CACHE` env is ignored by this build — verified empirically) and the cache is content-addressed (source hash), so: a new Dockerfile layer runs a throwaway `pi -p` at image build with `TMPDIR` redirected (agent dir mirroring the runtime layout, package list DERIVED from the preseed `package.json`), bakes the result at `/opt/codeflare/jiti-cache`, and **fails the build if the cache comes out empty**; the entrypoint symlinks `/tmp/jiti` → the baked cache at boot (same pattern as the npm preseed symlink). Baked entries hit at runtime despite the R2-seeded extensions' different path/mtimes because seeding is verbatim (verified). All coding agents — pi included — stay `@latest` per user policy (auto-update at every deploy); the bake is self-consistent under `@latest` because the warm run executes with the pi installed in the same build. Validated end-to-end locally: 153/153 cache hits, 3.8s extension load via the symlinked baked cache. Tests: `dockerfile-pi-warm.test.js` (warm layer + TMPDIR redirect + derived package list + empty-cache build guard + entrypoint symlink). **Status:** REQ-SESSION-015 stays Implemented.
- **`collectMetrics` now warns when the container reports an unhealthy R2 sync** (observability hardening from the data-loss forensics; no AC change — supports [REQ-SESSION-004](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-004-idle-timeout-extension)). The 2026-05-31 integration bisync death ran invisible for 11 days because the sync daemon's state never left the container. `collectMetrics` (60s tick) now emits `collectMetrics: container R2 sync unhealthy` with the `syncStatus` whenever `/health` reports `failed`/`timeout` — cheap, continuously queryable in Workers logs, and alertable. Tests: `container-metrics.test.ts` (warns on failed, silent on success). **Status:** no status change.

- **The final-sync drain 401'd at the in-container auth gate on EVERY stop/delete — the true proximate cause of bisync-on-delete data loss; both drains now authenticate** ([REQ-SESSION-011](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-011-graceful-shutdown-with-final-sync) AC8 added). Live-incident forensics on integration (full Workers Observability history + R2 listings) proved every teardown drain died in ~51-300ms with HTTP 401 — zero successful teardown final syncs recorded in ≥30 days, before AND after the budget-inversion fix (which was real but **unreachable behind the 401**; the budget-inversion entry below stands corrected on incident causality).
