Mechanism: both `drainFinalSyncAudited` (delete) and `drainFinalSync` (idle/quota-stop) used a bare `port.fetch('http://localhost/internal/final-sync')`; the raw TCP-port fetch bypasses the DO's public fetch override — the only auth-header injection point (the documented reason `/health`+`/activity` are auth-exempt in `host/src/auth-check.ts`; `/internal/final-sync` is not) — so `checkContainerAuth` rejected the drain before the handler ran. On delete, `destroy()` additionally wiped `containerAuthToken` (storage + memory) BEFORE the drain fired (REQ-SESSION-009 ordering). The storage-panel "Sync R2" button always worked because it routes through the worker's authenticated container fetch — the user-supplied contrast that pointed at the gate. Fix: `destroy()` captures the token pre-clear (alongside the audit session id, with a storage fallback for an unhydrated DO) and the drain sends `Authorization: Bearer`; the idle/quota-stop drain reads the still-intact token from DO storage and does the same; headerless best-effort is kept when no token exists. Tests: `index.test.ts` (drain carries the pre-clear-captured Bearer token while `containerAuthToken` is already deleted — the capture-ordering regression), new `container-metrics-drain.test.ts` (idle-stop drain sends stored token; headerless when absent). See AD57 second revision (2026-06-10, later). **Status:** REQ-SESSION-011 stays Implemented.
- **Footer `repo:branch` now resolves the user's WORKING repo when the session cwd is a non-repo parent workspace** ([REQ-AGENT-056](agents.md#req-agent-056-pi-local-statusline-footer) AC2 revised). Diagnosed in-product by Pi (gpt-5.5): with the session cwd at `/home/user/workspace` (not a git repo) and all work done in a nested repo via `git -C ai-news-digest …`, `repositoryLabel`'s chain (session-cwd git root → ctx-cwd git root → remembered review repo) missed entirely — no review had run, so the footer dropped the `repo:branch` segment even though `codeflare-pi.ts` was simultaneously tracking the correct repo in the graphify active-cwd sentinel. Two-layer fix, display-only by design: (1) a shared in-session `rememberActiveRepo`/`recallActiveRepo` pair in `review-job-helpers.ts` — `codeflare-pi.ts::updateActiveRepoFromPath` (the single sentinel write chokepoint, fed by `git -C`/`cd <repo> &&`/clone detection) now also remembers the git root in module state the footer recalls; (2) the on-disk sentinel itself as the LAST fallback, but only through the new pure `activeRepoSentinelForDisplay` guard — value must be a git repo AND live inside a session root (session cwd / ctx cwd) — because the sentinel is written by both Claude's hook and Pi under concurrent agents and flaps to whichever acted last (the documented reason review routing abandoned it on 2026-06-10; that decision stands — `resolveReviewRepo` and all review routing remain sentinel-free, these fallbacks are footer-display only). The footer's live review row gains the same tail fallbacks (after `recallReviewRepo`, which stays preferred there) so a pending review in a nested repo renders after `/reload`. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (active-repo remember/recall + separate-slot-from-review-repo; sentinel guard accept/reject including the path-boundary `workspace-other` case). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-056 stays Implemented.

- **Final-sync host endpoint timeout was inverted *below* the DO drain budget — the real root cause of bisync-on-delete data loss (survived ~10 fixes)** ([REQ-SESSION-011](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-011-graceful-shutdown-with-final-sync) AC1 + new host>DO constraint). The in-container `/internal/final-sync` endpoint capped its poll loop at `INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 115_000` — *below* the DO's 120s drain budget (`AbortSignal.timeout(120s)` in `container-lifecycle.ts::destroy`). Every final bisync landing in the 115–120s band (the long-idle sessions AD56's 15-min cadence produces) had the host return 504 first → `drainFinalSyncAudited` mapped it to `incomplete` → the session deleted with unsynced edits. A regression test (`final-sync-endpoint.test.js`) even asserted the inversion (`< 120_000`) as an invariant, so any correct fix failed CI — a large part of why this persisted. Fix: host timeout raised strictly ABOVE the DO budget (`125_000`) so the DO's `AbortSignal` is the sole authoritative ceiling; the guard test now asserts host `> 120_000`; `finalSyncAudit` additionally records HTTP status + reason + session id (captured before the storage-clear nulls `_sessionId`) for post-mortem correlation. A genuinely >135s sync still deletes (data loss accepted past the hard cap per product decision) but is now audited, not silent. The suspected rclone state-wedge was ruled out — locks/listings live in `~/.cache`, ephemeral per container AND excluded from R2 sync (`--filter "- .cache/**"`) — so no `entrypoint.sh` change was warranted. Tests: `final-sync-endpoint.test.js` (host `> 120_000` guard), `index.test.ts` (a final-sync 504 audited as `incomplete` with session id + status/reason; delete still proceeds). See [AD57](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad57-135-second-shutdown-budget-for-final-bisync) Revision (2026-06-10). **Status:** REQ-SESSION-011 stays Implemented.
- **Trivy deploy gate now fails only on fixable CVEs (`ignore-unfixed: true`)** ([REQ-SEC-011](security.md#req-sec-011-container-image-scanned-for-cves-before-deploy) AC3 reworded; `@impl` adds `deploy-dockerhub.yml`). After #518 suppressed an unfixed perl CVE (CVE-2026-48959), the very next production deploy failed on a *different* unfixed Debian base-image CVE — openssl `PKCS7_verify` heap UAF (CVE-2026-45447) — two unfixable base-image CVEs breaking production within hours, because the gate failed on any unsuppressed HIGH/CRITICAL regardless of whether a fix existed. Both deploy Trivy steps (`deploy.yml`, `deploy-dockerhub.yml`) now run with `ignore-unfixed: true`, so the gate fails only on HIGH/CRITICAL CVEs that have an available fix and are unsuppressed; unfixed CVEs (blank Fixed Version) are excluded automatically. `.trivyignore` is now reserved for fixable-but-deferred CVEs (e.g. fixed upstream but a vendored CLI hasn't rebuilt); pre-existing unfixed entries are kept as a documented record. Tests: `workflow-files.test.js` (both deploy workflows assert `severity: HIGH,CRITICAL` + `exit-code: 1` + `ignore-unfixed: true`). **Status:** REQ-SEC-011 stays Implemented.
- **Review-repo resolution detached from the shared graphify active-cwd sentinel (footer + finalize fix for nested/concurrent repos)** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC5). The footer progress row, the idle reaper, and the on-turn finalizers all resolved the review repo via `activeRepoFallback()` reading `/home/user/.cache/codeflare-hooks/graphify-active-cwd` — a single-active-repo sentinel written by BOTH Claude's `graphify-active-repo.sh` hook AND Pi's `codeflare-pi.ts` (proactively, per tool execution). Under concurrent agents in different repos (e.g. Claude in the outer codeflare repo, Pi reviewing a nested clone) it flaps to whichever agent acted last, so Pi's review code read the wrong `.git`: no progress footer, and the reaper/finalizer `loadPending` the wrong repo so the summary never emits and autofix never starts. New pure `resolveReviewRepo` resolves from the boundary-command cwd / Pi session cwd, with an in-session `sessionReviewRepo` remembered for the no-ctx reaper; `review-enforcement.ts` (all 8 resolution sites), `local-statusline.ts` (footer row + label), and `review-command.ts` no longer read the sentinel. Graphify's own single-active-repo model is left unchanged (deliberate design; its concurrency fragility is a separate, lower-severity concern). Mirrored to `~/.pi`. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`resolveReviewRepo` precedence; never probes the sentinel path). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented — but note the nested-repo footer `repo:branch` and the on-turn summary emit were only PARTIALLY wired here (`reviewRepoForCtx` did not yet thread `sessionReviewRepo`); they were completed in the `rememberReviewRepo`/`recallReviewRepo` follow-up entry below.
- **Pi PR-boundary review OFFERS on a fresh launch again (bug-A regression fix)** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 mechanism revised). The 2026-06-09 offer-once work derived `inSessionContinuation` from the on-disk ack (`isAncestor(lastAck, head)`), which is true on every fresh `pi` launch whose head descends from a prior ack — so reconciliation auto-started reviewers on launch instead of offering (user-reported: "offering worked yesterday you broke something today"; proven by `codeflare-review-events.jsonl` showing `trigger:"open-PR reconciliation (in-session continuation)"` at session start). Continuation is now decided from an **in-memory per-session baseline** (`reviewSessionBaselineHead`, the head first observed this session): the new pure helper `reviewBaselineContinuation(baseline, head, isAncestor)` returns true only when the head ADVANCED beyond the baseline (a genuine in-session push whose on-tool-end auto-start was dropped); a head present at launch (baseline unset or unchanged) offers. Process-scoped so a bare relaunch always re-baselines and offers. Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`reviewBaselineContinuation`: bare launch offers, only an in-session advance autostarts). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Implemented.
- **`gh pr edit --base main|master` now arms PR-boundary review across all enforcement surfaces** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC3; [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pr-boundary-review-idle-durable-reaper) AC3/AC4 split). A PR opened against a non-protected base (or via the web UI) and later retargeted onto `main`/`master` with `gh pr edit --base` is the same boundary `gh pr create --base main` establishes, applied after creation — previously it armed no review until the durable reconciliation catch-up. The Pi extension (`prBoundaryCommandBase = prCreateBoundaryBase || prEditBoundaryBase`, `isBoundaryWords` recognizing `gh pr edit` with a protected `--base`) and both Claude hooks (`enforce-review-spawn.sh` awk across Bash/`ctx_execute`/`ctx_batch_execute`; `git-push-review-reminder.sh` `pr-retarget` trigger taking the base from the command itself, not a stale `gh view`) now detect it; metadata-only `gh pr edit` (title/body/labels) and non-protected `--base develop` remain ignored. REQ-AGENT-061 AC3 split so off-turn finalization's "summary deferred, marker left unclaimed for the on-turn emit" is its own AC4. Tests: `review-trigger.test.ts` (`prBoundaryCommandBase`), `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (`isPrBoundaryCommand`/`cwdFromBoundaryCommand` for `gh pr edit`), `enforce-review-spawn.test.js` + `git-push-review-reminder.test.js` (real-hook block/directive across `--base`/`--base=`/`-B` forms). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-061 stays Planned.
- **Reloaded enterprise config falls back to the first route as default** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-012](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-012-setup-configured-dynamic-route-catalog-and-access-group-list) AC6/AC7 split). On a setup re-run, `loadExistingConfig` left `defaultRouteName` empty when no default was stored, so a configured-but-default-less enterprise tenant reloaded with no default selected; it now resolves to `dynamicRoutes[0]` (reasoning off), matching the first-route-is-default rule. REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 AC6 split so the "Continue blocked until ≥1 route" UI gate (AC6) and the "`POST /api/setup/configure` rejects empty `dynamicRoutes` with 400" backend gate (AC7) are separate; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-006](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-006-deploy-time-aig-secrets-and-enterprise_mode-var) AC7 added for the `enterprise`/`enterprise integration` deploy targets. Tests: `stores/setup.test.ts` (reload with `defaultRoute:null` → first route serialized as default). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 stays Implemented; REQ-ENTERPRISE-006 stays Planned.
- **context-mode is now ENABLED by default for Pi, and four tool extensions are preseeded so they work with and without `/ctx`** ([REQ-AGENT-005](agents.md#req-agent-005-pro-mode-includes-additional-skills-rules-agents-and-mcp-servers) AC4/AC5 revised, AC8 added). context-mode was carried as a *disabled* package spec in the Pi settings assembly — a fresh Pi session had no `ctx_*` tools until the user ran `/ctx on`. It is moved from `disabledPackages` into the settings `required` array (bare `npm:context-mode@1.0.162` string), so it loads enabled on every container start; `/ctx off` disables it for the running session and the next start re-enables. Four extensions are added to `preseed/agents/pi/package.json` (exact pins) and the same `required` array — `@juicesharp/rpiv-ask-user-question@1.19.1`, `@juicesharp/rpiv-todo@1.19.1`, `pi-web-access@0.10.7`, `pi-mcp-adapter@2.9.0` — so they are enabled INDEPENDENTLY of the `/ctx` toggle (the user requirement: MCP tools must work within ctx-mode ON, and the rpiv/web/mcp tools must never disappear when ctx-mode toggles). The entrypoint's idempotent Pi `settings.json` merge (keyed by version-stripped identity, `required` written last) guarantees a previously-disabled context-mode upgrades to enabled, the four extensions are present regardless of prior state, and user-added packages are preserved with no duplication. One concise `SKILL.md` per extension (registered in `manifest.json`) tells the agent which tool to reach for: rpiv-ask-user-question for a genuine user decision, rpiv-todo for multi-step tracking, pi-web-access + a unified web-fetch decision tree, pi-mcp-adapter for configured MCP servers. Tests: `host/__tests__/pi-settings-packages.test.js` runs the REAL entrypoint assembly heredoc against fixtures (all six required present, context-mode enabled bare-string, prior-disabled context-mode upgraded + unrelated package preserved, idempotent/dedup), `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (four new skills in the generated seed). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-005 stays Implemented.
- **Pi review footer regained `repo:branch`, gained a timer + per-lane token badge, and the completed-review summary now reaches the main session for nested repos** ([REQ-AGENT-053](agents.md#req-agent-053-pi-durable-review-status-and-result-formatting) AC2 revised; [REQ-AGENT-056](agents.md#req-agent-056-pi-local-statusline-footer) AC2; [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC5 completed). The 2026-06-10 resolveReviewRepo work (entry above) added a `sessionReviewRepo` precedence input but `reviewRepoForCtx` never actually passed it, so on a nested review repo the footer dropped the `repo:branch` segment and the on-turn finalizer's summary emit resolved the wrong repo and never reached the main session. A shared `rememberReviewRepo`/`recallReviewRepo` module pair now records the resolved repo on every resolution and feeds it back through `reviewRepoForCtx`, the reaper, and `local-statusline.ts` (footer label + live review row), so all three converge on the same repo. The compact footer (`compactDurableReviewStatus`) now renders a leading elapsed badge (`Review 1:18 · code | spec | docs`, `M:SS` from the earliest lane start via `formatReviewElapsed`) and a best-effort per-lane token count parsed from the lane transcript (`laneTokensFromTranscript`, cached per transcript path, `formatReviewTokens` → `950`/`2.1k`/`124k`); both degrade gracefully (badge/token omitted when their inputs are absent — the timer is reliable, tokens are best-effort since the transcript usage field is not guaranteed). Mirrored conceptually into preseed only (no `~/.pi` edit). Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`rememberReviewRepo`/`recallReviewRepo` round-trip; elapsed/token formatting; badge rendering + omission). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-053 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-056 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented (AC5 nested-repo emit now actually wired).
- **browser-run skill sharpened into an explicit web-fetch decision tree (last-resort framing)** ([REQ-BROWSER-003](browser-run.md#req-browser-003-pi-native-browser-run-wrapper) AC clarified). The vague "if WebFetch fails, fall back" guidance in both the Pi and Claude `browser-run/SKILL.md` is replaced with a single ordered decision tree — `web_search`/`fetch_content` (pi-web-access) → `ctx_fetch_and_index` (static HTML→markdown, indexed, cheap, when context-mode on) → `curl` (raw HTTP, no JS) → `browser-run` (JS-rendered/interactive, remote headless Chrome, quota/cost) — so the agent reserves the expensive remote browser for genuinely JS-rendered or interactive pages. The same tree is shared by the new `pi-web-access/SKILL.md`. browser-run's Quotas/Cost and advanced-mode + `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`ACCOUNT_ID` gating notes are kept. Spec/skill text only — no behavior change. **Status:** REQ-BROWSER-003 stays Implemented.

## 2026-06-09

- **Enterprise dynamic routes are now required (≥1), the first route added is the default, and the group/route chips get the accent border** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-012](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-012-setup-configured-dynamic-route-catalog-and-access-group-list) AC2 revised + AC6 added). Acceptance testing on the live integration tenant surfaced two issues: (1) the access-group and dynamic-route chips rendered without the blue accent border the admin chips have — the accent CSS lived in a modifier (`email-tag--admin`) applied only to admin chips; (2) the "Default Route" selector offered a misleading "(no default)" option, implying a request could reach no destination, even though the interceptor and container already resolve an unset default to the first catalog route. Fix: the accent modifier is generalized to `email-tag--accent` and applied to the admin, access-group, and dynamic-route chips (non-enterprise regular-user chips stay plain to preserve the admin distinction); the wizard now requires ≥1 dynamic route in enterprise mode (`ConfigureStep` blocks Continue; `POST /api/setup/configure` rejects empty/absent `dynamicRoutes` with `400` before any KV write) and the store auto-assigns the first route added as the default (re-points to the new first route when the default is removed), dropping the "(no default)" option so routing always resolves to a gateway route. The interceptor's empty-catalog passthrough is retained as a defensive fallback, no longer a reachable enterprise configuration. Tests: `setup.test.ts` (enterprise empty-routes → `400`, no partial KV write), `stores/setup.test.ts` (first-route auto-default + remove-reassign + first route serialized as the default), `ConfigureStep.test.tsx` (Continue gate + route select offers no empty option). A gating-hardening pass (per acceptance-test feedback that every non-review change stay behind enterprise mode) confirmed no non-enterprise leak across the epic: the `/prefill` enterprise extras are now gated on `isEnterpriseMode` so a non-enterprise response is byte-identical (`handlers.test.ts` non-enterprise omission, AC5), the container-router `defaultRoute`/`defaultReasoning` writes are nested under catalog presence so they travel as a unit with the catalog (no stray empty-string write without a catalog), and removing the default route resets its reasoning grade to off. **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 stays Implemented (UI gate + backend `400` + store auto-default + non-enterprise prefill omission unit-tested).
- **Enterprise multi-group metadata: all matched Access groups stamped as per-group tags, scalar `group` dropped** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway) AC4). The single-group design from 2026-06-07 (one `cf-aig-metadata.group` value) is replaced: `resolveUserAccessGroup`/`resolveSessionAccessGroup` now return **all** matched configured groups (`string[]`, the `matched[0]` collapse dropped), the DO handoff is `userGroup:string → userGroups:string[]` (legacy single-string reads coerced to a one-element list; value-equality restart compare), and the interceptor stamps **one `group_<sanitized>=1` tag per group plus `user`**, dropping the scalar `group` key entirely (clean redeploy, no back-compat). Per-group KEYS — not a CSV — because the AI Gateway filter operators are equals/not-equals only (verified against CF docs), so each `group_*` key is independently equals-filterable to build if/else conditions in Dynamic Routes. CF caps custom metadata at **5 entries/request** (extras silently dropped), so the budget is `user` + 4 groups; a user matching more groups is truncated DETERMINISTICALLY in configured order with a `console.warn` naming the dropped groups (never silent). `sanitizeGroupKey` lowercases, replaces non-alphanumerics, and appends a djb2 hash suffix so distinct names never collide on a sanitized key. Tests: `llm-interceptor.test.ts` (per-group tags / scalar dropped / empty-groups / deterministic 4-tag truncation + warn), `access-group-resolution.test.ts` (`resolveUserAccessGroup` returns all matches in order, drops unconfigured memberships, fail-closed `[]`). SaaS path byte-identical (interceptor never instantiated). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-004 stays Implemented.
- **Enterprise dynamic routes are configured in Setup (unlimited, no redeploy) and the static `AIG_LANGUAGE_MODEL` route-pin is removed** (new [REQ-ENTERPRISE-012](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-012-setup-configured-dynamic-route-catalog-and-access-group-list); [REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC1/AC3/AC4; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-007](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-007-gateway-route-pinning) rewritten; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-006](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-006-deploy-time-aig-secrets-and-enterprise_mode-var) AC2). The single Worker var `AIG_LANGUAGE_MODEL` (and its `deploy.yml` plumbing) is **removed**; route selection moves into the setup wizard, which persists an unlimited route catalog (`SETUP_KEYS.DYNAMIC_ROUTES`, JSON `string[]`) plus one optional default `route:reasoning` (`SETUP_KEYS.DEFAULT_ROUTE`, JSON `{route,reasoning}`; unset ⇒ first catalog route, reasoning off). The interceptor maps the agent-sent slash-free handle → `dynamic/<name>` from the catalog (`loadRouteCatalog`), failing safe to the resolved default on an unknown handle and forwarding verbatim when the catalog is empty — replacing the static `model`-rewrite of REQ-ENTERPRISE-007. The catalog + default + reasoning grade are fanned to the container (`ENTERPRISE_ROUTE_CATALOG` / `ENTERPRISE_DEFAULT_ROUTE` / `ENTERPRISE_DEFAULT_REASONING`) so `entrypoint.sh` builds Pi's `models.json` listing every route and pins `defaultThinkingLevel` from the default — amending REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 AC1's prior "exactly one enterprise var" invariant (still no gateway URL/token/account-id/secret reaches the container). Agents start at the configured default; a user `/model` change is not persisted (re-asserted each start). Tests: `llm-interceptor.test.ts` (Feature C catalog mapping: known handle → `dynamic/<name>`, unknown → default, empty-catalog passthrough, non-routable-path skip), `enterprise-route-config.test.ts` (the `loadEnterpriseRouteConfig` resolver: catalog parse, default-in-catalog, fallback-drops-reasoning, unset→first/off, malformed-degrades, non-enterprise-empty), `container-env-llm.test.ts` (route vars fanned when enterprise+present, omitted otherwise, `COPILOT_MODEL`/`PI_MODEL` still never fanned), `setup.test.ts` + `handlers.test.ts` (catalog/default persistence, `defaultRoute.route` must be in catalog, malformed-JSON prefill degrades). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 added as **Implemented** (Setup persistence + prefill + the `loadEnterpriseRouteConfig` resolver + interceptor mapping + container-env fan are all unit-tested); REQ-ENTERPRISE-007 stays Implemented (rewritten to catalog mapping, same test file); REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 stays Planned (AC2/AC3/AC4 are `entrypoint.sh` behaviours with no automated test).
- **Setup wizard manages access groups and dynamic routes as add/Enter/chip-with-x lists** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-012](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-012-setup-configured-dynamic-route-catalog-and-access-group-list) AC1/AC2; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC7). The enterprise access-group field (previously a comma textarea) and the new dynamic-route catalog are both edited with the existing admin add/Enter/chip-with-x interaction (`ConfigureStep.tsx` + `stores/setup.ts`), batch-saved through the existing `POST /api/setup/configure` (no new endpoint). Group/route names validate `1–256` chars, trimmed, comma+newline FORBIDDEN (storage stays comma/newline-joined and split by `parseAccessGroups`), so a name with spaces (e.g. `Agentic AI Test Account`) is allowed. Tests: `web-ui/.../stores/setup.test.ts` (add/remove/dedup), `ConfigureStep.test.tsx` (chip render + validation). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-012 Implemented (UI + store + wire-schema tested).
- **Enterprise vault service-worker reaches the Worker behind Cloudflare Access (bypass app auto-provisioned)** (new [REQ-ENTERPRISE-006](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-006-deploy-time-aig-secrets-and-enterprise_mode-var) AC6; enables [REQ-VAULT-017](vault.md#req-vault-017-silverbullet-native-service-worker) under enterprise Access). Root cause (confirmed live: `curl` → 302 to `*.cloudflareaccess.com`): in Enterprise Mode the host-wide Access app 302s the credential-less `service_worker.js` registration fetch to the IdP login BEFORE the Worker's REQ-VAULT-017 short-circuit can run, so SilverBullet never registers its native worker. Fix: the setup wizard auto-provisions a higher-precedence Access app + `decision:'bypass'` (include everyone) policy scoped to `/api/vault/*/service_worker.js`, so that one request reaches the Worker (the SW bytes are non-sensitive; the per-session key arrives later via postMessage). Provisioning is **best-effort**: a failure never aborts the (already-succeeded) host-wide Access setup, the app id (`SETUP_KEYS.ACCESS_SW_BYPASS_APP_ID`) is persisted only after the bypass policy succeeds, and a freshly-created app is rolled back if the policy step fails (a policy-less self-hosted app would deny the path — worse than the 302). Tests: `access.test.ts` (enterprise provisions the bypass app with decision `bypass` + include everyone; default/SaaS does not). **Status:** REQ-ENTERPRISE-006 stays Planned (the new AC6 bypass-app provisioning is tested, but AC1/AC4 transport scopes remain untested).
- **Session delete no longer loses unsynced vault edits when `running` reads transiently false (#516)** ([REQ-SESSION-011](session-lifecycle.md#req-session-011-graceful-shutdown-with-final-sync) AC1/AC6). The destroy path gated the final R2 drain on `ctx.container?.running`; on a delete where the platform reported `running:false` transiently, the drain was skipped and the bisync of unsynced edits was lost (disproved the #494 "delete drains identically to stop" claim — confirmed live). `container-lifecycle.ts::destroy` now hoists the teardown-clock vars out of the `if (running)` block and **always** runs the final-sync drain (the running gate is narrowed to the stop+poll phase only), and records a durable `finalSyncAudit` outcome (`{outcome, at, running}`) under DO storage instead of silently swallowing the drain result. Tests: `index.test.ts` (`#516` describe: drain attempted despite `running:false`; outcome `completed`/`errored` persisted; destroy still completes when the drain rejects). **Status:** REQ-SESSION-011 stays Implemented.
- **Pi PR-boundary review on a fresh clone OFFERS instead of auto-spawning** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 revised; AC4 now unit-tested). Cloning a repo with an open enforced PR made `reconcileOpenPrReview` auto-spawn a review immediately, with no way to stop it (a kill auto-retried) — user-reported on `ai-news-digest`. The missed-boundary reconciliation path now calls the new pure `reconcileBoundaryAction` (offer-once): instead of `ensureReviewWindow`, it `ctx.ui.notify`s "run `/review-run` or `/review-skip`" exactly once per head (an `offered` marker mirrors the `ack` marker so the 20s reaper never re-fires), leaving the merge gate blocked (head stays unacked) until the user chooses. New `/review-run` (spawns the window) and `/review-skip` (acks the head) commands; in-session push boundaries still auto-start, and the merge-time block is unchanged. Pi extensions have no interactive-prompt API (notify + commands only). Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`reconcileBoundaryAction` offer-once; and AC4 — every suppressed `shouldReconcileOpenPr` gate names a distinct non-empty reason, the value stamped into `boundary_candidate_ignored`). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 promoted Partial → **Implemented** — every AC's decision core is now unit-tested (AC1 reconcile/offer, AC3 `enforcedHeadDecision`, AC4 gate-reason, AC5 `prUrlFromText`, AC6 gating); the thin `appendReviewEvent` / `ctx.ui.notify` runtime wiring that acts on those decisions is integration glue per the repo's runtime-coverage convention.
- **PR-boundary review now runs all three lanes in parallel** ([REQ-AGENT-040](agents.md#req-agent-040-pr-boundary-lane-classification-and-agent-dispatch) AC4/AC5 revised; [AD78](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad78-pr-boundary-review-lanes-run-in-parallel-report-only-reviewers)). `code-reviewer`, `spec-reviewer`, and `doc-updater` now dispatch together at a PR-boundary instead of `spec-reviewer` → `doc-updater` sequentially. The reviewers are **report-only** — each writes findings to its own lane triage file (`spec-reviewer` → `sdd/spec/.review-queue.md`, `doc-updater` → `documentation/.doc-coverage.md`) and the **main session** applies every fix — so their write targets are disjoint and there is no shared-write race or ordering dependency. The prior spec→doc gate existed only for the superseded auto-fix model, where `spec-reviewer` edited `sdd/` in place and `doc-updater` validated REQ cross-references against the just-moved REQs. Pi: `durableReviewInitialLanes` returns all lanes and `durableReviewEligibleLanes` drops the doc-waits-for-spec gate; the spec-completion→doc-spawn trigger in `review-enforcement.ts` is removed (it would double-spawn). Claude: `enforce-review-spawn.sh` demands all three in the parallel MISSING block and acks the head on `all_required_lanes_completed_for_current_head` (the per-lane PIPELINE_COMPLETE sequencing is gone); `git-push-review-reminder.sh` emits a parallel directive. Skills/rules updated (`git-review-pipeline`, `spec-driven-development`, `spec-discipline`). `/sdd clean` is unchanged — it *applies* fixes inline and stays sequential (doc cross-references depend on the just-fixed spec). Tests: `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (all-lane initial set + parallel eligibility, no spec→doc gate), `enforce-review-spawn.test.js` + `git-push-review-reminder.test.js` (parallel demand + directive). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-040 stays Implemented.
- **Missed in-session PR boundaries auto-start review again (catch-up distinguishes continuation from clone), `gh pr edit --base main` is a trigger, and an idle-finalized review summary is never lost** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1 revised; [REQ-AGENT-063](agents.md#req-agent-063-pr-boundary-command-parsing) AC3 extended; [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC3 revised). Three user-reported `ai-news-digest` misfires, two root causes. (1) **Missed boundary never reviewed:** the Point-6 catch-up (`reconcileOpenPrReview`) OFFERED for *every* missed boundary, so an in-session push whose `onToolEnd` auto-start was dropped (a compound `cd … && git push`, a here-doc, a `gh pr edit` retarget, or a reload) — exactly the cases the catch-up exists for — never auto-started, contradicting the locked "in-session push still auto-starts" design, and the offer never surfaced either. `reconcileBoundaryAction` now returns `autostart` when the unacked head is in-session continuation (it DESCENDS from a head already acked in this repo, computed via `lastAckHead` + `isAncestor`) and `offer` only for a fresh clone/checkout (no prior ack in `.git` to descend from), so a dropped tool event recovers into a real review while `git clone` still never auto-spawns an unstoppable one. Separately, `gh pr edit --base main|master` is now a boundary trigger (`prEditBoundaryBase` → `isPrBoundaryTrigger`), so retargeting an existing or web-UI PR onto `main` arms review immediately rather than waiting on the catch-up. (2) **Completed-review summary lost:** the idle reaper's `finalizeCompletedReview` runs off-turn (no ctx) and `publishReviewSummary` claimed the exclusive `summary-v3.sent` marker *before* emitting, but off-turn `pi.sendMessage` does not surface — so the review was acked, the marker blocked every retry, and the merged findings were never shown (`announced/summary-v3.sent` present, no `codeflare-review-summary-v3` message in the session). The no-ctx path now persists `summary.md` only and leaves the chat announcement UNCLAIMED; the next on-turn tick (`refreshReviewStatusFromDurable` → `publishSummaryForCurrentPr`) claims and emits it with a live ctx (when there are actionable findings the autofix turn-trigger surfaces it with no extra user input). Mirrored into `~/.pi/agent/extensions/`; agent seed regenerated. Tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`reconcileBoundaryAction` autostart-in-session-vs-offer-on-clone, no-op on re-offer / non-reconcilable), `review-trigger.test.ts` (`prEditBoundaryBase` retarget parsing + `isPrBoundaryTrigger` `gh pr edit` across `--base`/`--base=`/`-B`/compound forms, non-main and non-base-edit excluded). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-063 stays Implemented (AC3 covers the `gh pr edit --base` retarget trigger, unit-tested); REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented (the off-turn summary deferral is the same `setInterval`/`sendMessage` integration glue as AC1, documented coverage-gap).
- **PR-#517 review-round fixes** ([REQ-AGENT-040](agents.md#req-agent-040-pr-boundary-lane-classification-and-agent-dispatch) AC4/AC5; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls)). The PR-boundary code-reviewer flagged two carry-overs earlier epic commits missed. (1) `onAgentStart` still blocked a `doc-updater` agent-tool invocation until `spec-reviewer` completed — the superseded sequential gate, directly contradicting the now-parallel lanes ([AD78](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad78-pr-boundary-review-lanes-run-in-parallel-report-only-reviewers)) the parallel-lanes change otherwise removed — so it is deleted (with its orphaned `toolName`/`input` reads); the merge gate is unchanged. (2) the first-config DO-storage path (`container-router.ts`) used truthiness guards for `defaultRoute`/`defaultReasoning` while `applyPrefsOnRestart` uses `!== undefined` (the documented empty-reset contract), so an empty default (reasoning-off / first-route fallback) was silently not stored — aligned to `!== undefined`. Seed regenerated; mirrored to `~/.pi`. No AC behavior change (both align code to already-Implemented ACs). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-040 / REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 stay Implemented.

## 2026-06-08

- **Entrypoint migration removes the deprecated `@gaodes/pi-graphify` from existing Pi settings on boot** ([REQ-AGENT-023](agents.md#req-agent-023-knowledge-graph-capability-graphify)). The graphify rebuild replaced the third-party wrapper with the first-party `graphify-native.ts` and dropped `@gaodes` from `npm/package.json`, the entrypoint install list, and `manifest.json` — but the entrypoint's Pi settings-merge PRESERVES existing `settings.json` packages, so a deployment upgrading from the `@gaodes` era kept `npm:@gaodes/pi-graphify` in its settings and then loaded BOTH it and `graphify-native.ts` → `Tool "graphify_query" conflicts` → Pi refused to start (hit live this session on a fresh `pi` launch). Added a `removedPackageIds` set to the settings-merge (`entrypoint.sh`) that hard-drops `@gaodes/pi-graphify` from existing settings on every boot — dropped and never re-added, distinct from the disabled-package path that re-adds context-mode as a disabled spec — so upgrades self-heal. Settings removal alone is sufficient (Pi only loads packages listed in settings); the stale `node_modules/@gaodes` files are left untouched (harmless, and the dir may be a preseed symlink). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-023 stays Implemented.
- **Roll-forward and stale-discard now emit a `review_superseded` audit event** ([REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement), [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery)). When a new push advanced the PR head while a prior head's review was still in flight, `rollForwardAdvancedReview` abandoned the old window (and killed its lanes) for a fresh review at the new head; the durable event log (`.git/codeflare-review-events.jsonl`) then showed `lane_spawned <oldhead>` followed by nothing, so a deliberate supersede was indistinguishable from a crash (observed live on the `7de81d3`→`4f29529` roll-forward). Both supersede paths (`rollForwardAdvancedReview` and `discardStale`) now `appendReviewEvent({event:"review_superseded", head:<oldHead>, reason, lanes})`, so the audit trail explains every abandoned window — preserving the "a surprising review is one `cat events.jsonl` away" guarantee. Diagnostic-only; no behavior change beyond the emitted event. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-055/058 unchanged (REQ-058 stays Partial).
- **Pi durable review now finalizes fully on an idle session — the autonomous timer emits the merged summary into the session and starts the autofix, not just a disk ack** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC3). The detached-lane reaper timer only ack'd + persisted a `summary.md` to disk when an idle session's lanes all finished — it could not emit the merged summary into the Pi conversation or start the autofix, because both need a live `pi`/`ctx` and the module-level `setInterval` has neither. So an idle completed review still required the user to submit a prompt before any results appeared or fixing began (two user-reported defects: results never shown, Pi never resumed). Fix: the default export binds a module-level `activeReviewFinalize` hook to a `pi`-aware finalize closure; on all-lanes-complete the timer calls it → `finalizeCompletedReview` (made `ctx`-optional) runs the existing claim-guarded `publishReviewSummary` (`pi.sendMessage({display:true})`) and `requestReviewAutofix` (`pi.sendMessage({triggerTurn:true})`), so the summary is emitted and the autofix turn starts with zero user input (the user cancels with ESC). The `ctx`-only paths degrade safely: the summary-emit fallback notify is skipped, the autofix manual-mode suppression defaults off (ESC-to-cancel replaces it), and the statusline clear is already try/caught. Dedup markers (`claimReviewAnnouncement` `summary-v3` + the `autofix.requested` file) mean a later real turn never double-emits or double-fires. Pi-agent-only; no Worker runtime path changes. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented (the idle-finalization wiring is an integration path verified live in Pi; the decision/parse/recovery core stays unit-tested, with the documented `setInterval`/OS-spawn coverage-gaps).
- **PR-boundary review follow-up fixes for detached lanes + native graphify** ([REQ-AGENT-023](agents.md#req-agent-023-knowledge-graph-capability-graphify) Constraints; [REQ-AGENT-059](agents.md#req-agent-059-pi-durable-review-fix-loop) AC1/AC2; [REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC3; [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1; [AD76](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad76-durable-review-lanes-run-as-detached-headless-pi-processes)). Restored lifecycle missed-boundary reconciliation on session/turn/resource/agent-end ticks while keeping the pushed-head gate, changed the no-ctx timer to ack + clear + persist a merged summary once every exact-head lane result exists, blocked prohibited local builds/tests inside detached review lanes with a tiny `review-lane-guards.ts` extension, and made `graphify-native.ts` ignore a different process cwd repo when the live session cwd resolves to another repo. REQ-023 Constraints are compressed below the section budget; REQ-AGENT-059 AC1/AC2 are trimmed to one pass/fail behaviour each; AD64 is superseded by AD76; AD75 now documents cwd-first graph resolution and detached-lane `-e` loading. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-023/059/060/061 stay Implemented; REQ-AGENT-058 stays Partial.
- **Spec-enforce conciseness pass on the review/graphify REQs + a "fix findings regardless of age" rule for Pi** ([REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC6, [REQ-AGENT-040](agents.md#req-agent-040-pr-boundary-lane-classification-and-agent-dispatch) AC2/AC8, [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC1, [REQ-AGENT-023](agents.md#req-agent-023-knowledge-graph-capability-graphify) AC1/AC2/AC4/AC5 + Constraints; [AD75](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad75-pi-graphify-tools-replaced-by-a-first-party-native-extension)). Trimmed every over-cap AC and Constraint in the PR-touched REQs: REQ-040 folds its 8th AC (generated-artifact lane mapping, 78 words) into AC2 and returns to 7 ACs (the `-> AC8` test labels move to `-> AC2`); REQ-036 AC6, REQ-058 AC1, and REQ-023 AC1/AC2/AC4/AC5/AC6 are trimmed to ≤45 words each; REQ-023's graph-resolution Constraint is rewritten to the cwd-first precedence (matching the `resolveGraph` fix above — it had gone stale claiming the sentinel wins), and the update-wrapper / `/dev/shm` / optional-extras Constraints are split or compressed to one terse single-sentence boundary each; AD75's Context gains a `graphify-native.ts` source anchor. Spec/ADR text only — no behavior change. Separately, Pi now carries the same rule the user set for the assistant — **a finding's age is never a reason to skip it: fix every legitimate finding, never ask whether to fix a pre-existing / out-of-scope one** — added to the PR-boundary autofix request (`reviewAutofixRequest`) and the `git-review-pipeline` skill (and, for Claude, to `~/.claude/rules/review-findings.md`). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-023/036/040 stay Implemented; REQ-AGENT-058 stays Partial.
- **Three review/graphify HIGH findings from the in-session review fixed** ([REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery) AC3 corrected; [REQ-AGENT-023](agents.md#req-agent-023-knowledge-graph-capability-graphify)). The live PR #505 reviewers (running through the new state machine) surfaced three HIGHs against the review/graphify extensions. (1) **`resolveEnforcedHead` armed reviews for unpushed local commits** — it preferred local HEAD whenever the current branch matched the PR branch and local descended from GitHub's reported head, which also matches ordinary unpushed WIP, so passive reconciliation could start a PR-boundary review for a commit the PR never had. Fixed with a *pushed* gate: local is enforced only when the remote-tracking ref `origin/<headRefName>` actually contains it (git push updates that ref locally, so the develop→main metadata-lag tolerance is preserved while unpushed WIP falls back to the reported PR head). The decision is extracted to the pure `enforcedHeadDecision` (`review-helpers.ts`) and behaviorally unit-tested (pushed-vs-unpushed table) in `review-trigger.test.ts`, so REQ-058 AC3 now has direct coverage (its prior `@test: none` note is removed; REQ-058 stays Partial only on AC4's untested audit-event emission). AC3's "transient `gh` read failure preserves the pending window" clause is dropped as redundant — already covered by [REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement) AC2. (2) **graphify `resolveGraph` could query the wrong graph** — it consulted only the advanced-mode-only active-repo sentinel then the global graph, so in default-mode sessions and review lanes (sentinel absent or stale) `graphify_query` ignored the current repo's `graphify-out/graph.json`. Fixed by resolving the cwd repo graph FIRST (then sentinel, then global); the precedence is extracted to the pure `pickGraphSource` and behaviorally tested in the new `graphify-native.test.ts`. (3) **a text-matching test masqueraded as behavioral** — `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts`'s missed-boundary-recovery test only asserted the generated seed *contained* `reconcileOpenPrReview`/`shouldReconcileOpenPr`, so it would pass even if reconciliation were dead code; converted to exercise the real `shouldReconcileOpenPr` decision (reconciles a real open/enforced/unacked PR; never from passive branch existence or an already-handled head), keeping one honest regression guard that the old unconditional catch-up string stays absent. Pi-agent-only; no Worker runtime path changes. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 stays Partial; REQ-AGENT-023 stays Implemented.
- **Pi durable review now self-finalizes on an idle session — autonomous reaper timer added** ([REQ-AGENT-061](agents.md#req-agent-061-pi-idle-durable-review-reaper) AC3 added; [REQ-AGENT-054](agents.md#req-agent-054-pi-durable-review-lane-failure-handling) AC1/AC4/AC6 restructured for the per-AC word cap; [REQ-AGENT-059](agents.md#req-agent-059-pi-durable-review-fix-loop) AC1/AC2 trimmed). Live-testing the detached-lane rewrite (entry below) surfaced a gap: the disk reaper only ran on Pi lifecycle ticks (`agent_end` / turn boundaries / `resources_discover`), and Pi exposes no periodic/idle hook — so a push followed by an idle session left both lanes finished on disk (`agent_end` + findings in the transcript) but unharvested for ~17 minutes (no result file, job stuck `running`, no merged summary) until the user happened to interact. Fix: `review-enforcement.ts` registers one reload-safe, `unref`'d `setInterval` (~20s, cleared-then-reset via a `globalThis` singleton so `/reload` never stacks timers) running `autonomousReviewReaperTick` → it reaps finished lanes from disk and spawns the next *fresh* eligible lane (e.g. doc-updater once spec-reviewer has a result) with no ctx; failed-lane RETRIES stay on the on-turn driver so the circuit breaker still bounds them, and the ctx-dependent merged chat summary + ack still post on the next real interaction. Best-effort (never throws) and a cheap no-op when no review window is pending. Same-turn spec-conciseness pass to satisfy the 45-word per-AC cap (the rewrite ACs below ran long): REQ-054 AC1 absorbs the over-budget process-group kill, AC4 absorbs the `/proc` start-time pid-identity check, AC6 narrows to the completion-write decision (`agent_end`, or a usable final message flushed before exit, → result file), and REQ-AGENT-061 captures the lifecycle and idle driver; REQ-AGENT-059 AC1/AC2 are trimmed to the bare assertion (the stripped rationale is already recorded in the entry below, and AC6's dropped "next review uses the fix diff" clause is already covered by [REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement) AC4). The interval driver is runtime-only (a `setInterval`), so it carries a documented coverage-gap alongside the existing OS-spawn smoke-test gap. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-061 stays Implemented (timer + OS-spawn layer smoke-tested with documented coverage-gaps); REQ-AGENT-059 unchanged (Implemented).
- **Pi durable review lanes rebuilt from in-process agent sessions to detached child `pi` processes reaped from disk — lanes now actually run to completion and survive the spawning session** ([REQ-AGENT-060](agents.md#req-agent-060-pi-durable-review-lane-tool-surface) AC1 rewritten, [REQ-AGENT-054](agents.md#req-agent-054-pi-durable-review-lane-failure-handling) AC1/AC4 rewritten + AC6 added). Lanes previously ran as in-process `createAgentSession` calls inside the spawning Pi session (`runDurableLane`): when that session exited — the user quitting, or a single-shot run ending — the in-process async work died mid-stream and its in-process `setTimeout` watchdog died with it, so the lane froze at `running` forever with a partial transcript, no `lane_completed`/`lane_failed`, and the watchdog never fired (confirmed from a real frozen on-disk job: the code-reviewer transcript ended on a `thinking_delta` with no pi process alive). The orphan was never reaped, so `recoverDurableReviewLaneState` reset its `running`→`pending` and reconciliation re-spawned it every session, churning to a `breaker_opened`. Pi's own canonical subagent pattern (`examples/extensions/subagent`: "each subagent runs in a separate pi process") is the fix: `spawnDurableLane` now launches each lane as a DETACHED, headless child `pi --mode json -p --no-session --no-extensions --no-context-files --tools read,grep,find,bash --append-system-prompt <agent-prompt>` (stdin `/dev/null`), `unref`'d so it outlives the spawning session and writes its event stream to the lane transcript. A new disk-driven reaper (`reapDurableReviewLanes` + the pure `reapLaneDecision`/`summarizeLaneTranscript`) — run by the `agent_end` driver and `refreshReviewStatusFromDurable` on every tick — is the single `running`→`completed`/`failed` authority: `agent_end` + usable final message → write the result file, mark completed, kill the child group; child dead without `agent_end` or over the 15-min budget → mark failed (over-budget killed). Liveness is the child pid persisted on disk and **identity-checked against the child's `/proc/<pid>/stat` start-time** (Linux recycles pids), so a recycled pid reads as dead rather than a live impostor — preventing both a wedged `running` lane and a SIGKILL to an unrelated process group; a group is killed ONLY when verified-alive-and-ours, and only on the over-budget branch (a completed/dead child is already gone). A usable final assistant message is preserved even if the child dies before flushing the terminal `agent_end` line (no lost reviews). Any session reaps a lane another (now-exited) session spawned — the in-memory `runningLanes` Set is deleted, and `recoverDurableReviewLaneState` no longer resets `running`→`pending` (the churn source). (PID-identity, lost-result, and needless-kill hardening came from the in-session code review of this change.) **Trade-off (supersedes the same-day "durable review lanes load graphify-native.ts directly" note below): lanes run with `--no-extensions`, so a reviewer no longer has graphify/context-mode/`codeflare-pi` inside the lane** — it reviews with `read`/`grep`/`find`/`bash` and the prompt's explicit "do not run builds/tests/linters" instruction. `--no-extensions` is required for correctness (no recursive `review-enforcement` load) and is what lets the lane child start fast and exit cleanly (verified: a bare in-extension `pi -p` lingered until killed; `--no-extensions` exits 0). Two env requirements proven against pi 0.78.1 and encoded: stdin MUST be `/dev/null` (an inherited stdin hangs print mode at startup with zero output), and completion is detected from `agent_end` in the transcript, never from process exit. New behavioural tests in `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` (`reapLaneDecision` transition table, `summarizeLaneTranscript` parsing, `recoverDurableReviewLaneState` reflective recovery); the spawn + pid-liveness + group-kill OS layer is an integration smoke test (documented coverage-gaps on REQ-060 AC1 / REQ-054 AC6), since the Workers vitest pool cannot spawn pi. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-060 and REQ-AGENT-054 stay Implemented (decision/parse/recovery logic unit-tested; OS-spawn runtime behavior smoke-tested with documented coverage-gaps, matching the existing runtime-coverage convention).
- **Pi graphify rebuilt as a first-party native extension; the `@gaodes/pi-graphify` third-party wrapper and the dead Pi `mcp.json` are removed** ([REQ-AGENT-023](agents.md#req-agent-023-knowledge-graph-capability-graphify), [REQ-AGENT-024](agents.md#req-agent-024-advanced-session-mode-graph-first-discipline)). Pi has no MCP client, so graphify is now registered by a self-contained `preseed/agents/pi/extensions/graphify-native.ts` (`graphify_query`/`graphify_path`/`graphify_explain` via `pi.registerTool`, mirroring `browser-run.ts`) that shells the SAME upstream `graphify` CLI Claude's MCP server runs (`graphify.serve._query_graph_text`) — one engine, identical ranking, no third-party reimplementation. It resolves the active repo's `graphify-out/graph.json` (active-repo sentinel) else the merged global graph, caps output, and returns the resolved graph + repo cwd in `details` so the graphify skill can `graphify save-result` against the same graph (the feedback loop). The npm wrapper is dropped from `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`entrypoint.sh`/`manifest.json`; `preseed/agents/pi/mcp.json` is deleted and its now-dead seed path-mapping (`generate-agent-seed.mjs`) and seed strip-branch (`r2-seed.ts::normalizePiSeedDocument`) removed; durable review lanes load `graphify-native.ts` directly (alongside `codeflare-pi.ts`) instead of the @gaodes package (`review-jobs.ts` + `laneExtensionSources`). Tests updated in `agent-seed-manifest.test.ts` + `r2-seed-mode-req-coverage.test.ts`. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-023 stays Implemented (AC2 native-surface test rewritten to assert the first-party extension and the absence of mcp.json/@gaodes).
- **Pi PR-boundary review gains a durable missed-event recovery path** (new [REQ-AGENT-058](agents.md#req-agent-058-pr-boundary-review-reconciliation-and-missed-event-recovery); [REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions) AC6, [REQ-AGENT-040](agents.md#req-agent-040-pr-boundary-lane-classification-and-agent-dispatch) AC8). Review initiation previously depended solely on capturing a single `onToolEnd` event; a compound `&&` command, a here-doc body, or a reload between the command and its event silently dropped the boundary and the review never fired (gpt-5.5 post-mortem). Added `reconcileOpenPrReview` (run on `session_start`/`turn_start`/`turn_end`/`resources_discover`/`agent_end`, network-throttled): when an SDD repo has an OPEN, non-draft, ENFORCED main/master PR whose resolved head is unacknowledged with no review window and no open breaker, it starts the review even with no captured command — gated by the pure `shouldReconcileOpenPr` so it NEVER fires on mere branch/PR existence (REQ-036 AC6 preserved). The onToolEnd window-creation is extracted into a shared `ensureReviewWindow` so a reconciled window is byte-identical to a command-triggered one; `resolveEnforcedHead` tolerates the develop→main metadata-visibility lag; a `boundary_candidate_ignored` audit event names every skipped-review gate reason (never-silent); and a `gh pr create` whose command text was unparseable but whose output prints the PR URL (`prUrlFromText`) is recovered through the same reconciliation. Generated-only diffs (the checked-in `graphify-out/` graph) classify to zero lanes and auto-ack in BOTH classifiers (`review-helpers.classifyReviewFiles` + the Claude `lane-classifier.sh`), so a graph refresh never spawns reviewers. New behavioural tests: `review-state.test.ts` (`shouldReconcileOpenPr` gating), `review-trigger.test.ts` (generated-artifact classification + `prUrlFromText`), `host/__tests__/lane-classifier.test.js` (graphify-out parity). **Status:** REQ-AGENT-058 added as Partial (`resolveEnforcedHead` lag-tolerance and the diagnostic audit events have no direct automated test; the decision core and PR-URL detection do); REQ-AGENT-036 stays Implemented (AC6 permits the bounded reconciliation); REQ-AGENT-040 stays Implemented (AC8 added).
- **Pi review-enforcement subsystem hardened against the stale-ctx flood and reviews that silently never fired** ([REQ-AGENT-055](agents.md#req-agent-055-pi-pr-boundary-review-window-advancement), [REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions); new [REQ-AGENT-057](agents.md#req-agent-057-pi-review-status-command)). The off-turn `pi.events` lane-completion bus (review-jobs `emit` + review-enforcement listeners) is **deleted**: it leaked one stale closure per `/reload` and ran completion through a fabricated/stale ctx whose `.modelRegistry` getter throws `assertActive()` once the turn ends — the console-error flood seen in the incident. Lane completion is now **pulled on-turn** by the existing `agent_end` + turn-boundary reconcilers (each holding a live ctx), so the redundant push path is removed with no behaviour loss. Also: an authoritative `Promise.race` lane watchdog that reclaims a wedged lane even if `prompt()` never settles; `modelRegistry` resolved to a value at spawn instead of a lazy ctx getter; a single `isPrBoundaryTrigger` predicate that fires on push / `gh repo sync` / `gh pr update-branch` / `gh pr create` into main-or-master and excludes `gh pr merge` (the merge gate); a `.git/codeflare-review-events.jsonl` append-only decision audit; and the new read-only `/review-status` command (REQ-AGENT-057) that renders the canonical `computeReviewState` plus a tail of that audit. New behavioural tests: `review-state.test.ts` (lane-status precedence + overall aggregation), `review-trigger.test.ts` (`gh pr merge` is not a trigger). Pi-agent-only; no Worker runtime path changes. **Status:** REQ-AGENT-055 stays Implemented; REQ-AGENT-057 added as Partial (the command's rendering layer has no automated test; its underlying state computation does).
- **Claude PR-boundary review-reminder hook fired inconsistently on multi-line pushes** ([REQ-AGENT-036](agents.md#req-agent-036-pr-boundary-review-trigger-conditions)). `git-push-review-reminder.sh` only recognised `git push` at start-of-command or after a `;` / `&` / `|` separator; a bare newline was not in the separator class, so a `git push` on its own line inside a multi-line Bash command emitted no in-turn review directive (the turn-end Stop hook still caught it, so reviews were eventually enforced — but the in-turn nudge was lost). The command is now newline-normalised (`tr '\n\r' ';;'`) before the trigger regex. Regression test in `host/__tests__/git-push-review-reminder.test.js`. No AC change.
- **Pi vault-extract self-trigger loop fixed** ([REQ-VAULT-003](vault.md#req-vault-003-user-curated-edits-are-detected-and-ingested-within-60s)). `memory-vault` re-classified its own re-rendered generated artifacts (`Raw/Graphs/vault-graph.html`, the graphify-out tree) as user edits and re-spawned the vault-extract subagent every turn. The exclusion predicate moved to the pure `memory-vault-helpers.isVaultExcludedPath` (segment-aware, so `Rawthoughts/` is not mistaken for `Raw/`) with `Raw/Graphs/` and `Library/Codeflare/` added to the generated-prefix set, plus an append-only spawn audit. New behavioural test `vault-exclusion.test.ts` (generated-artifact paths excluded, genuine user edits not). No AC change.
- **CI agent-seed drift guard** (`.github/workflows/test.yml`; [REQ-AGENT-006](agents.md#req-agent-006-preseed-configs-generated-from-single-source-of-truth)). A step regenerates `src/lib/agent-seed.generated.ts` and fails the build if the committed copy differs, enforcing the single-source-of-truth contract at CI time so a future preseed edit can no longer ship a stale embedded extension/hook payload to deployed agents.

## 2026-06-07

- **Copilot BYOK contract extended 3→5 vars (token-limit hints)** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC3). `entrypoint.sh` now also prepends `COPILOT_PROVIDER_MAX_PROMPT_TOKENS=920000` and `COPILOT_PROVIDER_MAX_OUTPUT_TOKENS=128000` to `.bashrc` alongside the BYOK triple. Copilot does not recognize the slash-free `codeflare` handle (a dynamic-route alias) in its built-in model catalog, so it warned and fell back to default token limits; these hints suppress the warning and right-size context to gpt-5.5's real 1,050,000 / 128,000 window (prompt = ctx − output headroom; gpt-5.5 is the dynamic route's primary, which Copilot always hits since it cannot send `reasoning_effort` to trigger the gemini fallback). Enterprise-gated; SaaS path byte-identical. `configuration.md` env-var table updated. Status of REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 stays Planned (AC3 still has no automated test — `entrypoint.sh` behaviour).
- **Enterprise group stamping + any-of access gate** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway) AC4; [REQ-ENTERPRISE-010](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-010-access-gated-jit-user-provisioning) AC2). The interceptor now stamps `cf-aig-metadata.group` with the user's single matched Access group (omitted when absent) so the customer's gateway can branch per-group routing/cost/rate-limit policies; the group is resolved once per session at the container `/start` route (`resolveSessionAccessGroup` → get-identity) and threaded setBucketName → DO `_userGroup` → `LlmInterceptor` prop. `ENTERPRISE_ACCESS_GROUP` now accepts a comma/newline-separated list; a user in ANY configured group is admitted (any-of gate via `resolveUserAccessGroup`, which replaces the single-group `isUserInAccessGroup`), preserving back-compat with single-value configs. Tests: `access-group-resolution.test.ts` (list parsing, any-of intersection, first-of-several, fail-closed-before-fetch SSRF guard), `enterprise-jit-provisioning.test.ts` (any-of admit/deny), `llm-interceptor.test.ts` (group stamped / omitted), `index.test.ts` (group prop). SaaS path byte-identical (interceptor never instantiated + gate only inside `isEnterpriseMode`). Status of REQ-ENTERPRISE-004 and REQ-ENTERPRISE-010 unchanged (Implemented).
- **Pi thinking selector restored (`reasoning: true`) with a per-session default of off** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC4; supersedes the same-day `reasoning: false` entry below). The enterprise Pi model is registered with `reasoning: true` so the thinking selector is available again (Shift+Tab / `/settings`), while `settings.json` pins `defaultThinkingLevel: "off"` so every session STARTS with thinking off — Pi sends no `reasoning_effort` by default (gpt-5.5 stays 200 tools-only on `/v1/chat/completions`), and the user can raise the level for a route model that supports reasoning over chat/completions (e.g. Gemini). The earlier `reasoning: false` lock removed the selector entirely; this keeps the gpt-5.5-safe default while restoring user control. Enterprise-gated (`entrypoint.sh`); SaaS path byte-identical. Status of REQ-ENTERPRISE-005 stays Planned (AC4 still has no automated test — `entrypoint.sh` behaviour).
- **Interceptor strips OpenAI-only fields on the compat leg + stamps the user email for gateway attribution** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway) AC1/AC4; [AD74](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad74-enterprise-llm-transport-on-the-ai-gateway-rest-api)). Two follow-ups from the live Gemini evaluation. (1) Non-OpenAI providers reached via the compat fallback reject OpenAI-only request fields — Google returns a `400` rejecting the unknown field `store` — so `LlmInterceptor` now strips `store` and `prompt_cache_key` **only on the compat replay**; the REST/OpenAI leg keeps them, so OpenAI prompt caching is unaffected. (2) `cf-aig-metadata` now carries the user's **email** (from the per-session DO prop sourced from `_userEmail` in `setupEnterpriseInterception`, falling back to the bucket id) instead of the opaque bucket id, so the customer's gateway per-user analytics attribute usage to the real identity — an explicit enterprise requirement that intentionally overrides the original opaque-id privacy design. Tests: `llm-interceptor.test.ts` (compat strip; kept-on-REST vs stripped-on-compat) and `index.test.ts` (email prop). SaaS path byte-identical (interceptor never instantiated when `ENTERPRISE_MODE` unset). Status of REQ-ENTERPRISE-004 unchanged (Implemented).
- **Enterprise LLM interceptor is now dual-transport: AI Gateway REST API first, deprecated compat path as fallback** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway); [AD74](../../documentation/decisions/README.md#ad74-enterprise-llm-transport-on-the-ai-gateway-rest-api) dual-transport amendment). A live Gemini evaluation found the REST API (`api.cloudflare.com/.../ai/v1/*`) does **not** carry the `google-ai-studio` provider — every Gemini id returns `404`, and a dynamic route resolving to a Google node returns the masked `404 Model execution failed`; the identical route works on the deprecated `gateway.ai.cloudflare.com/v1/{acct}/{gw}/compat/chat/completions` path (verified against a sibling Worker using BYOK + `cf-aig-authorization`). `LlmInterceptor` now sends to the REST API first and, only on a `404` for a model-routable request, replays the buffered request to the compat path — safe because a 404 is a complete error body, not a started stream (no double-billing, no truncation). As Cloudflare migrates providers onto the REST API the fallback stops firing with no code change. Consequence: `AIG_TOKEN` must now carry **both** Workers AI (REST API, `Authorization: Bearer`) and AI Gateway Run (compat, `cf-aig-authorization: Bearer`) permissions. SaaS path byte-identical (interceptor never instantiated when `ENTERPRISE_MODE` unset).
- **Pi stays on `openai-completions` with `reasoning: false`** ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC4, from the live enterprise deploy and subsequent iteration; supersedes the same-day plan to switch Pi to the Responses API, which was reverted): the CF AI Gateway's `/ai/v1/responses` endpoint rejects valid Responses `input` bodies with "Required value missing: messages" (it validates as chat/completions), so Pi's `codeflare-gateway` provider cannot use the `openai-responses` adapter and remains on `openai-completions`. gpt-5.5 in turn rejects `reasoning_effort` + function tools together on `/v1/chat/completions` (`Please use /v1/responses instead`) — exactly Pi's per-turn shape — so the model is registered with `reasoning: false`: Pi never sends `reasoning_effort` and operates tools-only, verified 200 through the dynamic route. Root cause of the original compaction loop: that combination returned a bodyless 400 that Pi mis-read as context overflow (on the `dynamic/<route>` path the gateway further masks it as a generic `Model execution failed`). Consequence: gpt-5.5 reasoning is blocked in enterprise until CF fixes `/ai/v1/responses`; a chat/completions-capable reasoning model (o3, gpt-5.1) would allow `reasoning: true` on this same adapter. Copilot stays on Chat Completions. SaaS path is byte-identical (enterprise-gated). Status stays Planned (AC4 still has no automated test).
- **Five enterprise REQs promoted Planned → Implemented** after a verification audit (CQ-SOURCE + CQ-TEST checked by hand): [REQ-ENTERPRISE-001](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-001-enterprise_mode-forces-unlimited-tier-and-pro-mode), [REQ-ENTERPRISE-003](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-003-agent-allowlist-in-enterprise-mode), [REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway), [REQ-ENTERPRISE-007](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-007-gateway-route-pinning), and [REQ-ENTERPRISE-011](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-011-container-start-interception-ordering). Each has resolving `@impl` anchors and `@test` files whose describes carry the REQ-ID covering every AC (e.g. six `REQ-ENTERPRISE-004:` describes in `llm-interceptor.test.ts` → AC1..AC7; the `REQ-ENTERPRISE-011` describe in `index.test.ts` → AC1..AC2). No code or test changed — these were already verified but left Planned; this only corrects Status drift. [REQ-ENTERPRISE-002](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-002-subscription-ui-hidden-and-subscribe-route-guarded), [REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls), and [REQ-ENTERPRISE-006](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-006-deploy-time-aig-secrets-and-enterprise_mode-var) were audited and **correctly remain Planned**: REQ-002's `@test` annotation points at a describe that does not carry the REQ-ID (real coverage is in `user-profile-enterprise.test.ts` + `Header.test.tsx` — annotation drift to fix first); REQ-005 AC2/AC3/AC4 (containers-CA install, Copilot BYOK, Pi config — all `entrypoint.sh` behaviours) have no automated test; REQ-006 has no REQ-ID-annotated test anywhere.
- **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC3 fix** (from the same live enterprise deploy): a returning enterprise user's `subscribedMode` was not persisted on JIT provisioning, so after the first login it read back `undefined` and degraded to `default` session mode. `resolveOrProvisionEnterpriseUser` now persists `subscribedMode: 'advanced'` on the JIT write and forces `advanced` on the existing-record branch (every enterprise user is implicitly Pro/advanced; the function only runs in enterprise mode). Flag-unset parity preserved. Status stays Implemented (`enterprise-jit-provisioning.test.ts` returning-user + legacy-record regression tests).
- **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC2 mechanism corrected** (from the same live enterprise deploy): the CA-trust env vars (`NODE_EXTRA_CA_CERTS`, `SSL_CERT_FILE`, `REQUESTS_CA_BUNDLE`) were previously exported only into the `entrypoint.sh` process, which Pi and Copilot — launched in PTYs by the terminal server after init — never inherited. `entrypoint.sh` now prepends these exports to `.bashrc` (idempotent, enterprise-gated) so they are sourced before the terminal-autostart block launches an agent. Without this, every agent's intercepted-TLS handshake failed as an opaque "Connection error" before reaching the interceptor. SaaS path is byte-identical. Status stays Planned (AC2/AC3/AC4 still have no automated test).
- **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-005](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-005-container-side-enterprise-routing-ca-trust--constant-base-urls) AC3 mechanism corrected** (same live enterprise deploy): Copilot's entire BYOK config is env-only — it has no config file (unlike Pi) — and the Worker deliberately keeps `COPILOT_*` out of the container env (`container-env-llm.test.ts`), so the three exports (`COPILOT_PROVIDER_BASE_URL`, `COPILOT_PROVIDER_API_KEY`, `COPILOT_MODEL`) lived only in the `entrypoint.sh` process and the copilot PTY never inherited them. Copilot therefore ignored the gateway base URL, showed no `codeflare` model, and fell back to a GitHub login. `entrypoint.sh` now prepends these to `.bashrc` (idempotent, enterprise-gated) — the same mechanism as the AC2 CA-trust fix. SaaS path is byte-identical. Status stays Planned (AC3 still has no automated test).
- **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway) AC3 streaming-terminator repair** (same live enterprise deploy): the AI Gateway **dynamic-route** wrapper strips the terminal `finish_reason:"stop"` chunk (and usage) when re-emitting a streamed response — verified against the live gateway (the same model is conformant non-streaming and when called directly as `openai/<model>`; only the `dynamic/<route>` streaming path drops it). Strict OpenAI-wire clients (Pi, Copilot) then error "Stream ended without finish_reason", retry, and (mis)interpret the bodyless failure as a context overflow → compaction loop. `LlmInterceptor` now normalizes streamed `chat/completions` responses: when `[DONE]` arrives (or the stream ends) without a non-null `finish_reason`, it injects one synthetic terminator chunk (`tool_calls` when the stream carried tool-call deltas, else `stop`). Idempotent and scoped to streamed chat-completions; non-streaming, `/responses`, error, and non-enterprise paths pass through byte-for-byte. Tests in `llm-interceptor.test.ts`. The temporary `[ENTERPRISE-DIAG]` instrumentation added during this debugging session is removed in the same change. Status of REQ-ENTERPRISE-004 unchanged (Implemented).

## 2026-06-06

- Enterprise Mode extended with three new requirements ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression)..[REQ-ENTERPRISE-010](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-010-access-gated-jit-user-provisioning), all Implemented) covering the single-tenant administration model and Cloudflare-Access-driven just-in-time user provisioning, per the 2026-06-06 requirements review. (A user offboarding / session-lifecycle requirement — scheduled Access-revocation cleanup and Access-routed logout — was considered and deferred for now.) **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) Enterprise Frontend Surface Suppression**: in Enterprise Mode the frontend hides the Administration "Manage Subscriptions" and "Manage Users" entries, the "Usage" and "Subscription" entries in both the Header and Dashboard username menus, the Standard/Pro session-mode selector, and the monthly-quota warning banners + upgrade CTAs, and routes a first-time user to the app home rather than `/app/subscribe` or the self-serve onboarding/waitlist — concretizing the surface list implied by [REQ-ENTERPRISE-002](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-002-subscription-ui-hidden-and-subscribe-route-guarded) AC1 (which keeps the `/app/subscribe` route guard) and adding the admin-button, mode-selector, and first-login-routing surfaces. **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-009](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-009-enterprise-backend-route-hardening) Enterprise Backend Route Hardening**: the matching routes fail closed so the disabled capabilities cannot be reached by direct call — user-management routes, billing checkout/portal/switch, `/auth/subscribe` + `/auth/request-access`, and the admin tier/subscription config routes return 403; the Stripe webhook is a no-op that cannot mutate a user's tier; `PATCH /api/preferences` accepts `sessionMode` without the SaaS advanced-mode entitlement gate check (effective mode stays Pro per [REQ-ENTERPRISE-001](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-001-enterprise_mode-forces-unlimited-tier-and-pro-mode) AC2). **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-010](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-010-access-gated-jit-user-provisioning) Access-Gated JIT User Provisioning**: an authenticated Cloudflare Access user with no Codeflare record is auto-provisioned as an `unlimited` enterprise user keyed by the IdP-verified `email`, replacing the SaaS pending→approve funnel (which currently bounces a fresh enterprise user to the hidden `/app/subscribe` page — a real first-run breakage this fixes); when the optional `ENTERPRISE_ACCESS_GROUP` is set, provisioning is gated on the user's membership in that group resolved via the Access `get-identity` endpoint (`${iss}/cdn-cgi/access/get-identity` with the request's `CF_Authorization` token — the application JWT carries no group claim by default), otherwise a valid JWT alone provisions and the group gate is delegated to the customer's Access application policy; the check runs once at provisioning (the record is the cache), JIT sends no email, the R2 bucket/token stay lazy, and non-enterprise deployments still 403 unknown users (no behavior change). **`ENTERPRISE_ACCESS_GROUP` is configured during the setup wizard and stored in KV (`SETUP_KEYS.ENTERPRISE_ACCESS_GROUP`), not as a deploy-time/GitHub secret** — consistent with how the other Access parameters (`ACCESS_AUD`, the admin/user group ids) are already setup→KV values, so an admin changes the gating group by re-running setup with no redeploy; it names a customer-managed Access group that Codeflare references via `get-identity` but never creates or populates (unlike the admin/user groups codeflare manages in non-enterprise modes). `ENTERPRISE_MODE` and the `AIG_GATEWAY_URL`/`AIG_TOKEN` secrets remain deploy-time bindings. Every new REQ carries an explicit flag-unset parity AC: with `ENTERPRISE_MODE` unset, all surfaces, routes, and provisioning are byte-identical to today. Source: the 2026-06-06 enterprise gap analysis (the `get-identity` contract verified against Cloudflare's Application-token + Validate-JWTs docs).
- **[REQ-ENTERPRISE-008](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-008-enterprise-frontend-surface-suppression) AC7 added** (from a live enterprise deploy): the setup wizard's "Regular Users" section is suppressed in Enterprise Mode — setup configures only Admin Users and the optional Cloudflare Access group, since regular users are provisioned via Cloudflare Access JIT ([REQ-ENTERPRISE-010](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-010-access-gated-jit-user-provisioning)) on first sign-in rather than entered by hand. The section already hid in SaaS mode; it now also hides when `enterpriseMode` is set, and renders unchanged when the flag is unset. Status stays Implemented (`ConfigureStep.test.tsx`).
- **[REQ-STOR-009](storage.md#req-stor-009-getting-started-docs-auto-seeded-on-first-session) AC5 added** (from a live enterprise deploy where a freshly created bucket was left without getting-started docs until a manual re-seed): the first-session seed now retries on a transient failure — a new bucket not yet writable on the S3 data plane, or R2 credentials still propagating after setup — with bounded backoff, so a new bucket reliably ends up seeded instead of being permanently skipped by the create-only gate; once retries are exhausted the failure still surfaces to the caller. Success-path behavior is byte-identical for every mode (the retry only triggers on failure). Status stays Implemented (`r2-seed.test.ts`).
- **New [REQ-ENTERPRISE-011](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-011-container-start-interception-ordering) (Container Start Interception Ordering)** (from a live enterprise deploy where Pi and Copilot failed every message with "Connection error" and the AI Gateway received nothing): LLM interception is now wired **before the container starts** instead of in `onStart`. Captured as a new REQ rather than an 8th AC on [REQ-ENTERPRISE-004](enterprise-mode.md#req-enterprise-004-outbound-interception-llm-routing-to-customer-ai-gateway), honouring the 7-AC cap (the 2026-06-05 split policy that rejected the per-REQ override escape hatch).
